After I have completed this book for you, O Sons, which is the last one in the science of medicine along with its complement, and after I have reached the end in it through its expositions and declarations, it seemed to me that I should complete it for you with this Treatise which is a part of operation, that is, surgery with the hand.
Since operation with the hand is prostrate in our region and at our time completely, until perhaps it has perished, and its trace has vanished; and only small descriptions of it remain in the books of the ancients, which have been corrupted by hands; and error and hesitation occurred to them until their intentions were closed, and the force was elongated; It seemed to me that I should bring it to life with the arrangement of this Treatise according to its position, declaration, and abbreviation; and to come with the shapes of the tools of the Cautery, and the remaining instruments of work; which is made by addition from the declarations, and by the properation of what is necessary.
The reason why a good craftsman of this art with his hand is not found in our time is because the art of medicine is long, and its author must be trained before that in the science of anatomy, which Galen narrated, until he knows the help for the members, and their forms, and their connection, and separation, and has knowledge of bones, nerves, muscles, and their number, and their exit, and the pulses of veins and arteries, and their quiets, and their locations.
And for this reason Hippocrates said that much is the name with the name, and little is the work, especially in the art of the hand.
We have already spoken about it at the beginning of this book.
Since one who does not know what we have said about anatomy will fall into error and kill men, as I have seen many of those who are formed in this science and boast of it without knowledge and without experience.
Because I saw a foolish doctor cut off a scrofulous apostema on a woman's neck and cut some arteries in the neck; therefore, the woman bled to death until she fell dead in his hands.
And I saw another doctor who presumed to remove a stone from an old man who had passed his prime, and the stone was large. Therefore he came to him and removed it with a piece of bladder. Wherefore the man died on the third day.
And indeed I had already been summoned to remove it; and I saw from the size of the stone and the condition of the patient that he would die.
And I saw another doctor who was receiving a stipend from one of our land's dukes because of medicine; and a black eunuch was with him, who sustained a fracture near his heel; and the doctor, with his ignorance, bound up the fracture over an ulcer with pulley irons and tightened it strongly, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
Then he cured him according to his devices. Afterwards he dismissed him for some days and ordered him not to loosen the bandage; and he stood thus until the apostema grew on his leg, and his foot, and came to destruction.
Therefore I was summoned to him; and I hastened to loosen the bandage; and peace came upon him, and he was released from his pains.
The corruption had already been confirmed in the member; and I could not prevent it.
Then, the corruption ceased to walk around in the member, until it perished.
And I saw another physician who pierced a cancerous boil; and it ulcerated for days, until the wickedness of it with its lord was manifested.
This is because when it is a pure cancer from black bile, then it is not fitting to reach it with iron at all, unless it is in a member that can bear it, so that the whole of it may be cut off.
And for that reason, according to O Filii, it is necessary for you to know that an operation is divided into two divisions: namely, the operation which is associated with safety; and the operation with which there is danger in many arrangements.
And I have already awakened in every place of this book where the operation comes that has fear and terror.
Therefore, it is necessary for you to be careful of that and divide it yourself so that fools do not find a way to talk and disgrace.
Therefore, take the measure with care and protection, and take care of your weak ones with ease and firmness, and use a better way leading by God's grace to health and praiseworthy success; and let go of fearsome illnesses difficult to cure; and remove yourselves from that which makes you afraid, so that hesitation in faith and your comfort may not enter upon you.
For it remains more for your glory, and higher in this world, and finally to your quantities.
Galenus has already said in some of his admonitions. Do not treat evil sickness; do not be called a bad physician.
Now, however, I have divided this Treatise into three Chapters. ¶
Chapter One.
On cautery with fire and cautery with sharp medicine, this chapter is arranged, from the head to the feet, and on the shapes of instruments and tools for cauterization, as well as everything that is necessary during the procedure. [Paragraph break]
De incisionibus generaliter: et de incisione capitae, et
Chapter Two. [Paragraph break] On general incisions and the incision of the head, [paragraph break] On section and perforation, phlebotomy and ventosities, and wounds; as well as extraction of arrows and similar objects: and all arranged in the shapes of instruments. [Paragraph break]
De cauterio cum igne et Cauterio cum medicina acuta,
Chapter Three. [Paragraph break] On cautery with fire and cautery with sharp medicine, [paragraph break] On restoration, dislocation, treatment of twisting, and similar cases: arranged from the head to the feet, and on the shapes of instruments.
Before I remember the procedure with it, however, it is necessary to say the quality of its benefits and harms, and in what constitution it should be used. [Paragraph break] Chapter One. [Paragraph break] On the benefit.
I therefore say that the discourse on the quality of the benefit and harm of cautery is a long, subtle, scientific, and hidden knowledge. [Paragraph break] Chapter One. [Paragraph break] On the benefit.
And there was much wisdom spoken about it and they disagreed on it; and for me, enough from their words is sufficient, fearing prolongation. [Paragraph break] Chapter One. [Paragraph break] On the benefit.
I therefore say that cautery applies universally to all constitutions, whether with matter or without; except for two constitutions, which are a hot constitution without matter, and a dry constitution without matter. [Paragraph break] Chapter One. [Paragraph break] On the benefit.
In a hot and dry composition, they separated from the matter. Some say that Cautery is beneficial in it. And others say the opposite, that Cautery is not appropriate in a disease which is due to heat and dryness, because the nature of fire is heat; it is inappropriate to cure a hot and dry disease with heat and dryness.
And he who says the opposite said that Cautery is beneficial for every hot and dry disease which occurs in human bodies, because when you compare a human body and its humors, according to the constitution of fire, you find a cold body in humans.
And I myself say through his speech, because I have already seen that many times confirmed to me.
Nevertheless, it is not necessary for him to come upon it unless he who has already been tested and trained in the last chapter on Cautery, and knows the diversity of human constitutions, the disposition of diseases in themselves, their causes, their qualities, their accidents, and the duration of the diseases.
Concerning the other constitutions, there is no fear for you: and especially for cold and moist diseases. Indeed, all physicians agree on these: and they have not separated from the benefit when using Cautery for them.
And know, my children, that from the secret of curing by Cautery with fire, and the goodness of it over Cautery with medicine burning, is that fire is simple, whose action does not reach except to the member being cauterized; and it does not harm another part joined with it unless it causes a slight damage.
But the action of medicine burning reaches to that which is extended from the limbs; and perhaps it causes a difficult-to-heal disease in the member, and perhaps it kills it.
Fire, on account of its subtlety and goodness of substance, does not do that except when it is excessive.
We have now come to know that (something), through experience, because of the length of service and study with art, and due to its conformity to truth: and because of this I excuse myself from the length of speech.
And if it were not forbidden to this book of mine, I would bring you the secret hidden in fire and the quality of its operation in expelling bodies, which expels diseases with a philosophical explanation demonstrated, which could be understood by your minds.
And know, sons, that they themselves differ in the time when cautery is to be done, and they put a better time for it according to truth.
And I say that cautery is suitable at any time: therefore, because the damage caused by time is submerged in the benefit which is attracted by the cautery. And especially if cautery is for pain due to necessary pains, strong, sharp ones that do not tolerate delay: therefore because it is feared that from them there might occur a greater mischief than the small damage caused by time.
And let not that enter your minds, sons, that it is not thought except by the common people and foolish doctors, namely that to the ailment which is cured by cautery there is no return: and they put this as a consequence, and things are not so as they think: therefore because cautery is not unless in place of medicine, which alters the complexion, and extracts humidities which are the cause, that why pains occur.
However, cautery is superfluous over medicine because of the rapidity of its health and virtue of operation and the force of its dominion: and it is possible that the ailment returns an hour of time according to the complexion of the sick person, the location of the ailment, and the power of the ailment: and what is prepared in his body from accumulation of superfluities in it: and what comes upon him in acquisition of his body from foods and similar things from causes, unless an ailment occurs, for which cautery is administered.
Subtle ailment in a member of few superfluities and moistures, like the cautery of a tooth, due to pain, and similar to it, is possibly such that the pain does not return in it. But this happens in few cases.
However, the common saying that cautery is the last remedy of medicine is correct only to what they intend by it, because they believe that there is no healing brought about with medication nor with anything else after the fall of the cautery.
But this is contrary to their intention, and the saying that cautery is the last remedy of medicine is not true, unless when we administer ways of healing for some ailments, these medications do not help; then we administer cautery at the end, and it helps; thus it comes about that cautery is the last of medicines, not in accordance with the understanding of the common people and most foolish doctors.
The ancients said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron; and they did not say this unless for the equality of gold, and the subtlety of its substance; and they said that it does not make a wound in the place of cauterizing. This is not absolutely true; for I have proven this and found that it does not do this in certain bodies without others.
And cautery with itself is good, and better than with iron, as they said. But when you heat the cautery with fire from gold, it is not shown to you when heated according to the amount that you wish, due to the redness of gold; and when it goes towards it, coldness comes about, and if you add more heating on top of this, it liquefies in the fire and turns into sheets.
Therefore, the craftsman falls into this mistake; and for this reason we use cautery with iron more quickly and closely among us in accordance with correctness for the operation.
And I myself have already arranged this Chapter on cautery, according to the Chapters: and I have arranged it from head to feet: so that one may alleviate what the inquirer wants from it.
Chapter II.
The cauterization here is applied to the dominion of moisture and coldness on the brain: which are two causes of scurvy, and of the flux of humors from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears, and of sleepiness, and toothache, and throat pain: and universally of all illness that comes from coldness, such as paralysis, scurvy, epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar ones caused by these illnesses.
The method of cauterization is that you order the sick person to: evacuate his head first with a solution of medicine cleansing it for three or four nights, according to the strength of the patient and his age and habit.
Then order him to make his head with a linen cloth. Then make him sit between your hands square, so that he has already placed his hands on his chest.
Then place the root of your palm over the root of his nose between his eyes. Whenever therefore your middle finger comes to a place, mark that place with unburnt (material).
Then oil the Cautery Iron; of which this is its form.
Then place it on the marked unburnt place with a downward pressure, by which your hand is gradually tightened and you turn it. Then quickly lift your hand and look at the place.
If you see that a piece of bone or quantity of flesh has been burnt off the skull or forehead, then lift your hand. And if not, repeat your hand with the iron itself, or with another one if it becomes cold: until the bones that I told you appear.
Then take something from salt, and dissolve it in water, and immerse the dressing in it, and place it over the location: and leave it for three days.
Then place the dressing soaked in butter over it, and leave it until the burn is destroyed by fire. Then treat it with a four-ingredient ointment until it heals.
They have said that the more an ulcer remains open, the more pus it discharges; wherefore it is better and more beneficial.
And some of them said that the skin should be cauterized up to the bone; and the cautery should be held until something is burned through the thickness of the bone.
Then file off what has been burned from the bone, then treat it.
And others say that when the cautery reaches the bone, it should leave an impression on it for as long as the bone falls out like the shape of a scab: or an instrument that women use to apply to the small alphabet letter: and they believe that steam from the head will escape from this place, and the wound should be left open for a long time.
Then treat it until it becomes firm.
But these two types of cautery do not seem to me at all useful except in some people, according to the way of fear.
And leave it alone, in my opinion, it is better for his health.
The head is weakened by the solution of its own natural continuity; as we have testified in other members; and especially when the head is naturally weak and frail; and the first type of cautery is safer and better in my opinion, and I use it: so operate with it for the benefit.
Caput III. Inhibetur ut perforatio
Chapter III. It is forbidden to perform perforation when there is chronic pain in the whole head and it persists in sickness, and uses herbs, oils, and plasters. And especially if it has already been cauterized with one cautery as we have said, and none of those [remedies] help him, then consider. If the head of the sick person is strong by nature and not weak, and it finds very cold: then cauterize with another cautery under it scarcely. Then cauterize it on all its horns of the head with a cautery, so that the skin is not penetrated, and a quantity of bone is excavated as we have said. And cauterize it with one cautery on the back of the head at the place called vase; it is a place where a vent is placed; pour your oil into this and do not excavate the bone. The sick person finds it because of that very violent pain, and it is different from the pain of all other cauteries on the head.
I will say that this cautery is in its place; it must be a cautery used for the horns of the head and the back of the head more finely with a cautery used for the middle of the head.
Chapter IV.
When there is pain and swelling in the head, or the pain extends to the eye, and the head is evacuated with cleansing medicines, and further treatment is administered as I have said in the divisions of diseases, but it does not improve fully: then cauterization in this case is according to two methods: either cauterization with a burning acute medicine, or with iron.
The cauterization with a burning acute medicine is: take one alum, peel it and cut off the ends from both sides. Then, make an incision in the time of pain with a broad lancet at the place of pain until there is a cavity under the skin where the tooth can be captured.
Insert it then into the cavity under the skin and let it be covered; then apply a suitable amount of pressure on top of it with a plaster and leave it for fifteen hours, then dissolve it and extract the alum, and leave the wound for two or three days: afterwards, place over it a hot compress submerged in butter until the place becomes pus-filled; then treat it with an ointment until it heals.
And if you wish to do this with some burning medicines, which I have written about in the twelfth treatise, on remedies for wounds.
Cauterization with iron is as follows: Hot Iron Cautery, whose shape is as follows.
And it is called Clauilis: because its head's shape is like a nail, in which there is something hollow, and in the middle of it there is a small projection.
Then place it on the location, and hold your hand; and you turn the iron slowly with swiftness; and let the quantity that is to be burnt be equal to its thickness. And lift your hand so that the artery, which is below, is not burnt, and let there be a flow of blood.
Then immerse the cotton in salt water, and place it on the location, and leave it for three days; then immerse the cotton with butter; afterwards take care with ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize this hemicania with the tip of the second type of Cautery. Be careful not to cut the artery in this hemicania, except for an old one specifically.
[Title] On the method of cauterization in old hemicania.
When curing a hemicania, if the treatment mentioned from the previous cure and what was said in the division of diseases does not help: and you see from the illness that what we said with the first cautery or with cautery and fire is insufficient, then it is necessary to use cauterium ignis cultellare until it becomes white after marking the location of pain with a line, whose length is half a digit, or approximately so: and place your hand instead of one, and tighten it until you cut the artery, and reach the bone.
It is necessary that you beware of the hinge part of the jaw, which moves during chewing, so as not to burn the side or the nerve that moves it, thus causing a spasm.
And beware of the flow of blood from the artery which was cut. Indeed, the fear is in its cutting and especially to him who does not know what he does, and is not diligent, nor experienced; and he dismisses the operation first with it.
I will come again with a reminder of the management of bleeding from the cut artery according to its manner, and in the place of this book.
If you see from the illness that this cautery is insufficient and you see the weak body enduring cautery in the middle of the head as we said, then cure the wound until it heals.
And if you wish, administer the cautery which we said in the chapter on the extraction of an artery with a cautery having two knives. For indeed cauterization is better and more effective by this method.
Chapter on the manner of cauterizing ear pain.
When there is pain in the ear due to cold and it is treated with solvents, and with the remaining cure as we said in the division, but the pain does not subside, then cauterize with fire: this is called a puncture, whose form is as follows.
Then make small incisions around the entire ear, after its ignition (burning), as it is being rotated; or around both ears, if the pain is on both sides. Then burn the base of the ear slightly with the cautery after marking the spots with pitch; and let the size of the cautery be ten small points on each ear, and so forth.
Then take care that they heal.
Chapter on the mode of cauterization for tortures.
Chapter VII.
The torture that is cured with cauterization, is not other than those accidents due to phlegm, according to what we said in the divisions of diseases.
And let us avoid cauterizing the species that occur from exhaustion, and from spasm of a nerve.
When you cure this species of torture with hiruses (leeches) and purges (medications to expel waste matter) and gargarisms (mouthwash), and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you cauterize the weak one with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and the second a little below its time (a unit of measure), and third at the junction of the two lips.
And place your cautery on the weaker side of the affected area. Since softening does not occur, unless in the healthy part that appears.
And the shape of cauterization is to cauterize the same with a straight cautery at the base of the upper edge of the ear below the corner of the head, and another at its time (the point), whose length should be according to the length of the thumb. And place your hand with the cautery until a quantity equal to half the thickness of the skin has been burned.
And this is the shape of a cautery and it belongs to the type with a blade (small knife), whose form is as follows: but it should not be too thin, as you see; and it is necessary that the blade is in it without being excessively thick.
Then cure the location (area) with what has been previously mentioned until it heals.
Chapter on the method of cauterization for ancient apoplexy (sudden loss of consciousness caused by a lack of blood supply to the brain).
When ancient apoplexy occurs and your treatment does not help with what has been previously mentioned, and the patient does not have a fever, then you should cauterize him with four cauteries over all of his cornus (horns) of the skull, and a cautery in the middle of his head, as we have said, and a cautery on the back of his head, according to what has been previously mentioned; and the method of cauterization should be as previously described.
Also, it is cauterized over the mouth of the stomach with a cautery; and this is more ultimate.
Then it will be cured, with what has gone before.
Chapter IX.
It is necessary that in a drink there are first, large amounts of hyssop, and purifying pills for the brain.
Then, shave the entire head of the sick person, and place on his head a plaster made from henna described in the plasters' treatise; apply it several times.
For that is the method of cautery: do it according to the same order as I said there.
If he is cured by this (method), it is good. If not (cured): then make three cauteries on the back of his head, which are descending from the top of his head to the lower part of his eye; place a thickness of finger between each cautery.
Then, after care for the cautery, do as before (with the purifying pills).
If you wish an additional treatment and the sick person can tolerate it: then make a cautery in the middle (of the wound or affected area). And if you want an additional treatment: then cauterize it above both horns (of the skull).
Then, care for it until he is cured: and let the cautery be anointed according to the shape mentioned before (with oil).
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in paralysis, and softening.
Chapter X.
It is necessary that you proceed in the mundification of the head with hyson, and with what has been said.
Then scrape the head of the sick person: afterwards cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head, and with a cautery over all the horns of the head, and with a cautery over the back part of it, and three over the spondyles of the neck.
If, however, you need the softening of the body by many of these things, and the sick person is weak and the illness is strong: then cauterize it with four cauteries over the spondyles of the back, and the last one with a cautery, until most of its skin is burned off, and let go of your hand. Then take care of him until he is well: thus cauterize Olive oil.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in epilepsy.
A person with epilepsy should not be cauterized, unless his epilepsy is due to phlegm.
Therefore, it is necessary that you clean the brain of the patient first with hirses (a type of plant used for cleansing) and with the rest of the treatment as we have said earlier: when the patient is seriously ill or is resistant to medications.
If the patient is a child who cannot tolerate medications, then gargarisma (a type of mixture) is administered and cleansing mastications are given to clean the brain before that for many days with good food provision.
Then shave his head, afterwards cauterize him with a single cautery on the mid-point of his head according to what has been previously described; and cauterize another place on his occiput (the back part of the skull), and over all the horns of his head with cautery. If the patient is strong and tolerant, then cauterize him with cauteries as previously described in the presence of paralysis, and apply mollification to his body over the spondylus (a type of vertebra) of the neck and dorsum (back part): and oil the cautery according to the method that has been previously described.
If the patient is a child, then place a subtle cautery according to this method.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in melancholy.
When the cause of melancholy is corrupted humors and gross phlegm, then cauterize him with the cauteries that have been mentioned in the presence of paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is an excess of slopes leading to melancholy and the body of the patient is damp, then give him a drink that cleans his brain, according to what has been previously mentioned earlier: then shave the head of the patient, and afterward make a well-centered turban from linen, similar to a circle.
Then place it in the middle of the head: and a weak person sitting square should hold it from every side.
Then apply the liniment. And it is more suitable from ancient butter of sheep. And heat it above a fire with moderated temperature, as much as a finger can bear when it is inserted into it. Then evacuate it from the middle of his head in a circle, and let it out until it cools down.
Do this to the weak one once a week with the rest of his good regime, until he is cured.
Or if you wish, cauterize it by making many small holes in it, except that you should keep your hand with the cautery; preferably use something that smells good.
For this kind of cauterization moistens the brain with its nature.
Then place on top of it a plate soaked in butter or goose fat.
Chapter on how to cauterize when descending into the eye with water.
Chapter 13.
When you are informed about the beginning of water in the eye by the signs that I said in the division, then begin and clean the weak person's head with him.
And keep him away from all moistness, and make him sit in a bath, for some days in fasting.
Then command him to shave his head, and cauterize it in the middle of his own head. Then cauterize him on both temples with two cauteries, if there is no opening for the descent of water in both eyes at once: or from one side, if there is an opening of water in one eye: and cut with cautery all veins and arteries that are under the skin: and let the cauteries be long in width like the temples: and avoid bleeding.
If you see something from it, then immediately cut it with any medicine that is possible: and I will come with wisdom, which is in the removal of arteries, and cutting of them, and caution against bleeding.
And sometimes it is cauterized on the neck, under two bones, with two lastly produced cauteries.
Chapter on the ancient method of cauterizing in tears.
When the tears of the eyes are old and continuous: and they are above veins and arteries that are manifestly on the outside of the head, it is verified that this is from superfluitates frigidarum phlegmaticarum: then cauterize with the same cautery as I have mentioned in the opening of water, cauterizing in the middle of the head, and with two cauteries on both temples, and with two cauteries on the neck under two bones. And if it is necessary to add, then cauterize him carefully on all sides of the eye, above the edge of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in nasal stench.
When you treat it (the patient), as we said in the division, and the medication does not improve: then rush and give infirmocochia for three nights; afterward shave its head, and cauterize it with a medium cautery, with oil-based cautery. Then cauterize it (the head) with two cauteries and a medium cautery, on top of the eyebrows slightly beneath the hairs.
And take care not to cut the artery.
And this is the form of the claw-shaped cautery.
Chapter on the method of cauterization for softening the eyelid.
When the eyelid of the eye becomes softened due to illness or humidity, then cauterize the eyelid with one cautery, using this moon-shaped cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it (the head) above the eyebrows slightly in all parts with two cauteries; and they should extend from the temples; and let the length of the entire cautery be equal to the length of the eyebrows; and do not move your hand with the cautery, but rather according to the amount that is being heated, the third part of the eyelid.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing the eyelid when the hairs turn inwards and poke the eye.
The instrument (cautery) is of two kinds: either a hot cautery, or a cautery with a burning medicine.
For the hot cautery, instruct the patient to shave beforehand if he is one who cleans himself, until they (hairs) extend and become even. If (they perform the cautery) at its origin: then bind his eyes with an ointment, so that they do not move, until they (wounds) grow.
When they grow and become even, then place the head of the patient in your lap: then mark over the eyelids of his eyes with encaustic, marking that it is in the shape of a myrtle leaf; and let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs.
Then place a warm vessel filled with egg white or slippery elm gum on the eye.
Then heat the cautery, which has this shape.
Then cauterize gradually on the marked places in many spots, until the surface of the skin becomes burned to a depth equal to the shape of a myrtle leaf in its entirety.
And the sign of your health is: if you see the eyelid of the eye already contracting and hairs growing at the site of cautery.
Then withdraw your hand: and release him for three days.
Then place a warm vessel with butter on it until the eschar is removed. Then care for him with ointment until he is healed.
If some hair returns after an hour and the eyelid becomes softened: then repeat the cautery on that spot as you did before.
If the hairs are in the lower part (of the eyelid): then cauterize it, until they grow back to their natural position; and it becomes even so that the hairs do not touch the eye.
It is to be commanded to the sick person that he lets his hair grow until they become long and equal. Make a leaf shape out of paper from cloth in the form of a myrtle leaf.
Then take from known soap and unmixed lime each a weight of an ounce or about that: then grind them together with good grinding, and make it quickly so that it does not become cold. Then, from that (substance) spread it out on the cloth you have made in the shape of a myrtle leaf, and place it over one or both eyelids. Then pour the substance soaked in egg white onto a plate, and keep the head of the sick person in your arms.
Place your index finger on the medicine, and press it slightly. You move (the medicine) whenever the sick person feels the bite of the medicine, because its bite is like fire.
While it continues to feel that bite, then release the medicine and move it with your finger. When the bite subsides, then remove the medicine, and wash the eye with water.
Then consider if the eyelid rises like it is raised by heat or incision, that is good: and if not, then apply the medicine again to the same place where the medicine does not press and does not discolor, until your treatment is even and the eye contracts.
Then place the substance soaked in butter on it until the skin of the burn is removed. Then treat him with a diaphine ointment or another ointment until he is healed.
It is necessary for you to maintain the final protection during the operation so that nothing from the medicine falls into the eye.
If the eyelid becomes softened after a few days and something from the hairs falls into the eye, then apply the medicine again to that place where the eyelid is becoming soft itself, as you did at first. Then treat him until he is healed.
And this is the shape of a myrtle leaf.
And know that human eyes differ in size and smallness. Therefore, let your attention be on this: and the way of rightness for that which is devoted to this art should not be hidden.
Method for cauterizing in lacrimal fistula.
When treating fistula, if the treatment as said in the classifications of diseases does not help: then it is necessary to cauterize it using this method.
Command the sick person to place his head in your armpit, and hold his head with a servant between his hands so that it is not moved or shaken along with his head.
Then place a cotton swab soaked in eye ointment or psyllium mucilage on his eye, and then apply the cautery iron of this shape (as shown below).
It is concave, like the form of a bird's feather quill at one end, with which you make a cautery iron: and if you want it to penetrate to the other end, or if you want it to point upwards in this way.
However, it is better for your use that the concave part be towards the work.
Then squeeze the fistula if it is open and drain pus from it, and excise it; and if it is not open, then open it and drain its pus.
Then place the cautery iron on it, which has been heated very strongly.
And hold your hand near the cautery iron from the eye to the nose so that your hand does not wander or the sick person moves; and you will place the cautery iron on the eyelid fat and destroy it.
If, therefore, you reach the beginning of your cautery to the bone, it will be good. And if not: then apply the cautery iron once or twice as needed; and let it go for three days.
Then place cotton with butter on it, and treat it with an ointment of antiseptic, until it heals.
If they exceed forty days and are not cured: then place sharp corrosive medicine upon it until the bone is exposed; and shave it according to what comes in its chapter.
And another method of cautery for the fistula, which some of the first called. Stretch to the place of the fistula and close it; then put in its fissure a thin cannula, that is, a thin tube, whose form is as follows. Pour over it an amount of drachmas of melted lead, and hold your hand with good retention on the cannula, so that the weak one does not move at all, lest the melted lead reaches or comes to his eye.
And it is necessary for you to place over the weak one's eye a warm infusion of eggs in milk, or in water.
For lead burns the place of the fistula and heals it with wonderful healing.
If the fistula is cured along with what we said from cautery, and with healing, it is good. And if not, then it is necessary to make a nasal opening and bring the fistula back to the course of the nose, according to what comes in its own place.
[Chapter heading] On the method of cauterizing in fissures of the lips.
Often occur on the lip fissures, which are called hairs, and especially in the lips of children.
When you treat these fissures, with what I said in the division of diseases, and healing does not help, then make a small cautery iron in this shape.
And let its hollow be according to the fineness of a knife's edge.
Then place it quickly into those cracks, until the cautery reaches the depth of the cracks.
Then care for it with pitch until it heals.
Method of Cauterization for a Mouth Fistula.
When an abscess occurs at the root of a tooth, or in the palate, or in the roots of the teeth: then it produces pus and bursts; afterwards it becomes old, and the pus runs and forms a fistula: then care for it, and do not apply treatment to it, then if necessary heat cautery according to its quantity, which can be inserted into the fistula. Then insert the heated iron into the hole of the fistula, and hold your hand, until the hot iron reaches its depth and its end: do this once or twice.
Then care for it afterwards, with what we said about treatment, until it is healed.
If therefore the pus separates and heals, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place, and remove the rotten bone according to what comes out at its head.
Chapter on Cauterizing in Softened Gums and Teeth.
When the gums become soft due to moisture and the teeth move, and treatment with medicine does not help: then place the head of the sick person in your lap.
Then heat the cautery, whose shape will come later, so that you place the cannula on a tooth: and insert into it the heated cautery hastily: and hold your hand for a while until the sick person feels the heat of the fire has reached the root of the tooth.
And remove your hand: then repeat the cautery as often as you wish.
Then let the sick person fill his mouth with water and salt, and hold it for an hour: and rinse himself.
For a moving tooth is strengthened, and softened gums are tightened, and the corruption of moisture dries up.
Method of Cauterizing Tooth Pain.
When tooth pain is due to coldness or there is coldness within the tooth, or worms, and treatment with medicines does not help: then the Cautery is applied in two ways: either Cautery with butter; or Cautery with fire.
The Cautery with butter is as follows: take butter and boil it in an iron cauldron or copper. Then receive the bandage and roll it over the end of the wound. Then immerse it in melted butter and place it quickly on the painful tooth, hold it until it cools; then repeat this process several times until the heat of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, immerse wool or a bandage in cold butter and place it on the painful tooth; then place heated iron over it until the heat reaches the depth of the tooth's hollow.
The cauterization with fire is as follows: stretch out the probe made of brass or iron. Let there be something thick in his body so that the sharpness of the fire does not reach the weak bone.
Then apply the cauterization tool with fire, whose shape will come; place it on that tooth and hold your hand until the tool cools.
Repeat this process several times, as pain will disappear, either on the same day or on another day.
It is necessary to fill the weak bone with good butter during the application of the cauterization and hold it for an hour; then spit it out.
And this is the form of the cauterization.
Cauterize with whichever end you wish, according to what is possible; and this is the shape of the probe.
Chapter on the method of cauterization in abscesses.
When the boil is from phlegm and cold moistures and not obedient to digestion by medicines and desires digestion quickly: then to the hollow concave Cautery, whose form is this.
Having two open extremities, so that the smoke may exit from the Cautery at one of the extremes: and place it (the cautery) heated upon the boil once, and again if necessary, until it reaches the depth of the boil.
If the boil is small: then place the Cautery according to the size of the boil.
Then leave it for three days, and place upon it a heated plaster soaked in butter, until what the fire has burned is removed.
Then care for it with tooth ointment until the form of the canal heals.
§ Method of cauterizing in throat hoarseness and constriction of breathing.
When moistures prevail over the canal of the lung, and especially when it is accompanied by coldness of the temperament, then the ill person should first be evacuated with soluble medicines.
Then cauterize it (the affected area) in the neck at the root of the throat in a depressed location: and beware not to reach the throat with the Cautery nor the skin, unless something of its (the Cautery's) effect is needed.
Then cauterize it (the affected area) with another Cautery at the junction of the neck and shoulder blade in the last part of its end: and let the Cautery be like a nail according to the method described earlier.
Then care for it with what was mentioned before until it heals.
§ Method of cauterizing in diseases of the lung and cough.
When there is coughing and sickness of the lungs due to cold humors, and the person is not feverish, nor does he have consumption, and the sickness is old: then cauterize it with two cauteries above the clavicle in depressed, smooth, empty places. With another cautery in the middle of the chest between two nipples: and let the cautery be cylindrical in shape, as was previously described.
And if your treatment is to puncture with a cautery named the Punctum, whose shape was previously described in the treatment of ear pain: and let there be punctures from thirty punctures up to another.
Then care for it with what was described before until it is healed.
And now let the cautery have three branches in this shape. Because cauterization is applied with it, when you do it with one of three cauteries.
Chapter 27.
When the head is dislocated due to help [positioning], and it does not heal within an hour of returning from its dislocation, until that has become accustomed to return, then it should be dislocated slightly, which happens as we have already testified, at this point it is necessary to reduce the dislocation first. Then the patient lies on his back or on a healthy side. Then the skin is peeled, which is on the inside of the Titillico towards the top with your left hand fingers: and if the joint is dislocated towards the inside.
Then fire is placed in a cautery having two hollows. Its shape is as follows:
Then cauterize the skin until it penetrates to the other side, and the figure of the cauterization will come with four cauteries.
And sometimes the cauterization is with a cautery having three prongs, therefore the figure of the cauterization will be that of six cauteries: and these prongs are according to the subtlety of the tendon tested.
And this is the form of the cautery having three prongs.
And sometimes an additional one is added to this method, therefore there are eight cauteries.

For joining it becomes strong and moisture is removed; the sick person recovers.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing the stomach.
When cold and many humidities occur in the stomach, until it separates itself from its composition and produces many catarrhs for it, and continuous methods of treatment do not help; then the sick person should lie on his back, extend his legs, and stretch out his hands. Then cauterize with three cauteries, a cautery of the size of one finger under the concavity of the chest and a curved cautery on the shoulder, and two cauteries below the sides of one cautery, until a triangular figure of the cauteries appears. And extend them apart so that they do not join together, when they produce pus.
And the depth of the cautery is the size of two thirds of the thickness of the skin.
And let the figure of cauteries be in this shape without addition. And if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this shape: and let the cautery that is made for this purpose be one in the shape of a circle according to this shape.
The stomach is to be cauterized by touching it with this cautery that frightens it. Let there be marks on the stomach at the point where you wish to apply encaustum. Then cauterize that point with the pointed cautery. Then care for it with the remedy that preceded until it heals.
On the mode of cauterizing the epigastric region (frigidum).
When there occurs in the epigastric region (Epate) pain due to coldness and moistness, or due to excessive gas, until it exits from its natural expulsion of superfluous matter and the patient is cured with what has been said, and it does not improve in this: then it is necessary that the patient lies down on his neck, and marks with encaustum three cauteries in this shape, and the same amount below the hypocondria, where a man's elbow reaches; and let the space between each cautery be of the size of a finger; and let the cautery be of the length of the body straight; and do not press your hand tightly with the cautery.
And let the thickness of that which is burned be according to the thickness of the skin, without any addition; and let the patient stand on his feet.
If he is not standing, then let him lie down who has already extended his legs and raised his arms.
This is the shape of the cautery.
It is possible for you to cauterize these cauteries with a pointed cautery when subtlety and wisdom are present in your art.
"Take care not to proceed too far in cauterization, lest the entire thickness of the skin be burnt, for the body as a whole is burnt, and it reaches the intestines; since there the skin is delicate, therefore you know this.
"On the method of cauterizing abscesses of the liver.
"When it happens that an abscess is about to burst and one wishes to know whether it is within the flesh of the liver or its membrane; if it is within the flesh of the liver, there is a dull pain without sharpness, and if it is in the membrane of the liver, with a very acute pain: and you see that the treatment has become tiring.
"Therefore the patient should lean forward on his neck. "Then mark the position of the abscess with a hot iron, and then heat an iron similar to a probe. "This is its shape (the probe). "And cauterize with the probe until the entire skin is burnt and it reaches the pus, until all the pus comes out; then treat him with care for bursting abscesses, until he is cured.
"And one should not use this method of cauterization, unless one's study extends to the art of medicine; and through whose hands these diseases often recur with experience: then he may dare to perform such an operation.
"But it is better to let it be (the abscess), in my opinion.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing pleurisy.
"The ancients said that a probe with the roots of Aristolochia should be used for cold pleurisy in this manner. "And it is to take a dry and long root of Aristolochia, one longer root which can be found among them, and let it be as thick as a finger. Then immerse her in oil and burn it in fire. Then cauterize it with a single cautery where the neck meets the shoulder, and with two small cauteries on the areas slightly below the chin, in that region under the beard.
And with two more cauteries on the area between the fifth and sixth ribs towards the back, and another cautery in the center of the chest, and another one above the stomach. And with three more cauteries from the back: one where it is between the two scapulas, and two more on both sides of the chest, with the lower cautery where it is between the two scapulas.
And you should not press your hand with the cautery, rather let it smell of skin.
And some ancient men have said that there are those who use a cautery made of iron resembling a rod and burn it inside the chest until it reaches the same place as the boil, and the pus comes out, just as we said in the case of an abscess in Epates.
But in this perforation with the cautery, there is a fear that either the sick person will die immediately or a fistula will occur in a place where healing cannot be achieved.
Chapter 32: The method of cauterizing the spleen.
When you treat the illness of the spleen, as we said in the treatment of diseases and your treatment does not work, then cauterization is to be done in this case in three ways, all of which are correct.
One is to make three or four cauteries in a row along the length of the spleen according to the shape of the cauterizations described earlier [in the book].
And let every cautery's size be that of a finger's thickness, more or less.
The method of cauterizing the liver, as we mentioned earlier, should be equal on both sides.
And do not press your hand with the cautery: let it be weak and prone onto its backside.
Another method of cauterizing is: having heated the cautery with two openings, as we mentioned in the chapter on dislocation of the shoulder; and peel the skin, which is directly above the spleen, where the weak arm arrives; let your peeling be along the body's width, so that the cauteries fall along the body's length.
Then introduce two openings heated very strongly, until they penetrate the skin from one side; then remove the cautery; thus there will be four cauteries.
And if you wish to cauterize with a cautery having three openings.
Then care for the cautery after you have released it, let it emit pus for many days; for this is more conducive than the other treatments that preceded it in healing.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in Hydropsy.
A cautery does not fall in Hydropsy, unless it is properly applied.
When you treat a Hydropsy with the methods of treatment we mentioned earlier, and it does not improve, then you must cauterize it with four cauteries around the navel, one on the stomach, another on the liver, another on the spleen, two behind the loins, and one on the chest and another on the stomach; let the depth of the cautery be close to the thickness of the skin.
Then release the open cautery, so that it emits pus for a long time.
And it is not right to evacuate the sick from treatment after cautery, for it is necessary that two intentions are gathered towards him: and healing will hasten towards him with divine aid.
The form of the cautery for the abdomen should be clavilis; according to its preceding form. And the form of the cautery for the back should be oliuaris; according to its preceding form.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing Feet and Legs.
When they are amputated in Hydropico and filled with citrine water: it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot at the navicular bone, which is between auricular and annular; then remove your hand with the cautery, and do not twist it. Then remove your hand. Do not go back to it at all.
For citrine water will flow out, and let the cautery be in this form.
Then make two cauteries on each leg, and let the cautery be at the end of a cultellar cautery throughout the entire leg; and let the cautery be along the length of the leg, one below the knee, and the other lower than that, about half the length of the leg. And over the whole hip two cauteries; and leave the open cautery without treatment for a long time: until some water flows out of it; then cure it with what we have said.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing for the solution of the abdomen.
Chapter XXXV.
When the solution of the belly becomes loose due to cold and moistness, until it weakens the powers retained and digestive, which are in the stomach and intestines: and it is cured with methods of treatment, but it does not heal: and you see a person enduring an excessive force of heat, then cauterize him with a large cautery on his own stomach, according to what has preceded in the cauterization of the stomach with a circular cautery, and four subtle cauteries around the navel, with a subtle claw-shaped cautery: and a cautery over alum on top of blisters large or with two cauteries.
If you see excessive moisture and a person enduring it, then cauterize him with a cautery on his chest (pecten) and on the whole hip: and perhaps you may add two small cauteries near the large one on the stomach.
For indeed, this treatment is progressing, of which the benefit does not wander off.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing hemorrhoids.
Chapter XXXVI.
When in the anus there are many old hemorrhoids or one, and they are made of thick fluids, cold or corrupt moistures, and they are treated with what we have said before, but treatment does not improve: then cauterize them with three cauteries on the lower part of the loin under the flank slightly triangularly, and with a cautery under the navel as if two fingers.
And if you think that his stomach is cold and food is not digested, and you see his face becoming pale: then cauterize him on the stomach with a large cautery, according to what has preceded: and with a cautery on his liver (Epar), and another one on his spleen (Splenem), with a cautery claw-shaped (clauili): and leave the open cautery for some time: then treat him until he is healed.
Head XXXVII.
When you excise althelul (a type of tumor or growth), then apply a burning cautery similar to a rod. Then introduce the burning (cautery) into the excised althelul; and withdraw your hand until the cautery reaches the opening of the vein from which blood flows; do this once or twice.
If there are many althelul (tumors or growths), then cauterize each one with a separate cautery as we have described. Then take care of them, applying to them the remedy that is used for them until they heal.
And if you cauterize it with a large cautery on alcatin (a type of stone), this is more beneficial for the treatment.
On the method of cauterizing a fistula in the anus.
Head XXXVIII.
When the sick person does not obey the incision and operation as we have described in its place, and is afraid of it, perhaps he will heal with a cautery.
If a fistula occurs and discharges pus and becomes corrupt, cure it. It is necessary to test it as it should be, with a probe of subtle material. Then find out the depth of it by means of a probe.
Then heat the cautery which is like a rod. Then insert yourself heated (into) that fistula and find out the depth to which the probe has penetrated.
Then repeatedly apply the cautery to it until all the corrupt bodies are burnt up, once, twice, or thrice, according to the necessity of your case.
And be careful not to burn the nerve or the large vein (if it is there); or if the fistula opens up to the bladder or the intestine, then be careful of these places altogether.
And do not make that (action), unless when the fistula is in a fleshy place; and consider that it does not penetrate.
Then care for the place until it has healed.
If, however, the place is sealed and the materials are cut off from it and remain for a long time; then you will know that it has healed completely.
If the materials do not fall off from it, then you will know that it is penetrating, or that a rotten bone is at a deeper part of it, or something like that; whose memory will come back to its place.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing kidneys.
When pain in the kidneys occurs from cold or from thick wind, and it is weakened by this disease of the body, then it is necessary to cauterize it above the flank on both kidneys, with a cautery over the entire kidney with a cautery claw, whose precedent has been remembered.
And perhaps we cauterize it again in the same flank. Therefore, three white lines will come. Thus, there will be more relief in the latter (stage).
Chapter on the method of cauterizing the bladder.
When weakness and softening occur in the bladder due to cold and moisture, so that it does not hold urine properly, then cauterize it in the lower part of the abdomen below the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, with a cautery on one side from the right side of the abdomen and another on the left side: let the length of this cauterization be according to the size of the knuckle of the thumb: and cauterize it with a lower back cautery, or two cauteries if necessary: and let the preceding cautery be as that of the claw.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing the uterus.
When coldness and moistness occur in the Matrix (womb), and it is forbidden for conception because of this, and its menstrua are corrupted, and the summoning of them is delayed, and there is pain at their approach, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with three cauteries around the navel, as we said in the cauterization of the bladder, and with a cautery below on the back, or with two cauteries: and let the cautery be a claw.
The Method of Cauterizing the Womb in Dislocation.
When the mucous humors flow out to the perineum of the womb and become the cause of its displacement from its place; and the sign of this is that one leg is extended over the other when they are brought together: and a gap or void is found in the place of dislocation.
Therefore, it is necessary to cauterize the weak spot above the perineum of the womb with a similar cautery in a circle; after you have marked the circumference of the perineum with hot iron, as is customary: and that the perineum falls into the middle of the circle.
If this cautery is not at hand, then cauterize it with three cauteries, using a large lard-caustery; and the depth of the cautery should be in proportion to the thickness of the skin.
Then take care of it until it heals.
The Method of Cauterizing for Sciatica.
When pain occurs in the ankle joint, and its cause is coldness and moistness: and the sick one is treated as mentioned before, but it does not improve, then that should be allowed to heal by itself: then it is necessary that you dissolve the sick person from thick humors with foul pills or artificial pills, and similar ones. Then cauterize him.
And the method of cauterization is according to two modes: either cauterization with medicines applied, or cauterization with fire.
Cauterization with fire, is according to many modes.
One of these modes is that you cauterize over the ankle joint with three triangular cauteries in this manner. And make their depth good or bad. And let the space between each cautery be of the thickness of a finger: and let the cautery be covered with oil.
Sometimes however, a cauterization takes place in the middle of the ankle joint itself. Therefore there are four cauteries.
And if you wish to cauterize with a ring, whose shape preceded in the ankle joint dislocation, one: so that the ring encompasses the entire ankle.
And burn off the thickness of the skin entirely.
This is the method of cauterization in sciatica, when the pain is attached to the ankle itself and does not extend to the hip and leg.
If it extends to the hip and leg, then cauterize it with two cauteries on the hip, at the place where the sick one indicates, in which there is pain, and your cautery four fingers on the outer part of the shin: and let the cautery be a knife-shaped one.
And let the depth of the cautery be according to the thickness of the skin.
If the sick person indicates that the pain extends almost to the toes of the foot, then cauterize it there where he indicates with a cautery, with one, two, or four, or more, if necessary.
If he indicates that the pain is turned towards the leg below the knee, then cauterize it there with a one-edged cautery.
And be careful in every cauterization of yours, that you do not burn the nerve or the great artery, and attract harm to it through this, or contracture.
And I myself have seen one and another, from those who cauterized above the ankle, and burned too much in the cauterization, and the leg became swollen until the tumor reached the foot, and it was perforated completely, and the whole foot was corrupted: then the abdomen burst open, and death followed this.
If the pain is in two parts at once, cauterize each one according to this method.
And some wise men said in cauterizing the ankle, that this is the method of the cautery. Make a small crucible of iron, whose diameter is half the size of the palm: and it should be at its mouth according to the thickness of the nut of a thumb or less: and inside this small crucible there should be a third small crucible.
And let the space that is between every crucible be as much as the size of a knuckle: and let the crucibles be open from two sides: and let their height be like a knuckle, or two knuckles: and make handles for them from iron appropriately placed in the crucibles.
Then it is heated in the fire until it turns red and throws sparks: then it should be placed on a potsherd of the ankle, with the sick person lying down on his healthy side. Cauterize it therefore with three round cauteries at one time.
Then let him go for three days. Afterwards pack it with butter and let the open wound heal for many days. Then treat him with ointment until he is healed.
Albucasis says, we have not used this kind of cautery enough, because of the horror of its appearance; and therefore, because few are found who can bear to look upon it.
Nevertheless, it is one of the good cauterizations for him who can endure it and finds a place for it.
The cautery with medicines driving it is, you shall make two small bags containing a perforated armillary, from which descends the key of its door made of bronze or iron, as long as the height of the wall; and on the height of these there should be two knots, or as if they themselves.
And the space that is between the two should be of the thickness of a finger and they should be open from below and above; and it should hold each other according to this form.
Then place it on a box with an anchor lying upon the sick side. And press your hand much upon the box with the anchor. Then pour water between the two circles which has been heated a little by fire and hold it as much as an hour's time; and let the sick bear the biting of it and its burning, for he himself finds the biting like that of fire, until the biting ceases.
Then wash your hand with the tool and clean the anchor completely with warm water and sweet water; then let it go for three days.
And place butter upon it until the blackness of burning is removed; and let it go for some days, and pus will run out from it. The remedy is at last in aid.
Then apply a cure with ointments until it heals.
If the pain spreads to the hip or leg: make a splint for him in such a way that it contains water, as you did in the case of the broken bone equally.
And this is the method of hot water: I have already written about it in the treatise on rectifying remedies. Take two parts of lime and unburnt plaster, grind each separately; put them in a new pot whose lower part is pierced with a small hole, according to the amount that will be added to the radius; place another earthenware pot underneath; pour over it lime and plaster from sweet water, so that both are submerged by about a finger; press them down with your hand; let go of the pot, until the sharp water goes down to the bottom of the earthenware pot.
Then gather that water entirely, and pour it over another mortar; and grind, until it returns.
For that very reason it will then be strong and highly sharp, which is administered in many medical operations, and in the cauterization of other members. Because it makes the action of fire itself.
And among the medicines, with which they are cauterized (or burnt), such as tartar emetic, also strychnine, and almond oil with soap, in such a way that both are mixed together.
And indeed, Galen relates the story of a certain man from the ancient times, who was cured of the pain in the anus and the sciatic vein; and he greatly praised his cure. And he said that it did not require any other treatment, and that he was cured from the pain in one application, until he reported that perhaps he himself entered the bath, and came out already healthy.
And it is to be taken from green seitarag; and if green seitarag is not found, dry one should be taken, recently; and it should be ground very much with a little fat, and placed over the anus, where there is pain, or thigh, or hip; and it should be tied, and allowed to stay for three hours, or until the sick person feels the relaxation of the burning sensation. Then introduce it into the bath.
When his body becomes hot, introduce it onto a bed. For the pain subsides, and he is cured.
And know that no one should use a cautery with these medicines unless after the evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides himself said that the feces of goats, when with it the sciatic vein is cauterized, should be added to it; and a cautery is made according to this method. Take flax (or linen), immerse it in old oil, and place it over the deep place which is between the big toe of the foot and the sole, and is closer to the sole.
Then take dried goat droppings, heat it over fire until it becomes charcoal.
Place it on the flax and let it burn out (completely). Then do this again. Do not cease to do that until sensation arrives through the mediation up to the ankle, and the pain stops.
And this method of cauterization is called Vaccinum cauterization (or branding).
Chapter on cauterization for back pain.
Whenever there is back pain due to various causes such as fall, blow, excessive evacuation, and similar conditions, due to the infiltration of cold and moist matter; cauterization only applies in this specific case, which is done by the infiltration of cold matter.
Therefore, after evacuation (bowel movement) of the sick person with foul-smelling pills and similar things, three lines should be drawn on the back where there is pain, following the width of the palm; after marking each line with encaustic in five cauterizations or more depending on the quantity that comes from the strength of the patient; and make cauterization by cauterization puncture.
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauterizations along with the medial claw shape.
Chapter on the method of cauterization for humpback (kyphosis).
This illness often occurs in small children.
The sign of its beginning in children is that it happens above them with a constriction during inspiration at elevation, and you find it at the bottom of the spine of the back and the nodes of this part, which has already begun to appear over the other spines.
When you see it and wish to treat it, then cauterize it with a cautery that is in the shape of a circle.
The cautery should catch the entire spine part equally: and if you wish to cauterize around the spine with a pointed cautery, do two or three lines, and let the points be close together.
Then care for the place until it heals as we have said.
And beware not to administer the cautery on a hump that is formed from a spasm of the nerve.
Chapter on Cauterization in Gout and Joint Pain.
When the pains of joints are caused by cold wetness that is poured out to any part of the body, then when pain occurs in the feet, according to medical custom, it should be called gout properly.
When gout caused by cold is being treated with methods of treatment and the pains do not subside, then cauterization removes them.
And it is that you should cauterize him after evacuation around the joint of the foot, with many cauteries: and let the cautery be Olive Oil.
And if you need to puncture the sole of the foot, then do it with a pointed cautery. If the pains ascend to the knees or other joints, and it often happens this way, then cauterize it over all the knee with three or four cauteries from every side, with the same cautery of Claw.
If more than one are necessary for you with this cautery, then cauterize it. Do not immerse your hand in the cautery, rather let it be about the thickness of the skin.
If the pains rise to the knees and back, then administer what was said about cautery in its own chapter.
If the pains are only in the hands, then pierce around the circumference of the nails, as two lines are rolled up.
If pain remains in the fingers, then pierce them all, over every knuckle and over the back of the hand.
If pains rise after days to elbows or shoulders, then cauterize both from all sides.
And do not evacuate the weak from good management, from receiving medicine. For if there is good management and phlegm is evacuated, it will be cured with the help of God with this cautery.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in ruptures.
When there is a rupture in the groins and the intestine or yarn goes down to the testicle, and it is close by: then one must order that the weak person should abstain from food on his day. And let him use laxatives so that stool comes out of his stomach.
Then let him sit between your hands on his back: and order him to hold his breath until the yarn comes out or the intestine appears.
Then bring him back with your fingers, and mark with a hot iron under the rupture on the back of the hand with a sign whose end is similar to half a circle above the body.
Then heat the iron cautery in this form until it becomes white and throw small pieces of charcoal onto it. Then reduce the intestine, or the hernia to its hollow. Then place the attendant's hand over the location so that the intestine does not come out: and you have already opened between the limbs of the sick person, and placed a retractor under it, and another serving on his limbs, and another on his chest who holds the hands.
Then place the cautery over that mark, with your hand holding the cautery upright. And hold it until you follow the bone with it; or repeat with another tool if you are not able to follow it to the bone in the first instance.
And be careful to observe the exit of the intestine during your cauterization, lest you burn it and bring harm upon the sick person or great misfortune occur.
And know that when you do not follow the bone with the cautery, the operation is of no benefit.
And it is necessary that the cautery for children be delicate, according to their measure.
Then take care with the remaining ointments until he is healed.
And let the sick person lie on his back for forty days until the wound is healed.
And it is necessary to give him nourishment for the duration of his treatment, which will soften his stomach, lest the intestine come out during attempts and evacuations.
Then when he wishes to rise after forty days, then administer a well-made ligament and let him hold it for another forty days.
And he should be diminished in labor, and in food and drink intake, and in violent speech.
For when he is subjected to this regime, he will heal completely.
And I shall speak of the treatment for hernias with incision in its own chapter.
When hernias occur in the remaining abdomen, and they are beginning and wish to be stopped, then cauterize the hernia with a round cautery according to its size; and let that which is burned be as the third part of it from then on. Then take care of yourself, as I have said, and do not add to it.
And some first ones said: that a rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautionery, in this shape.
After it is signed with hot iron, and a line is placed that runs through the width on the upper side of the rupture, and another line towards below. And place your hand in the middle with a nail-like cautionery.
But the first cautionery is easier and better.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing for pain due to rupture or trauma.
Chapter 48.
When pain occurs in some limbs due to rupture or trauma and the pain persists for a long time and there is no cure with medicine, then it is necessary to be cauterized with a cautionery of puncture point.
And the cautionery of all members should be according to its size and its smallness, and its weakness, and its power, and the location of torsion, and pain from it.
If he is cured by the first cautionery, it is good. If not: then apply another cautionery on top of it.
Because by the custom of these pains they are changed from one member to another that is closer to it. Therefore you should follow them with cautionery until the weak one is cured.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing for leprosy.
The leprous, however, are sometimes helped by great cautionery. And especially the species of leprosy that comes from rottenness of phlegm and melancholy: when it is considered to cauterize it itself.
If leprosy is beginning and it has been treated with what was said in the division, and it does not decrease nor stop: and fear that corruption will spread over the entire complexion of it: then cauterize him on top of his head with five cautioneries: one in the middle of the head known, and the second below it towards the forehead at the end of the hairline, and two above the two horns, and one behind the nuchal bone.
Place your thumb lightly on the cautery until it makes a small impression on the bone, and the cortex should dislocate: to relieve the expiration of large vapors from it, and cauterize also over the spleen as previously described.
If however, the leprosy has already spread over the sick person and is clearly visible: then it is necessary to cauterize with those cauteries that were mentioned earlier in the head, and with a cautery on the tip of the nose, and with two cauteries on both cheekbones, and with two cauteries on both shoulder blades, and six on the hip bones, and one large one over alhahosos near the tail and one on it, in the same almeidati: and with two on the ankles: namely, on each ankle with one, and with two on the thighs, and two on the upper arms, and two on the elbows, and two on the tendons of the chest, and cauterize it over all the joints of his fingers of both hands and feet, and cauterize over every calcaneum of his feet, and burn the palms of his hands.
Be careful with the nerves that are above the last calcaneus to avoid burning them.
And sometimes the cautery is applied on the forehead, and another on the stomach, and another on the ebar.
And know that, the more you apply the cautery, the greater the benefit and the stronger it becomes.
And know that, the sick person does not feel pain from the cautery as healthy people do; this is because his body has already become numb.
It is necessary that the cauteries be of different sizes and shapes according to the members and joints; this is based on the types of iron instruments as previously described.
Then, prepare a cautery from wheat flour and honey, and for the rest of the treatment, until it heals.
Method of Cauterization in Sleep.
When a part of the body is numbed (stupet) and treated with medicines, oils, plasters, but does not heal, then cauterize the affected part using cauteries, according to the size of the member or its diminished state.
And let your cautery penetrate slightly into the thickness of the skin. Then take care of it with an ointment until it heals.
And when cauterization is performed for certain numbness that occurs in the hand and foot, in the spine at the nerve exit point moving that limb; and the numbness is removed.
But do not presume to perform it (cauterization) on that unless the one who knows about the structure of the body and the course of nerves moving the body is wise.
Chapter LXI.
When Albaraz (a type of wound?) becomes old and does not receive anything from the arts of medicine; then cauterize it with a deep cautery slightly, according to the thickness of the skin, until the white disappears and its color changes.
Then take care of it with wheat flour and lentils with rose oil, and leaves of arnoglossa (a type of fern), and blood of a dove and of a heron; each part should be equal; mix all these together, spread them on a cloth, and let them adhere to the location until it heals.
Chapter on Cauterization for Cancer.
When cancer is beginning, and you wish to stop it: then cauterize it with a circular cautionery around its circumference, as it revolves.
The wise say that it should be cauterized with the last cautery in the middle.
I, however, do not find that to be so: because I fear that it will burn, and I have already seen that happen several times.
It is truer, however, to cauterize it around its circumference with a circle, as we have said; or with many cauteries.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in Adubelati.
Chapter LIII: When someone has Adubelati that is slow to mature, either because of excessive production or due to weakness from old age and scant blood supply, or because one wishes to hasten the maturation of Adubelati, then cauterize it around its circumference with many small cauteries by puncturing.
