Place it [the instrument] in the middle of Adubelati, until it penetrates the skin; and let the cautery that follows be weakened, so that its course may be purified.
Then take care of it until it heals.
Chapter on the mode of cauterizing in a corrosive disease.
Chapter LIV [The forty-fourth chapter].
A corrosion is not anything except corruption walking in a limb and consuming it, just as fire eats dry wood.
If therefore you see a corrosion in a place that can bear a cautery with fire, then apply much cautery, small and large nails, according to what suits the place where the corrosion is located.
Then cauterize it from all sides until you eradicate the entire corruption and nothing remains of it deep within.
Then let it be for three days and place finely ground sulfur with oil on the cauterized places until all scabs and all corruption are eradicated.
Then care for it with ointments that promote flesh growth.
If therefore you see that after three days flesh is born in a healthy way, in which there is no corruption, it is good.
And if not: then repeat the cautery on what remains from the corrupted places.
A corrosion is sometimes treated with an acidic medication. The corrosion itself arises where the cautery was.
However, a cautery with fire is more effective; and I myself have said that the cauterization of it with an acidic medication is used in division; so take it whenever you need it there.
Chapter on the mode of cauterizing in nails and warts.
Chapter LV [The forty-fifth chapter].
This illness often occurs in the lower parts of the feet and it is a thick, filtered matter that injures the foot.
The cautery is indeed of two kinds: the cautery with fire, and the cautery with hot water.
As for the type with fire, it should be made similar to a bird's talon in shape: which is to be made of iron, according to its size that contains a nail from all sides; and it should be fine at the edges.
Then place the heated [tool] on the nail. Then turn the hand with the cautery around the nail, until the cautery reaches the depth of the nail; and leave it for three days, until it begins to emit pus. Then apply ointment with forest herbs, crushed with salt; and leave the ointment on it at night. It will be rooted out by its roots.
Then care for the place with a gentle ointment until it heals.
If they are not converted and occur frequently on the surface of the body, particularly in hands and feet: then administer cauterization with hot water; and it is to be had that you take a cannula made of copper, iron or bird's feather; and place it on the nail, or althea. Then pour a small amount of hot water into the cannula; hold your hand and turn it with pressure for a short time, so that the tip of the cannula is pressed onto the root of the nail, and let the hot water find its way to the depth, to the root of the nail: and wait briefly for the weak one over the bite of the hot water for an hour.
Then leave it, for the nail will be rooted out with its roots.
Thus do this one after another, until you come to all who are on the body.
Then care for them when they have been rooted out, with that which generates flesh from ointments.
Method of Cauterization During a Shake/Tremor.
If a tremor occurs from cold in the nerve or from quartan fever or another cause, then it is necessary to cauterize it with four or five cauteries on the dorsal vertebrae, and between each vertebra with a cautery, and in its chest with a cautery, and over its stomach with a cautery.
The tremor is quieted when the cautery is applied to oil, and health from cold illness hastens.
Method of Cauterization of Albathir.
Si accidit alicui Tremor ex frigore in ner
Sometimes the foul Albathir are expelled from the body, that is, pustules which are made from corrupted gross matter.
Therefore, when they appear, it is necessary to cauterize over every head of the pustule with a subtle cautery and myrtle wood whose tip is burned with fire. Or with the root of the long aristolochia. Or with a lenticular cautery.
And sometimes they are cauterized with a small piece of raw meat, at the beginning of their expulsion according to this method; and they are not increased; and superfluity is broken causing them to be expelled, and they heal from them.
However, it must be done after the evacuation with phlebotomy.
Method of Cauterization for Bleeding from an Artery in a Wound.
Often bleeding from an artery occurs which is cut near the wound, which happens externally, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cauterization of a limb, and similar to them; and it is difficult to separate it.
When therefore it happens to someone, then hurry with your hand to the opening of the artery, and place your index finger upon it; and bind it tightly, until the blood is held under your finger, and nothing escapes from there.
Then place a small oil lamp cautery on fire, and many in number; and blow upon them until they are very hot.
Then take one, either small or large, according to the wound and place where the artery is broken, and place the cautery upon the vein after you remove your finger; and hold the cautery until the blood is cut off.
If it is expelled when you remove your finger from the opening of the artery, and extinguish the cautery, then take another cautery quickly, from those which are prepared in the fire.
Therefore do not cease to do that with one after another until the blood is cut off.
And be careful, lest you burn the nerve which is there, and other harm befall the weak patient.
And know that when blood flows from the artery, then it is not possible to cut it; especially since the artery is large, unless with one of four methods. Or with a cautery, as we said. Or with extraction, when it is not extracted. For when it is drawn out, its extremities contract and the blood is cut off. Or it is tied with a strong thread ligature. Or medicines are placed upon it of the kind that are for cutting off blood, and it is bound with a tight tourniquet.
He who administers the amputation with a ligament and tourniquet, or with things burning, and similar ones, does not help him completely, unless rarely.
If it happens to someone and the physician is not present nor medicine: then let him begin with the positioning of the index finger over the opening of the vein as we have mentioned, and tightly constricting it until the blood is besieged from above the wound, and upon the artery. And the finger should not be removed, above it with cold water of intense coldness always, until the blood freezes, swells, and is severed.
And meanwhile he should consider in him what is needed from a cautery, or medicine.

Chapter: On the treatment of water accumulating in children's heads.
Chapter I.
Know that this illness frequently occurs in children during childbirth, or when the midwife squeezes the child's head without due care.
And sometimes it also happens for reasons hidden and unknown to us.
And indeed I have never seen this illness in anyone other than children, and death has come swiftly to every one of them whom I saw; for that reason it seemed to me advisable to abandon the operation.
And I myself have seen a child whose head was full of water and whose head swelled every day until it could no longer sit up on its own due to the size of its head; furthermore, the moisture increased until he died.
This swelling, indeed, either occurs between skin and bone, or it occurs beneath the bone at the forehead.
And the operation in this case, if there is swelling between skin and bone and the abscess is small, then it is necessary to make a single incision in the middle of the head, extending as far as two finger-widths; the length of the incision should be such that the moisture can drain away.
And this is the form of the spatula.
If, however, the swelling has increased more, and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions according to this shape.
If the swelling is beneath the bone and there are signs that the skull is separated from all sides and water collects when you press it with your hand, and this cannot be hidden from you; then make three incisions in the middle of the head according to this method.
And after making the incision, remove all the moisture. Then tie up the incisions with strips of cloth and wool. Then apply it with wine and oil for five days.
Then untie the bandage, and care for the wound with plasters and ointments.
And thou shalt not omit to tie head with equality. Feed the sick man with all dry food of scant moisture until his limb is strengthened and healed.
Another method of incision is to consider where it appears the abscess's size is, and the collection of water.
Since sometimes it is more so in the back part or forehead, right or left.
Therefore climb with the incision where it appears to you that there is an abscess and filling of water, and cut through it as much as possible for you.
And observe that you do not cut an artery, and there be a flow of blood, and the sick person dies from the flow with evacuation of moisture.
[Section Title: Incision of Arteries After Ears]
[Chapter 2.]
When catarrhs happen to someone for the eyes or chest and it has not been treated with remedies, then more so is the last treatment in that, incision of these two arteries.
Therefore, when you wish to cut them, let the sick person shave his head first. Then scrape the place with rough cloth so that the arteries appear. Then let the sick person tie his neck with any cloth he has. Then consider where the vein beats. And the places of each are located behind the ears and depressed, and they rarely hide themselves unless in some men.
Then mark with pitch both, and cut one on each side with a scalpel, the incision reaching to the bone, and make it broad enough to match the width of the head.
And if you wish, insert a scalpel under the artery and cut it upwards with the incision.
And let the length of the incision be like two fingers joined together.
When a vein is cut, blood gushes out with pulsating flow, which jumps into the interior with frequent leap.
But if the artery is not apparent to the senses, then it is necessary that measurements be made from the ear three fingerbreadths in space. Then mark with wax and bind up to the bone.
And that which is necessary to draw from blood is VI ounces, and perhaps you will draw more or less from it. Cut the whole thing according to its size that appears to you from the strength of the weak and the filling of the artery.
Then look at the wound. If anything remains at the bone from the flesh, then cut it off, so that a hot abscess does not occur; then bind up the wound with linen strips.
Then take care of him with ointment until he is healed.
Chapter on the extraction of arteries, which are in the temples.
Chapter III.
When an old hemicrania or acute catarrh occurs due to acid moistures and heat in the temples, or an old scald, violent and similar to these; and it is treated with methods of treatment for illness, but it does not help: then we have experience in dealing with such illnesses by extracting arteries from the temples, or cauterizing them, as we have said.
And the method of operation for extracting them is to shave the sick person's hair in the temples and stretch out the skin over the appearing artery in the temple. Itself is shown to you by its pulse and is rarely hidden except in a few men or due to violent cold.
If it is hidden from you, then the sick person should bind his head with any cloth of his own; then rub the place with a rough cloth. If an abscess is present, let it be opened with hot water until a clear appearance appears to you. Then take the lancet which I previously prepared. Then scrape the skin with it easily until you reach the artery. Then thrust a hook into it and extract it upward until you extract it from the skin, and let it come out from all sides through the layers beneath it.
If, however, the artery is delicate: then roll it up with the tip of the hook. Then make an incision in that place according to its size, where the ends extend and contract, and avoid bleeding. For if it is not incised, and if it is not separated, blood will not rise up deeply.
Then let six ounces of blood out, until the third [point].
If the artery is large: then it should be tied in two places with strong double thread or silk, or with cords of alum, so that putrefaction does not approach it before the wound is consolidated, and bleeding does not occur.
Then make an incision in the excess that is between two bindings. Do this at that hour, or another hour.
And if you wish, cauterize it with a cautery until the bone, with a knife-shaped cautery, until the ends of it are cut, and it remains in place for this same operation.
And this is better work, unless if one has a fever, or weakened by heat treatment. Because the cautery is from those things that help to end moistures. Therefore it is better as a remedy.
And after the extraction of arteries, it should be filled with cooked old linen, and powdered fly-ash should be placed on top of it.
And after solution (of a wound), it is to be treated with dry medicines that cause flesh to grow, and with linen until it heals.
If during the operation, bleeding occurs from an artery, then hurry to cut it with a cauterizing iron, or fill the place with wax: and tighten your hand until the blood stops flowing. If there is nothing present (to use), then place your finger on the location until the blood freezes. And cover the location with water of intense coldness until the sharpness subsides, and tie it as necessary.
And because the artery that is lighter and easier to extract is to be cauterized with this iron having two blades: and let the sharpness of the two blades be similar to a razor's edge. However, they are much less sharp than two knives. Because if they are as sharp as two knives, coldness is required for both of them: and they do not cut flesh quickly. Since therefore they have a certain thickness, heat is required within them, and the flesh is cut quickly: when this work needs to be done, it is better than any other operation, and easier, and more convenient.
And this is the shape of the iron.
And the space between the two blades should be of the thickness of a finger, after you have marked two places with hot iron: and place both very hot ones, until they reach the bone, and cut the vein in two places: so that what is between its ends can be removed. Because this iron does not harden completely.
Chapter IV.
Chapter on the care of chronic and recurring tear ducts from the eyes.
When tears are persistent and flow from the veins on the exterior of the skull of the head: and no treatment medicine is applied to them with medicines, and the face of the sick person turns red, and one feels a walking sensation in the forehead, as with the movement of ants: and the eyes are weakened, moist, so that the hairs have already corroded with corruption: and the eyelids are heated from the acuteness of tears: then the ancients resorted to this treatment for them, and they named it the cure, with a knife.
And it is, to instruct the sick one to shave the hairs that are on his forehead. Then make three cuts in the forehead, each one equal in length to the forehead: and the length of the cut should be about two fingers, and the first one should be at the middle of the forehead, and the second one slightly lower towards the movement of the arms, and the third on the other side: and avoid cutting the arteries that are on the two sides: and extend your hand from the continuation of the two jaws, and let the space of all the cuts be the length of three connected fingers: and have a piece of prepared sponge or dried cloth with you, which you can use to absorb the blood.
Then insert into it two pointed ends of a splint whose following shape is as follows: From the incision on the side of the temple, up to the second incision: and scrape off with it all the skin that is between the two cuts, which is above the eye. Then do the same from the middle incision up to the second incision. Then remove the splint and insert into the first incision another tool called a sharp scalpel, with one edge blunt, not sharp on the other side. And this is its form.
And place the sharp side towards the skin attached flesh and the blunt side towards the bone; and push it so that it reaches the mid-fissure; and cut along with it all vessels descending from the head to the eyes, except for the incision which should be continued until that which appears from the skin.
Then make it in the mid-fissure up to another fissure.
And when an equal amount of blood flows out, squeeze the places from the clotted blood vessels.
Then place linen cloth from old cooking on all the fissures and put above them boiled chickpeas soaked in wine, oil or vinegar. And ensure that no hot abscess occurs.
And on the third day, dissolve the ligament and administer a large amount of infusion with warm water. Then treat it with ointment of Basilicon and others that heal wounds until it is healed.
Chapter 5.
Chapter on the treatment of sharp tears and catarrh in the eyes from internal parts of the head.
When someone experiences sharp and frequent catarrh or tears, the eyes appear weakened, small, and their sight is already impaired; the eyelids are ulcerated, hairs fall out and there is a strong pain deep in the head that causes sneezing: then take from these symptoms those materials and catarrh which do not come unless from multiple veins.
A better treatment for them is this. And you shall order a sick person to shave their forehead. Then make one incision in the middle of the forehead, or slightly off-center to the side by a certain width, starting from the left temple and ending at the right temple; and let the incision go as deep as the bone; and move your hand away from the temples that move during chewing until when the bone is exposed; then dry up all the blood with a sponge.
Then separate with a scalpel or scissors from the two lips of the incision, made previously with a hot iron or with linen strips. Then tie it on top with thread; and soak the thread in wine and oil to prevent a hot abscess from forming.
And when you release it and see that a hot abscess is starting to decrease, then it is necessary to break the bone, until flesh begins to grow in it.
Then treat the wound with a drying agent that promotes tissue growth; as if you were taking two parts of wheat flour and four parts of pitch, prepare an ointment from it and apply it to these wounds to promote tissue growth.
Chapter VI.
Chapter on treating a wound that affects the ear.
Every case that affects the ear falls into four categories: a mineral stone, similar to a stone such as iron and glass; or from plants like chickpeas and beans; or liquid such as water, vinegar, and similar substances; or of animal origin.
When a stone falls into the ear, or one of its kind that does not grow within the ear and cannot be added, expose only the ear; if you see a stone, then pour some oil or sesame into the ear. Then administer the extraction, and make it sneeze with powdered mixture, and apply oil in both nostrils at the onset of sneezing; when you place ear fragments in cotton or wool, stretch the ear upward.
This sentence is repeated many times [with this care].
If it does not come out, then administer the extraction with Gestifull (Pizzighelli's Subtle). Its shape is as follows.
Therefore if it comes out with Gestifull, it is good.
And if not, then administer the extraction with a small subtle hook.
If it still does not come out through that [method], then make a cannula from brass and insert the end of the cannula into the ear hole deeply; apply what is in the tip of the cannula with softened beeswax mixed with oil, so that the airway is only for the cannula; then draw it out with your strong suction.
This sentence is repeated many times [with what I have said]. If it still does not come out this way: then take some helkalimbat or water (prepared gluten), which birds are captured with; place a small amount of it on the end of a rod after you have centered the cotton properly placed over it; then insert it into the ear canal with ease, after you have straightened the ear from moisture.
If it still does not come out with everything I have said, then hurry to cut [it], before a hot abscess or spasm occurs.
The method of cutting [it] is, that the bloodletter first uses a lancet on the head; and draw out from him according to the bloodletting's strength. Then make the patient sit between your hands, turn the ear upward, and make a small incision at the base of the ear in the fatty area depressed there; let the incision be shaped like the moon until you reach the stone; then remove it with what is possible for you using your instruments.
Then from your hour, seal and care for the fissure until it heals.
If something falling into the ear is from one kind of grains that grow and swell, then administer its removal.
But if it does not obey you for extraction, then take a thin, delicate spatula in this shape.
And administer with it the removal of that kind of grain falling into the ear, and do not do this when you think that the grain is already moistened by the steam of the ear, until you place many fragments on it: then remove it with uncinus or with a delicate probe or with suction, as we said, for its extraction is relieved.
In the water that enters the ear, it is necessary for the sick person to sneeze with its nose blocked at first: and already the ear has filled up with some hot water; and there lies on top of it the ear where the water is. If therefore it comes out through that (ear canal), it is good.
And if not: then take many small, soft stones, about the length of a finger, and heat them slightly with fire; and let the sick person introduce one from these into the ear canal of his own: and he should spit on one foot from that part, and hit with another stone the stone that is in the ear. Therefore, let him not cease to do this with stones and stones until all the water comes out.
And now the water comes out so that you take with a sponge or a reed one end, and insert into the ear its other end; and heat the other end with fire until it is burned as much as possible. Then take another reed and do the same thing many times until all the water comes out; and remove it with a cannula as described above with the stone.
In the extraction of an animal entering into it (the wound), if it is a small body such as a louse, care for it as I said in division.
If it is of a large body, which appears to the sense: then administer its extraction with tweezers and unciform instruments; and its removal is easier for all who are held in the ear.
In the extraction of a worm generated in the ear, when you care for it with what I said in division and in the treatment of distillations, and your care does not help: then it is necessary that you look at the ear in sunlight. If therefore something appears from the worms (there), then extract it with tweezers or with delicate unciform instruments.
If however nothing appears from there, then take a cannula, of which this is the shape (described as), narrow at the bottom and wide at the top; and insert its fine end into the ear according to the quantity that the weak one can tolerate; then suck it with strong suction. Do this repeatedly until all the worms come out.
If they do not obey you to go out, then encircle them with the point of a cannula with wax, as I said in the stone (chapter).
If they do not come out with what I said, then administer the distillations that have already been experienced by the ancients in the elimination of worms; and you will find this in the treatment of distillations.
And let your flow (of oil or medicine) be which you pour into the ear with this instrument, whose shape is depicted here. As you see, make it from silver or bronze, narrow below, in which there is a small opening, wide above.
Therefore let the thing that pushes (in the concave part of the cannula) be made of bronze well-made. And if you wish, take radish, and insert it into the affected ear with a suitable lining; then pour oil, or vinegar, or whatever medicine you prefer into the tube; and let it be in the ear; then introduce the heated radish onto the top of it, and press it gently with your hand until the oil is pushed out into the hollow part of the ear, and the sick person feels it; and what is poured into the ear should already be slightly warm; beware that nothing cold which distills into it is very strong; for medicine does not tolerate this.
Chapter VII.
On the treatment of an obstruction in the Ear.
Sometimes infants are born from their mothers' unperforated ears.
And it also happens that the obstruction of the ear arises from a wound or flesh born therein.
And this obstruction sometimes occurs deep within the ear canal, which cannot be seen; and sometimes it occurs in the outer part of the ear canal, and it can be seen.
Therefore, that which occurs deep within the ear, which cannot be seen by sight, is difficult to cure in many cases.
And in that which can be seen by sight, it is necessary to place the sick person's ear on the sun and look into it; then if you see an obstruction appearing, open it with a thin spatula whose shape is as follows: its end should have a small notch, whose part should be sharp; and the rest of the spatula should be soft on both sides so as not to hurt the ear.
If the obstruction is born from flesh within the ear, then hold it with a thin hook and cut it out with great force until all the flesh is removed.
If there is an incision in the depth of the ear: then take fine copper wire, linen, and heat it slightly; then insert it into the wound of the ear.
If you find an incision accompanied by illness and hearing loss, attempt its opening with ease; be careful not to wound the nerves of the ear.
Then place linen in the ear according to the size of the opening that you have closed with an Egyptian ointment; do this for several days until you are confident about the healing of the wound.
Or take linen, immerse it in rose water, sprinkle on it ground zinc and use it.
If you see the ear beginning to abscess: then you must remove the linen and let it drain with another piece of linen that has been soaked in a cerate made with rose oil, until the warm abscess settles; then take care of it until it heals.
If there is bleeding: then immerse a sponge or cloth in cold water and place it over the ear; use the rest of the treatment that was mentioned in the section on distillations to stop the blood flow.
Chapter on Althele's treatment for eyelids.
Chapter VIII.
These are the Althelil (affections) that happen in the eyelids of the eyes, which are sometimes moist and sometimes dry.
Therefore, it is necessary to hold them with tweezers (or with a hook), and cut them at their roots with a spatula. Then place it on the affected area crushed.
If blood flows out of them (the affections), then cauterize them with a fine lenticular cautery.
And it is better to cauterize them after the incision. They often return when there remains something of their roots. And when they are cauterized with fire, those roots burn and do not return.
§ On the treatment of tumors on the eyelids of the eyes.
Chapter IX.
Often something happens in the eyelids that resembles a tumor in its strength and hardness, and it is called Grandino because of this; it is an accumulation of thick moisture on the upper eyelid and lower eyelid.
Therefore, the operation in them is to examine whether it is a Grandino that is coming out of the eyelid, which appears on the eyelid and moves to all parts, and its nature is easy.
Therefore, make an incision across it (the tumor). Then scrape off all parts of it with ease until it comes out. Then hold it (the scraped part) with a hook and cut it.
If its removal is not prepared for you unless after you make a small incision through the eyelid, then it harms weak people.
If the incision is large: then gather it (the scraped part) with suture; and treat it until it heals.
And if it is small, no harm will come to you from it. Ointment indeed restores it, and fleshes it out.
If the grain is turned towards the inner parts of the ear and it faces the internal surface, then turn the eyelid and hang the grain with a hook; besides, you will need an incision, and press it from all sides.
If the eyelid is stretched by an incision, it does not harm anything.
Then clean the eye after the incision of the grain with salt water; and care for the place with it until the weak one is healed.
Chapter on the treatment of the eyelids.
Chapter X.
The Axirnath is a pimple that is generated in the upper eyelid; it indeed mostly happens to children; and it weighs their eyes down, and cataracts occur to them in the mornings, and they are unable to see the light of the sun, for this reason, because tears flow towards them, and you can see them constantly lying on their faces, and sleeping on them, and their eyelids are below the eyebrows, which have already swollen; and indeed the swelling of Axirnath is noticeable to the eye, and when you press the place with your fingers, you feel it among them.
And the method of operation for it is that the weak one puts his head in your lap.
Then take a linen cloth, and prepare a piece of it, and make a circle out of the cloth according to the size that contains the Axirnath from all sides. Then put it on it and press it with your fingers from all sides, so that the Axirnath is gathered in the middle of the circle.
Then find in the middle of this moistness with a small incision and not a larger one than that which is made in phlebotomy at depth.
It is necessary that you find the entire skin until you reach Axirnath, for in many arrangements does Axirnath proceed from the fissure according to the shape of a white plum-stone.
Extract it with a cloth, which you have soaked between your fingers for the outside parts; and you turn your hand to the right and left until it is dispersed; and beware, lest you add in the fissure, so as not to reach with the spatula to the eye, and harm it.
If Axirnath does not appear to you at the beginning of the fissure, you add a little in the fissure with ease, until Axirnath comes out. Then extract it as we have said.
Then immerse the cloths in vinegar and water, and place them over the place, and bind it with small stones.
And among men are those who grind salt and place it in the hollow of the fissure, so that it melts what remains from that moisture.
Then take care of it until it heals.
If, however, a hot abscess occurs in the place, then treat it with soothing plasters until it heals.
Chapter on Ataxmir of the eye: that is, when the eyelid becomes softened, so that it weeps as it should not.
Chapter XI.
When hairs grow in the eyelids beyond the course of natural hairs and turn white: then they harm the eye, and cause diseases such as continuous tearing, softening of the eyelids, and clouding, until it leads to the cause of the destruction of the eye.
And Ataxmir of the eye is cured according to four modes. Or by cautery with fire. With sharp medicine, as stated in the chapter on cautery. Ataxmir is cured by incision and suturing. By means of reeds, as I shall say.
Place the head of the sick man on your chest. Then turn the eyelid of the eye with your left hand.
If it therefore turns, it is good. And if it does not [turn]: insert a needle into it where there is a thread from the lower part of the eyelid, and let the needle penetrate with the thread above, and let it be near the hairs themselves, that is, near the edge of the eyelid, where the hairs grow: and pull the thread towards the upper part with the eyelid, and turn it with a flat instrument.
Then find in the inner part of the eyelid under the added hairs with a spatula slipping from the greater lacrimal to the lesser lacrimal.
Then pull out the thread, and place under the eyelid a small fleck of cooked wheat or cloth: then mark on the eyelid with a signet using encaustic, as in the figure of a myrtle leaf.
However, it is necessary that the figure be made according to the size and elevation of the eyelid: because it is diversified in men.
For there are those who need to be cut from the eyelid according to its large size, according to its softening part.
Then with the spatula find on top of the two lines that you have marked, and start from the greater lacrimal to the lesser lacrimal, and let there be one crack near the natural hairs, as in a swelling of the radius.
Then insert the hook into one of the two corners of the skin. Then scrape it all off. Then gather with suturing the two eyelids, with a sharp needle and fine woolen thread: and remove blood, and let that which superfluous exudes from the threads above the eyebrows adhere, if you wish to do so: and if not, do not treat it.
Then release the suture and the thread for three or four days; afterward care for it.
And if you wish, release the wound without suture, and take care of it, so that it dries up and contracts. For the eyelid is to be raised during the sealing of the wound and its closure; but it will be better later on.
This method of treatment was taught by Ataxmir the ancients.
However, there is concern over the patient in this case, and it comes from a good surgery, not fear.
And there is another method in Ataxmir as well: and it is to make marks on the eyelid, like the shape of a myrtle leaf, as we have told before.
Then raise the eyelid with three separated or joined combs, following this shape, then cut off what is excessive with small scissors, according to this shape, with evenness of the cut.
If it is not possible for you to hold the comb and it does not match, then take a needle with thread, and insert it in the middle of the figure; and insert another thread near the greater tear duct, and another thread near the smaller tear duct; and tie the threads evenly between your fingers.
Then raise your hand with an equal elevation; and raise the skin where it is marked, as we have told before.
Then bring together the two lips of the wound with suture; and care for it until it heals.
If, however, a boil occurs at your incision or your tear, but it is filled with pus; apply that boil with cerate and similar substances, from soothing ointments.
And sometimes the eyelashes may also turn inside out.
Therefore, you should use what we have said in the incision; but suturing is more artificial for both. On treating Ataxmir with dogs.
And turn the eyelid, and cut the fissure that is inside, as I have described. Then make two dog's jaws or two thin sticks, whose length should be according to the length of the eyelid, and their width should be smaller than the width of a spindle; and you have already cut at both ends where you hold the threads.
Then attach each of them to that which projects from the eyelid of the eye and tie the two dog's jaws together tightly on both sides with a strong ligature, and leave it for some days. For the tightened skin will die, become black, and rot until it falls off by itself.
If it slows down (healing), then cut it with scissors. Then take care of it until it is healed.
When it has consolidated (healed), lift the eyelid and do not pluck the hairs.
And this is the shape of two dog's jaws that you should make according to this form and size (dimensions).
Chapter 12.
On plucking out hairs in the eye with a needle.
The operation is to take a fine needle and insert a thread from fine silk into it gently. Then join the ends of the thread and tie both with a very fine knot; let the length of the threads be one palm.
Then prepare another thin thread called Alinxotat under it and tie its ends if you wish.
Then place the patient's head in your lap and bring it close to the sun so that the operation may be seen clearly; because this is a delicate or small operation.
Then insert the needle with Alinxotat into the root of the eyelid and make it penetrate quickly into the eyelid until you pull out the natural hair from above.
Then draw out the needle above the anulixotatus (a type of wound or abscess): and insert the needle into the anulixotatus, if it is one, two, or three, not more than that.
Then draw your hand with it until the needle along with the anulixotatus comes out of the eye with its natural hair.
If the anulixotatus is being pulled out and the needle does not come out with it: draw the anulixotatus downwards, with the thread you have made in it, until the anulixotatus comes out through the upper opening, and you see it with the eye: then draw out the anulixotatus and the thread; extract both, and close the eye; and leave it closed for two or three days until the hair adheres to its place, and flesh grows over it.
If the hair is short, then attach a long hair from the natural hairs to it and draw it out with that: or leave it until it grows out on its own, and then draw it out.
Chapter 13.
When this ulcer happens to the eye, it is called "Leporina".
This ulcer is either natural or acquired.
The acquired ulcer occurs from the consolidation of a wound, or an incision, or a cautery, and similar things.
The method of treatment is to open the consolidation, separate its lips, and place a linen cloth between them, and tie it until it heals.
It is not necessary to use in the treatment of this ulcer things that dry and constrict, for if you do that, the ulcer worsens rather than improves; instead, use things that soften, such as fenugreek; embrocation with water, in which althea has been cooked, mixed with flax seed; unguent of dyaquilon, which has been melted with some oil; and wrap it with linen and treat it with that.
Your treasure of care is to strive with all your ability, so that it does not become consolidated according to the original form.
This indeed is not other than a correction of X-ration, so that the shape of the place does not return as it was entirely.
Section on the care of X-ration in the lower eyelid, and it is a roughening or contraction upward to the right and left.
Chapter XIV.
This that is below, is what is truly named X-ration. It is natural and it is accidental.
And the accidental one arises from a wound, or a fissure, or cautery, and similar things.
The way of operation in it is to take the point, which has a double thread, and to anoint it with flesh, and to make it penetrate from the left tear-duct to the right tear-duct, until the thread reaches both ends of the skin.
Then stretch the skin with the point upward, and cut it with a broad knife. If therefore the shape of the eyelid returns as it should be, it is good.
And if not, take the rod, and place it in the fissure, and turn the eyelid with it: and cut two fissures on the inside of the eyelid, and let their ends be at the corners of the incision, until they converge and form an angle: until when gathered together this shape is formed, and it is the letter lauda graeca.
Then remove that skin by the amount of its sharp lower part, from the one following the eyelid. Then gather the separated parts: or it with a thread of wool.
Then care for them with what we said, with softening medicines and bandages, until they heal.
If the alxahtrati occurs from a split, either by suture or cautery: then it is necessary that you explore the split flat beneath the eyelashes, as was previously done. Then separate between two lips with a linen cloth, as we said before.
In summary, the treatment of alxahtrati, whether it is above or below, consists of treating it according to the procedure prepared for the shape of alxahtrati.
Indeed, it has many diverse forms; the skilled artisan prepares his ability in any way possible to him, so that he may return the figure to its natural form or as close to it as possible, and the patient himself, according to what suits him from the operation and instruments in various arrangements.
Chapter XV.
Chapter on the adhesion of the eyelid with the conjunctiva, or cornea.
When this consolidation happens to many people, so that the upper eyelid adheres to the white of the eye and prevents it from performing its natural functions.
Therefore, one must insert the end of the rod under the eyelid and lift it up; or extend it with a hook; then cut the adhesion with a thin spatula, not with the sharpness of the spatula's cuts but blunted slightly; so that the patient is not disturbed during the operation and the spatula is removed without causing damage to the eye by its sharpness; and your incision should be as if you are scraping off the adhesion easily, until when the eyelid returns to its natural form and the adhesion heals completely.
Then pour salt water into the eye and wash it; or let it drip onto him from a syringe made of sheep's horn with water dissolved in wine.
Separate a linen strip between the eyelid and the eye. Place wool soaked in egg white on the eye. Use it three days later, or with solid ointments until it heals.
On the incision of the nail and swelling of the skin around the eyes.
Chapter XVI.
Know that the nail has two ways. Either it is horny: and it is like the hide of a deer, soft and brittle. Or it is not horny, similar to frozen milk-white moisture: which, when touched with iron or attempted to be grasped with a nail, is severed and the nail does not bite into it.
And both types do not start until from the greater tear duct, until it gradually penetrates the vision, and prevents light, and the movement of the eye.
And the method of operation for its incision is: that the sick person places his head in your lap. Then open the eyes of the sick person with your hand and lift the eyelid. Then gather the nail with a small nail few times and extend it upward. Then take the awl and insert a horse's or cow's hair, or that of a sheep, into it: let it be threaded and double the point of the awl slightly, and pierce it in the middle of the nail: and penetrate with the awl and tie the nail with the thread and extend it upward: and remove the hair from the side of the nail following the pupil, as if you are pulling it with the hair to the end of its.
Then cut the remaining part at the root of the lacrimal bone with a fine spatula or with small forceps; and let the natural flesh of the lacrimal pass without it happening that, due to the incision, there is a constant flow of tears.
And sometimes, the nail extends with the only tweezers; or with thread, as I said. Then scrape it with a soft spatula, whose form is this.
And take care that the soft spatula does not touch the horny layer and there occurs a break there and the pupil is pierced.
Then after the incision, throw into the eye something of ground salt or made from wax and linen, and let it remain until another day. Then care for it with what is necessary, until it heals.
If the nail is not sensitive and you cannot insert a needle into it nor does the tweezers fit into it, then this type of nail should be treated frequently with medicines, and it heals as I told in the division.
If you want to cut it, then open the eye of the sick person, and take a fine, soft, delicate, blunt spatula in this form. And smooth the nail above with a rasp, with subtlety. If you see that it hardens and breaks and the rasp imprints on it, then pour from your hour into the eye a solution made of wax and linen or red wax or finely ground salt; and let it be closed until another day.
Then repeat the above procedure until the entire thing is removed. Unless it is a warm abscess in your eye; then let the former go and care for the abscess until it heals.
Then repeat the procedure on it with the rasp, until it heals.
Prominence of the lacrimal flesh, if it harms the eye greatly, should be suspended with a hook and a portion of it should be cut off; not at the end, to prevent the flow of tears.
Then let blood from the lacrimal or red, or made from zinjarium, until it is healed. (Lacrimal: tear duct; Zinjarium: probably a type of copper vessel used for leeches or cupping)
Chapter on the incision of Alguardenic and flesh born in the eye. (Alguardenic is not found in any known medical texts, possibly a mis-spelling or error)
Chapter XVII.
A red flesh composed or laid over in some human eyes is sometimes born, which covers the pupil or approaches it, or presses on the eyelids and possibly turns the eyelids outwards; resembling a rosebush.
And the operation for this is also that the sick person should place his head on your chest. (Inferius means chest or breast) Then open the eyes of that person and collect all that flesh with suitable hooks; hold it with a single forceps or tweezers. (Collige = collect)
Then cut the flesh first, until its entirety is finished with a scalpel. (incisorio = knife or scalpel) And beware of the eye so as not to harm it during the operation; and make your cut such that you cut it, or with a spatula (spatulam), which we mentioned in the incision of the nail; or with small forceps, with which the flesh is collected, according to what its form will be after this chapter. (Asebel: probably a tool used for collecting tissue during surgery)
When your cut is completed and all of the Alguardenic is removed, then fill the eye with salt water; or drizzle red powder on it, and similar substances from corrosive medicines; and place a piece of cotton with egg white over the outside of the eye to protect it from hot infection. (Apostemate calido: hot inflammation)
If anything remains from the cautery and warm blood governs you, and you fear a hot abscess; then let the eye be, and treat the same along with what will calm the abscess.
Then again upon it with an operation until it heals.
And similarly do with the added flesh that occurs in the eye of this kind.
Nevertheless, it is necessary that any treatment of the weak eye, either by natural or accidental way, be performed with iron; and do not insert your hand into any of these operations until you see that the limb can tolerate this operation.
Chapter on removing a seed from the eye.
Chapter XVIII.
The red veins that weave over the eye, preventing the vision from operating; and they weaken the eye with the passing of days.
Therefore, it is necessary for you first to determine if the eye in which there is a seed (Sebel), is strong and there is no other illness besides the Sebel; then collect the Sebel from that eye.
And it is to command the weak one (patient) to place his head in your lap.
Then suspend the veins with a single or double hook according to your discretion; and let the hook be fine, doubled, in this shape, or there be two hooks graduated in one body, in this shape.
Then collect the veins with fine forceps and remove the blood by the hour; until you see that the veins are removed from the eye and resolved; and be careful not to injure the eye with the tips of the forceps.
Let your operation be in the middle of the day before the sun, and be very firm in your operation; so as not to injure except the veins.
And when you have finished, then pour into the eye either green or red; so that its acidity corrodes what remains from the Sebel.
If it is not possible for you to collect the whole thing within that hour, then pack the eye with something that alleviates eye pain; and leave it for some days until the pain subsides; and secure it from infection with warm poultice; afterwards, repeat over it in the same manner until it heals.
And this is the form of forceps.
Chapter on reducing a nose to the mouth.
Chapter XIX.
Physicians call the fistula known as Arissat, which you treat with a cautery or with an acidic medicine burning it, according to what has been previously stated about its treatment.
And if it does not heal, then there is no skill in that; unless to look for an abscess near its birthplace, and extract all the moisture and pus that is in it until the bone appears.
When the bone appears, and you see corruption or blackening in it, then grind it with an instrument of this form.
It is called the head of a rasp.
Make it from iron, and let its head be round like a rasp, with points made by a file, or by the more subtle point of an alisclifers; and place it over the corrupted bone.
Then turn it with your fingers and press your hand slightly, until you know that the corruption is now ground away; and do this several times.
Then restore the place with the most powerful ointments of styptics.
If the place consolidates, and flesh grows in it, and the flow of pus ceases; and it remains for forty days without being renewed, or infected, or any accident happening to it; then you will know that it is healed.
And if not, there is no skill in that, except to reduce the fistula to the nostril opening, according to this form.
And it is as follows for you to expose the second bone with iron, or with sharp medicine: and when the bone is detected, then take the trepan in this shape, having its end iron and triangular: and the wood of it is a pyramid extended up to the end, just as you see.
Then place that upon the very bone itself: and let it be near the tear duct: and extend your hand slightly away from the eye. Then turn your hand with the trepan until it penetrates the bone and feels weak; by this you will know that wind is escaping from it, when you hold your hand over its nose.
Therefore then, restore the place with medicines drying, as I have taught you.
When therefore flesh is born and the place becomes hard; then the matter that was flowing outward returns to the nose; therefore it is easier for that over the weak.
Section on Reducing Swelling of the Eye.
Chapter XX.
When the eye protrudes completely and neither sight is damaged nor decreased; then it is necessary to dissolve the weakened part. Then phlebotome it. Afterward place poultices on the neck without scarification, but with suction.
Then place over the eye a liniment made of acacia, aloes, frankincense, and sarcolax. Then squeeze the eyelid shut with many plasters.
And the method of plasters is to take soft cloths, many, and fold each piece over four; make many from them. Then place one on top of another, according to how much the eye needs; then squeeze them with a stiff cloth firmly on top.
Repeat poultices with suction without scarification.
Then remove the windy (afflicted), and let the squinting eye rest day and night.
If the ligament becomes soft again, then it must be tightened much more: Then remove the ligament after a day and night, as we said.
If you see that the eye has returned to its original sheathing, this is good: and if not, then apply plasters, leeches, tightening (of the eyelid), and windy (afflicted), until it heals.
Chapter on Incision of the Sheathing.
Chapter XXI.
When there is a rupture in the sheathing of the eye, it then comes out and protrudes beyond the eyelids like a grain of sand, and defiles the human form due to this, and one wishes to cut it: then the operation is done according to what I have said: and it is to introduce a needle at the root of the sheathing from below to above.
Then insert another needle where there is a double thread from the lacrimal part, and make it penetrate: and let the first needle go according to its placement.
Then cut the place of the double thread, and tie it with the sheathing in a circle around the needle: and tighten it much.
Then pull out the needle, and place wool soaked in oil over the eye on the white of the eye: and let it remain until the thread comes out with the sheathing.
Then care for the eye so that it is comforted until the wound heals.
And sometimes the sheathing is tightened from all sides with a circle made of cloth until the eye protrudes considerably.
Then it is pierced with a fine spatula that reaches to the depth of the eye, and moisture is spread on the white of the eye, and the eye falls down and enters immediately: then tighten it until it heals.
Treatment of the Alcomnat.
Chapter XXII.
This sickness called Alcomnat is nothing but pus that gathers in the eye, similar to descending water, and it itself is not [the eye].
And the method of operation in this [case] is that you make the patient sit on a prepared chair or straight.
Then take the head of [the patient] with both your hands at two sides and move it until you see the pus go down to the lower part of the eyes. Then it is to be shaped [the pus] and not allowed to go down, and the eye should be opened: let the patient see as he saw before: and if it does not go down below, know that it is water.
If [the pus] does not come out as described, then make the patient sit between your hands. Then take a fine probe and cut through it on the horny fold at the junction of the conjunctiva with the corneal layer in the corona until the pus comes out.
When it comes out [the pus], then pour hot water into the eye in which you have mixed honey or warm water in which you already boiled fenugreek and honey: then treat the rest with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
Chapter on the care of water that descends into the eye or cataract.
Chapter XXIII.
We have already said the types of water and which one is suitable for piercing according to the discussion and explanation: then take that same one in accordance with health.
Then you should make the patient sit between your hands, facing the light and close to the sun: then tie the healthy eye shut and squeeze it very hard: then with your right hand close the left eyelid if the water is in the left eye or the left hand if the water is in the right eye.
Then take your right hand, if the eye is left: or take your left hand, if the eye is right.
Then place the tip of your right hand near the crown on the surface of the white part of the eye visible by the smaller lacrimal duct: then push your right hand with force and you turn it while moving, until it penetrates into the white part of the eye; and feel that the instrument has reached the empty space.
It is necessary that there be a measure of the journey of the instrument into depth, the space from the pupil to the end of the dark part; and this is the border of the eye. You will see it there in the very pupil of the eye because of the clarity of the cornea tissue.
Then place the instrument until it reaches the place where the water is located. Then press it down once after another.
If the water descends immediately, then the blind man sees immediately what is above him and the instrument in his eye.
Then rest for a little while. If the water descends, then remove it and let the instrument come out.
When it is fastened and does not rise up: then remove the instrument with ease; and you turn your hand gradually.
Then dissolve something from salt in water, like a clear gemstone; and clean the eye with it inside. Then place over the entire eye a swab of wool soaked in rose oil and white linen; and tie it with the healthy eye.
We and those who are of our time place over him camphor powder mixed with white linen on the eye.
If the instrument does not obey you to enter the eye due to its hardness, because it is from a man whose eye is very hard: then it is necessary that you take a spatula called "Alberid", and this is its shape:
Pierce therefore only the joint itself, and not the ultimate end of the hand into the opening; it is only so that you make a way to a subtle place.
Insert almagda as previously mentioned.
Prepare for the completion of your work, a well-made sleeping chamber should be prepared for the sick man, where he can sleep on his back in a dark room; let him be prevented from all movements and coughing; and place food for him that soothes his nature; and do not move his head to either side at all.
Let the bandage be according to its arrangement until the third day.
Then dissolve it in that dark room and test his sight; make him see things. Then lead the bandage until the seventh day.
It is not necessary that he do it at the hour of healing or immediately after incision; on the contrary, let someone else do it because water rises quickly through an intense gaze.
If, however, there is a hot abscess: then it is necessary that you dissolve the eye before the seventh day; and correct it with what calms the abscess until it is calm; then remove his sight from him, and place over his oral cavity what regulates his vision for several days, he being in that dark room.
Then gradually leave the house and convert to his own beds.
And know that a student is not often excused from watching; then he dares to perform an operation.
Now indeed a certain one of them who are from Alayrach has come to us, who said that a large perforation was made in Alayrach for drawing water.
Therefore, I have not seen anyone in your land who has done it; nor have I read it in any of the ancient books; and it is possible that it is new.
These are the forms of shapes from a handle, so that it stands upon one who does not know it.
Make them from copper: and let their extremities be with the same subtlety of triangular shape, and their extremity sharp.
Chapter XXIII.
Treatment for newborn flesh in the nose.
Sometimes are born in the nose various fleshes similar to many-footed scorpions: and from it is a cancerous flesh, stoney, dark colored; and from it is a soft flesh, not dark colored.
Therefore, for that soft flesh which is not fraudulent nor cancerous, you must make the weak one sit opposite the sun with his face between your hands, and open his nose, and throw the hook into those fleshes; then draw them out towards the outside, and cut what you have caught with a thin spatula sharp at one end, until you know that all the flesh has been removed.
If something remains from that which the removal is not possible: then scrape it with one of the fine instruments until there remains nothing of it. If blood dominates you or a hot abscess happens: then oppose it as required; or it is from malignant abscesses, then hurry to cauterize him until the blood is separated and all fleshes are removed.
Then throw into the nose after the cut vinegar, water or wine. If the nose opens and liquid comes out to the palate, then you know that he is already well.
If the liquid does not penetrate as required, then you know that there is newborn flesh within the bones of the nose, which did not reach with the cut.
Then it is necessary that you insert a thickened thread of linen with many knots; and place between every knot an amount equal to a digit or less; and have the weak one, so that he sends forth one end of the thread into the nose with a radish, or as possible for him after he has made it similar to a syringe; and draw out the smell until it reaches the cavity, and exit above his throat.
And indeed many times this is done like Attomus' boy in schools; and it is easy for him who wants to do so.
Then place two ends of the thread, one that exits above the nose, and the other that remains in the nose. Then as an assistant you tie flesh with the knots on the thread. Make this until you know that the flesh is already with the knots of the thread.
Then remove the thread; and place linen which you have soaked in Egyptian ointment inside the nose after the blood has been drained; do this for three days or more until the ointment has completely eaten away what remains of the flesh.
Then place a lead tube at the end of the matter into the nose for some days until it heals.
If it requires treatment to dry it out, use that.
For the nose purge, when olive oil and other medications are distilled into the nose, make it of silver or copper; it should be similar to a small lamp, open like a snail shell; and its passage likewise.
And if you wish to make a closed tube, like a cane.
And the snail shell instrument for nose purge should be full, pierced; which has a handle at its end, with which you hold it, when you heat oil or what you wish from juices and fluid substances in it.
Chapter XXV.
Multotiens nascitur in extremitate nasi Thelul, et magnificatur, et augmentatur cum diebus, donec foedus fit aspectus eius translates to: "Thelul often appears at the end of the nose and grows and becomes more prominent with days until its appearance becomes disgusting.
"And on account of this, it is necessary to cut it at the beginning of its appearance and to remove all of it. "Then place over that spot, either a cautery or a medicine burning in its place.
"If cutting it does not cause it to disappear before it becomes prominent, then examine if it is hard, dark colored and has few sensations; in this case do not touch it with iron because it is a cancerous ulcer.
"For often I have seen that someone cut an apothema and great harm came to the one who had it.
"If the apothema is soft to touch, not dark colored and it appears that cutting it can be performed on its entirety, then evacuate the weak part of it and cut it without fear, without dread; and care for the place with it so that it drains and constricts until it heals.
"Chapter XXVI.
"On suture of the nose, and lip, and ear.
"Know that when discontinuity of one of these cartilages occurs, the operation does not help much unless in certain men.
"Therefore when something happens to anyone from that, you should examine if it is a recent wound with its blood; in this case apply double the size of the wound with stitches; then take care of it until it heals.
"And if the discontinuity of the lips has already separated and each part is healthy; then it is necessary to remove all parts appearing from the skin until it bleeds. "Then attach the two lips with stitches and bind them, and sprinkle over it powder of dragon's blood and pulverized olibanum; and put on top of powders a fragment of consolidated emplaster such as diafinicon or another stronger emplaster; and leave it bound for two days or three. Then dissolve it, and change the medicine; and let it go until the threads separate by themselves. Then treat it with an ointment until it heals.
The method of suturing is to gather the solution of continuity with needles, as we have said in the surgery of the abdomen; or gather the solution with thread, as I have told you.
Chapter XXVII.
Chapter on the extraction of lip nodes.
Many men suffer from ulcers similar to hard grains of wheat in the internal parts of their lips, and some of them are smaller, and others are larger.
Therefore, one must turn the lip, and search for every knot of it, and hang it up with a hook, and cut it from all sides.
Then fill the place after the incision with fine sediment until the blood is separated.
Then it is to be anointed with vinegar, and the place where there is the obstruction is to be rubbed with it until the wounds are healed.
Chapter XXVIII.
§ On the incision of a child's flesh on the gum.
Often, a piece of flesh grows over the gum, which the ancients called abscess.
Therefore, it must be hung up with a hook, or held with forceps and cut at the root, and allow the pus or blood to flow out.
Then place fine sediment or other powdered purgatives on the place.
If that piece of flesh returns after treatment, which often happens, then it should be cut a second time and cauterized; for it does not return after cauterization.
Chapter XXIX.
§ On the scraping of teeth with iron.
When they accumulate on the surfaces of Teeth from both interior and exterior parts, between gums and rough cortices, and sometimes turn yellow or green, until corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth become foul through it.
Therefore, one should make the sick person sit between your hands and lean his head in your lap, and file the pulp and tooth, where you see the cortex, until nothing remains of it, and similarly do for blackening, greenness, yellowing, and others until they are cleaned.
If what is inside them is removed at the beginning of the reasoning, it is good; and if not, then apply the filing on them day by day, second, and third, until finally the effort reaches what you desire.
And know that the tooth requires rasors of various shapes and forms, many figures; according to which it is prepared for your operation; because the rasp used to file the tooth from below is different from the rasp used to file between the teeth, due to their other shapes.
And these shapes of rasors should be prepared by you, which you see.
Chapter XXX.
Chapter on the extraction of tooth pain.
One should cure the Tooth from its pain with all skill and be patient in extracting it. For there is no replacement for it when it is extracted; since it is a substance raised up; until there is no excuse for extracting it, then one who is sick must extract it himself, to strengthen and assure you that the tooth in pain is extracted.
For many times pain deceives the sick man and believes that it is in the tooth and extracts it himself; then the pain does not subside until the sick tooth is extracted.
We have already seen that from the operation of phlebotomists.
When it is confirmed to you that the toothache himself is sworn, then it is necessary that you scarify around the tooth with a spatula, in which there should be something of virtue, until it dissolves the gums from all sides: afterwards move it yourself with your fingers, or with subtle forceps in the first place gradually, until you shake it.
Then place large forceps there at a good position, and hold the head of the weak one between your knees: what you have already tightly held, so that it does not move: then pull the tooth in a straight line, so as not to break it.
If it does not come out, then take one of those instruments and insert it under it from all sides with ease, and try to move it as you did at first.
If the tooth is perforated or corroded: then it is necessary that you fill that hole with a cloth and tie it with the end of a subtle radius so as not to break it during your constriction with forceps.
And you must be careful when making the scarification around the gums from all sides.
And keep your strength so as not to break it and a part remains and returns over the weak one from that greater pain which was first there.
And be careful not to do what unknowing phlebotomists do in haste and the arrogance of their own removal of it, apart from what we have said.
Many times they make great infirmities come upon people, which are more difficult to break and all the roots remain, or some of them: or they pull it out with certain bones of the jaw: as we have often testified.
Then it is to be washed after its removal with wine, or with vinegar and salt.
If there happens to be a bleeding from the places (for it often happens), then rub something from pigeon-shite and fill that place with it; and if not, cauterize it yourself if you do not have pigeon-shite.
The handles of delicate forceps with which the tooth is moved should be long at the ends, short at the handle, thick so that they do not split when pressed upon the tooth; as you can see, the thick parts of the handles, until when you close them, they do not bite themselves, or split: short in length, and made of iron from India, or skillfully fashioned flatiron with sharp ends: and at their ends should be teeth, some of which enter into certain ones and tighten by a suitable constriction, strong.
And sometimes the ends are shaped like the beak of a bird which is called stork, and they are strong in constriction.
Chapter XXXI.
Chapter on the Extraction of Teeth and Removal of Broken Bones of the Jaw.
When something remains after the extraction of a tooth that breaks apart, then it is necessary to place hot iron with butter for one or two days until the location becomes soft; then introduce alum or forceps into it whose ends are similar to the beak of a bird which is called stork. The form of this forceps is:
Extremities should be made as flat as a file or as an aliskilfegi.
If it does not obey you with these forceps, then it is necessary to cauterize over the root, and to undermine the whole flesh, and introduce a tool called small Palanca, whose shape is as follows.
Make the end short, slightly thicker; do not saturate it so that it does not break.
If the root comes out through that [opening], it is good; if not, help with these other instruments whose shapes are as follows.
The shape of the first is a triangle, in which there is a certain thickness.
The shape of the subtle triangle.
And with other instruments and tools like the toothpick.
Also help with this tool similar to a large nail, whose shape is that of a twisted triangle with some thickness so as not to break, and do not saturate it.
And know that there are many toothpick-like tools; and similarly the rest of the instruments are not counted, and the wise artisan, skilled in his art, finds himself an instrument according to which the operation and the illnesses signify to him.
Because from diseases there are those for which the ancients did not provide an instrument, due to the diversity of their species.
If the bone is broken from the jaw or other bones of the mouth, or it rots; then examine over it in its place with that which suits it from instruments and forceps I have mentioned for root extraction, and help with geste, whose shape is as follows.
Let there be some thickness gradually, so that the bone can be tightened or held with it, and not flee or move away, until the bone comes out; and restore the place with appropriate medicines for it.
If however there is a small putridity in the bone, then scrape it from its putridity and care for it until it heals.
Chapter 32.
On locking the protruding teeth over others.
When teeth emerge not according to their natural course, the shape becomes foul, and particularly when this happens in women and girls, that is, in those who menstruate.
Therefore, you must consider. If a tooth is born after another tooth and does not settle, or its removal or grinding is not possible, then uproot it. And if it is attached to another tooth, then cut it with this instrument, whose shape is as follows:
It resembles a small beak and is made of hard iron, with an extremely sharp tip.
Make your cut several days later, and because of the hardness of the tooth, so as not to disturb another tooth.
If it is projecting, exposed for grinding: then grind it with a file made of iron, whose shape is as follows:
Let it be made entirely of iron, and the handle small with many sharp points, like a file with which needles are filed: with which you grind the tooth gradually over several days with ease, so as not to disturb another tooth and let it fall; then soften it, and finally sand it with certain rasps.
If the tooth breaks off from which part of the tongue is injured: then it must be ground until the roughness of the fracture is removed and smoothed out; and it should not injure the tongue nor distort speech.
Chapter XXXIII.
Chapter on drilling teeth with gold threads.
When there is shock and disturbance of the front teeth due to blow or accident, and the weak person cannot hold what he eats so that it does not fall out; and you have treated them with medicines for swelling, but the treatment has not helped: then it is appropriate to string them with a gold thread. Because silver becomes green and rots after days, but gold never changes.
And let there be a thread of medium thickness and coarseness according to its quantity, which can pass between the Teeth.
The shape of the reel is such that you take the thread and insert its double between two healthy teeth; then you weave it with its two ends between the moving teeth (whether one or more), until you reach with the needle to the healthy tooth on the other side. Then repeat the weaving until you reach the part from which you started; and tighten your hand with subtlety and wisdom until it is completely removed; and let your constriction, which you use to tighten the thread, be at the roots of the teeth so that it does not slip out.
Then cut the excess parts of the thread with scissors; and tie both ends together and twist them; and hide these within the healthy tooth and the moving tooth so as not to harm the tongue; then release the tightened part only when it remains so.
If it is loosened or cut, tighten them with another thread, and it will remain in that state for the entire time.
And this is the form of teeth, and the figure of the reel of two healthy teeth and two moving teeth, as you see.
And sometimes it happens that a tooth or teeth return after the loss of one or both at their respective places, and they are retained as we have said, and remain so; this does not occur unless by a skillful and experienced craftsman.
And sometimes a tooth is fitted from the bones of an ox; and it is made in the shape of a tooth, and placed in the place where it strengthens and tightens the tooth, as we have said; and it remains and serves for a long time.
Chapter XXXIV.
Whenever a ligament occurring beneath the tongue is found, it may be either natural, as when a man is born with it, or accidental, resulting from a healed wound.
The procedure for this is as follows: open the weak jaw at its hinge in your own mouth and lift the tongue; then cut through the sinewy ligament across its width until the tongue is released from its grasp.
If there is something hard and knotted in it, and it comes from the healing of a wound: then thrust a hook into it and bore through it across its width until you reach the sinewy ligament, and the knot is released.
And beware that there is no tear or opening in the deeper flesh, and do not cut into an artery there, lest there be bleeding.
Then it is irrigated with rose water or vinegar, or cold water.
Next, place a linen cloth under the tongue to keep it pressed down every night, so that it does not heal again.
If there is bleeding, then cover the spot with a piece of damp cloth. If the bleeding persists, then cauterize the spot with a lentigo-type cautery, which is suitable for this; then treat it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
Chapter 35.
Sometimes there occurs a cyst beneath the tongue resembling a small frog that hinders the tongue from its natural function and perhaps grows to fill the jawbone.
The procedure is as follows: open the weak jaw so that the cyst can be seen in sunlight, and observe it closely.
If you see it is dark or black, hard and insensate, then do not touch it, because it is a cancer.
If it is cut to the white matter, where there is moisture, then throw in the hook and cut it with a sharp chisel, and release it from all sides. If blood veins during your operation, then put a piece of gauze crushed on it until the blood is cut off; then return to your operation until you extract it with its appendage.
Then wash it with vinegar and salt; care for it with appropriate treatment until it heals.
Chapter on the treatment of two molar cysts.
Chapter 36.
Whenever glands resembling goiters appear near the throat, that is, those which are called amygdalae: when you treat them as we have said in division and they do not heal, then consider.
If the abscess is hard, of a dark color, with few senses: then do not touch it with iron.
And if it is of red color and its root is thick: then do not touch it even with iron, fearing the flow of blood, rather let it be until it matures. Then either perforate it or let it burst itself.
And if it is of white color, round and its root is fine: then it is necessary to cut it.
And the operation in it is that you consider before its operation whether the abscess of it has ceased to be warm and completed rest, or has decreased by a slight decrease: then let the patient sit facing the sun, and his head in your lap: and open his mouth, and let a servant take hold between his hands, and press his tongue down with an instrument, whose form is as follows.
Let it be made of silver or bronze, which is thin like a knife.
And when you press his tongue with it and the abscess is shown to you and falls onto it: then take a hook and fix it in the amygdala, and extract it as far as possible, except that you pull something from his tunics along with it.
Then cut it with an instrument, whose form is as follows: (A sketch is provided here, I'm unable to provide an image in text format) It is similar to forks, but its extremities are curved so that the opening of each of them is facing the other sharply. Therefore take care that it is made from iron or brass coated with alum.
If however this instrument is not present, then cut it with a spatula, whose shape is as follows: [insert image or diagram of the spatula's shape] Be sharp on one side and not sharp on the other.
And after you have cut one almond, cut the other according to the same shape of the incision.
Then after the incision, the sick person should rinse with cold water or with vinegar and water.
If however there is a flow of blood, rinse with water in which the bark of pomegranates has been boiled or with leaves of myrtle and similar things from poplar trees, until the flow of blood stops: then take care of him until he is cured.
And sometimes boils other than almonds appear in the throat. Cut them therefore according to what I said in the incision of the two almonds equally.
I myself have been cured of a woman suffering from a boil that was born in her throat, which was drawing toward choking, and she had few senses, as it had almost closed her throat: and the woman breathed with a tight mouth, and already she had been prohibited from eating and drinking water: and now death had come upon her if it had remained for one day or two.
The boil had risen only to the extent that it had expelled two branches until they came out through the two nostrils.
I therefore rushed quickly and tied a hook on one of them. Then I pulled it out and a large piece was removed.
Then cut it off at the opening of the nose.
Then I made that which came out from the other nostril.
Then I opened its mouth and pressed its tongue; afterwards I fastened a hook on the ulcer; then I cut off part of it, and no pus ran out but a little blood; therefore the woman's throat was healed, and she began to drink water immediately, then she ate food.
Therefore I did not stop cutting from the ulcer for a long time; and the ulcer kept growing in place of what I was cutting, until it grew too long with that (woman).
So I cauterized the ulcer in her throat.
Therefore she stood after her application; then I walked away, and I did not know what God had done with her after me.
Chapter on the excision of a mouth ulcer.
Chapter XXXVII.
When a catarrh descends to the mouth, and an ulcer forms, and it is long, then it is called 'perpendicular'; and if it is thick and round in the lower part, then it is called a 'bubble'.
When it is cured with what was said in the division, and treatment does not help; and you see that the ulcer has become warm and soft; then it must be cut.
And when what comes together from it is round and not long, and it is red or dark or black, and there is no feeling in it; then it must be cut. There is fear for the weak in that (ulcer).
Therefore when you see it according to the way I said, white and long, make the weak person sit facing the sun; then press his tongue with the instrument whose description precedes; afterwards fix a hook in the mouth, and pull it downwards; and cut it with one of the two instruments that were said in the incision of the two wisdom teeth.
It is necessary that you do not cut from it (the patient), unless what is added exceeds the natural limit without addition.
If you cut more from it (the patient), you wound speech and discourse.
Then after the incision, use what I have said regarding the incision of two almonds (teeth): and take care of it until it heals.
If the sick person is afraid of the incision: then it is necessary that you use your skill in cauterizing it without fear and dread.
The method of cauterization in it (the sick part) is not anything other than with sharp water: and it is that you place the head of the sick person in your armpit. Then press his tongue with the instrument which I have said.
