Then take from the water which I have said in the chapter on cauterization, and make a not-extinguished lump of plaster, not thick nor thin, and fill with it the hollow of this instrument, whose shape is as follows:
Let the extremity where the medicine is placed be concave like the concavity of a conical shell (radial groove).
Place the instrument with the medicine on the boil itself: and let the sick person lie on his side so that saliva runs from his mouth through the internal medicine, so that nothing falls from it to his throat and harms him.
Then hold your hand with the medicine. And you, from above, place it on the boil with a quantity of half an hour, until you see it turned black and calmed by the biting of the medicine.
And if you wish to take a curette, and wrap it around the edge of the boil, and pour the ointment with the medicine over it, and insert the curette with the ointment on top, until the ointment adheres to the boil.
Apply this frequently until you achieve what you desire with regard to cauterization of the vein. Then release it; for indeed, it will burn and fall off after three or four days.
If you need to repeat the medicine, do so; and after cauterization, cleanse the area around the vein with a cotton dipped in butter, and clean it with the same medicine; and irrigate with cold water.
It shall be treated externally with ointments, and internally with poultices, until it heals.
Therefore, this method of treatment is healthier than incision and further from fear (risk).
And sometimes the vein is also cured with something more subtle than cauterization and incision; it is cured by suffusion, as described below. Take calaminthe, hyssop, origanum, rutus, sassafras, chamomile, abrotanum and similar herbs; grind them all together or some of them in a pot, submerge them with vinegar, and boil; the pot should be well coated with lime plaster; and there should be an opening in the middle of the pot, over which a concave instrument should be placed as follows.
It should be made of silver or bronze; the end with the granules should be inserted into the mouth of the sick person until the vapor reaches the vein through the tube until the vein becomes obscured greatly.
Then repeat over it frequently until it burns.
And be careful not to perform this treatment at the beginning of an abscess. Usually, however, the following is added to an abscess: and it should not be done unless at the decline of its warmth (heat).
If this instrument is not available to you, then take a reed, and roll the bark of an ox's horn on its end; so that the bone of the sick person is not burned; since the bark of the ox prevents burning the bone; and this is part of good treatment with safety.
On the extraction of spines, and bones from the throat.
In this context, "spinarum" refers to fishhooks or similar objects
Often a bone or fishhook, or some other sharp object adheres in the throat.
Therefore, it is necessary to extract what appears visible on top of the object that impedes vision, after pressing the tongue with an instrument in sunlight and it becomes clear to you that it is in the throat.
And what is not apparent to you and hidden in the throat, it is necessary that you make a emetic before the food has been digested in the stomach. For perhaps the attached object will be expelled through vomiting.
Or the sick person may swallow a fragment of nutmeg, or the root of lettuce, or a piece of dry bread crust; or he may take a dry soft sponge fragment and tie it up with thread, then swallow it. When it reaches the place where the spine or bone is located, and it is extracted, then it comes out.
If it does not come out as we have said: then use an instrument made of lead in this shape.
Let it be thicker than a radius but less so slightly, and at its end let there be a hollow, into which you can insert easily; and the tip should have its head raised upward.
And let it touch neither the epiglottis itself nor cause a cough; lest it push the bone or spine with it, or the physician insert his hand himself.
But if the sick person inserts it himself, that is better; because of his knowledge of the place where the thing is attached; and he pushes downwards or pulls his hand with the instrument upward, all of this according to the amount prepared for him, until it comes out.
Chapter on the Extraction of Leeches.
Chapter XXXIX.
When the leech is treated with what I said in the division of cure with medicines, and it does not heal, then consider at the throat of the sick person in front of the sun, or under the sun after pressing his tongue with the instrument that I told you about.
If your sight falls upon the leech, remove it with a small hook or a thin and well-placed probe.
If it is not possible with them (the small hook or thin probe): then take a hollow cannula, and insert it into the throat of the sick person up to his throat; then introduce into the hollow of the cannula hot iron with fire. Do this often, and let the sick person refrain from water all day.
Then let him receive a vessel full of cold water, and open his mouth in it; and rinse his bone with it, and do not swallow anything from it; and move the water an hour after another with his hand. The leech drops immediately upon feeling water.
If it does not come out as described, then fumigate the sick person with bedbugs, or with the tool mentioned in the treatment of an ulcer.
Do this repeatedly, for it will fall by itself.
And the method of fumigation is that you take a pot containing live prunes with fire, and the pot should be covered with a lid having an opening; and at the opening place the end of the tool.
Then pour the fumigation and place the sick person's mouth at the end of the cannula, and close the mouth so that the fumigation does not escape before you know that the fumigation has reached the leech. For the leech will drop immediately.
If it does not drop, then repeat the fumigation repeatedly.
Let the sick person bear thirst, eat salt and other things, but do not let him drink water.
Therefore, it is necessary for it to come out with this treatment.
And this is the form of the tool with which the leech is extracted from the throat when it falls onto it.
It resembles forceps, as you can see; except that it has this hook which enters the throat. And its end resembles the beak of a bird called ciconia, on which is the roughness of a file; when it grasps something, it does not let go at all.
Chapter on opening abscesses, their incision, and treatment in general.
Chapter XL:
The appearances of abscesses are numerous, various according to their remembrance, namely one and one in this book; and they are diverse in their perforations, and in the cutting of them from two ways.
One is of the nature of an abscess itself, and that which encompasses it from humidities.
And the second mode is due to locations where it occurs in the body.
Because an abscess happening in the head is different from an abscess happening in the anus; and an abscess happening in a fleshy place is different from an abscess happening in joints; and each of them has its own judgment according to the operation.
And among abscesses are those which should not be perforated unless after the maturation of pus in them and its completion; and from these are those which should be perforated while they are raw and do not mature according to their completion.
As abscesses which are near joints.
Because when an abscess happens near a joint and extends, as long as it becomes putrid what is in its surroundings, perhaps the ligaments or the nerves of that joint are corrupted; hence it is the cause of the contraction of that member.
Or it is an abscess near the main member; because if you delay the perforation of it until it matures, it will harm either that one or through the main member.
Or it is near the anus, so perforate it while it is immature; and it is not necessary to perforate a raw abscess, not completed digestion, except that it is near the anus, so that it does not become putrid deeply and extend towards the interior of the anus, and becomes a fistula, or becomes at its end which does not heal.
It is necessary that you know the hour of perforation of the abscess, which has ripened according to the completion; and it is at sedation of pain, recession of fever, and diminution of redness, and pulsation, and acuity of the head of the abscess; and the remaining signs.
And it is necessary that you make the same perforation at a lower place of the abscess, and of greater protrusion; and the perforation should be directed towards the length of the body, if the abscesses are in the parts of hands and feet, and in the places of arms, shoulders, necks, veins, and finally in all places without reflection.
In those which reflect (themselves), go with the perforation according to that limb.
But when the abscess is in fleshy places: then it is better to leave the perforation of it until its digestion has confirmed, as we said according to completion.
Because if you perform the perforation on it before that (the digestion has confirmed), the course of the virus from it is prolonged, and there are many dirt and foulness, and perhaps its edges harden, and its depth.
And some abscesses are to be perforated according to the breadth of the body for necessity; or according to that limb which needs it.
And it is necessary that you administer a small perforation for small abscesses, and a large perforation for large abscesses; or multiple cuts according to the likeness of the size of the abscesses.
And there are among abscesses, in which it is necessary that the skin be concave; and it should be cut when it has already become like a cloth, and made into an end, which is already dead; such as what often happens to boils and buboes.
And among them are those which are cut by a section having three angles. And from these, one which is cut as the figure of the myrtle leaf.
As an inguinal abscess.
And among them are those in which a round section is administered, and a crescent-shaped section; and similar ones from sections.
But that which has no head, like superficial abscesses, must be pierced by a superficial perforation or just with a flat one.
And it is necessary, when the abscess is large and has already collected much pus, to pierce it so that it does not burst and you extract all of the pus at once; rather, extract a part of it. Then lancet an abscess until another day. Then extract something from the pus again.
Do that repeatedly according to degree, until it comes out; especially if the person is weak in strength, or a woman pregnant, or a small child, or an old man decrepitus: for the animal spirit is many times resolved with the discharge of pus; and perhaps the weak person dies, and you do not perceive it.
Therefore beware of this chapter with great caution.
And after your perforation, by which you pierce the abscesses, it is necessary that you clean the wound; and consider. If therefore the wound of an abscess is small, or the section is flat, then administer linen cloths from linen or an old pot. And if the abscess is large, and there are many fissures of perforation, it is then necessary to insert linen into each fissure until they meet.
And if you have cut a part of the skin in an abscess, or if you have hollowed out its circumference; then it is necessary to fill it with an old pot, or as when a cloth is sewn, or shorn with linen wool without moisture; and tie it up until the third day.
Then cut it open, and care for it with what is necessary from an ointment, until it heals.
If bleeding occurs during your operation hour, then administer cold water and vinegar. After being soaked in them, place a cloth on the location of the bleeding multiple times.
If the bleeding persists, then it is necessary to administer treatment and medication, as I have described in many places of this our book, and by division.
If it is winter time and the location of the excision is among many nerves: then it is necessary to pour warm powders with wine and oil, and place them on the locations.
And if it is summer and the locations are fleshy: then it is necessary to place warm powders soaked in water or oil, or with wine and oil, and cool the entire thing. Until the third day, as we said, it is necessary to dissolve the excision, clean it and administer what is appropriate for its treatment until it heals.
This is therefore what is generally necessary for the knowledge of treating excisions.
According to the method of distinguishing, I have already said for every excision, how the way to its treatment is divided individually.
Chapter 41.
Chapter on the excision of excisions occurring on the skin of the head.
In the skin of the head occur small excisions, which are of the kind of knots, which are contained in the bags, which are like pouches themselves, as if they were sucked out like hen's bladders.
And their kinds are many.
Among them are fat ones: and among them are those that contain moisture similar to mud: and among them are those that contain moisture similar to scabies and powders: and those similar to them, and among them are the hard, stone-like ones.
And in the incision of all, and their extraction there is no fear, when at their incision, the artery does not make opposition.
The operation on them is to try it with the instrument whose shape comes after this, which is called "Introductory probe", until you know what it contains.
For if it contains moisture, then cut it with a transverse incision along the length of the superficial incision according to this shape: in this manner.
And begin with the incision along line b to line g. Since the moisture is evacuated, then remove the cyst that contains this moisture, and do not leave anything in it.
For often it returns if something remains from it.
Then immerse the wound in Egyptian ointment if it is present; and if not, in water and salt; fill the wound with it, and let it remain until another day. For the cyst itself corrodes what remains from it.
Then again over the wound with Egyptian ointment twice, thrice, and if necessary, until you are confident that nothing remains from the cyst; then care for the wound with ointment until it heals.
If the abscess contains a thick knot: then cut it according to this shape, with an incision having the form of a cross; and throw forceps between the divisions of the incision, and remove it from all sides; and try your strength in extracting the membrane that contains it.
If the artery opposes you, then do what I will tell you afterwards.
And similarly do for an abscess that contains stone, by incision and the same treatment, as we have said.
Incision on an abscess containing stone is easier because there is little blood or moisture. And sometimes there are some of these abscesses which are in the head in certain men, in which there is not deep moisture.
Because I have cut off above the abscess on an old woman's head, and I found the abscess to be as hard and solid as a stone, rough, white, which could not be broken: and if anyone struck it with something thrown at it, it would wound itself.
However, in other cases of abscesses in the head (except for these abscesses that occur in children's heads and at the roots of ears), their section should be a superficial one.
Or make a perforation in them always from below part of them, so that the course of pus may be relieved towards lower parts.
Then care for it with what is suitable for it from treatment.
Chapter on the section of goiters (swollen necks) in the neck.
Chapter XLII.
These abscesses often occur in the neck, under the buttocks, and in the groins; and sometimes they occur in the rest of the body.
On those which often occur on the neck, there is one kind and many; they are generated mutually; and every pustule from them is within its own proper tunica, as is in nodes and abscesses of the head, as we have said.
The species of these pustules are many. For from them there are hard ones; and from them there are those that contain liquids; and from them there are malignant ones, which do not obey treatment.
In that which you see good disposition from them in touch, of which it is evident that it is near to the skin color and moves to all parts, and is not attached with the neck muscles, nor with the buttocks, nor with an artery, nor is deep: it is necessary to separate it by superficial incision from the upper part to the lower part of the body along the line, b, to the line, g. And peel it off from all sides; and stretch two lips of skin with a scalpel or with several scalpels if needed, as we said in abscesses of the head, and extract it gradually.
And it is above caution, not to cut a vein or nerve.
Let the instrument not be very sharp; so as not to add your hand to the incision, or to disturb the sick person and cut what is not necessary.
If you cut a vein, or an artery, it forbids you from the operation; then place in the wound zegi powdered, or some powders that separate blood, and tie up the wound, and let it be until the sharpness of the abscess subsides and the wound becomes soft; or it begins to stink.
The blood is cut through the tunica, therefore return to your operation until you finish.
Then ask your index finger if anything remains of the small stitches: therefore cut and clean them.
If there is a large vein in the root of the stitch, then it is not to be cut from its root: instead, it should be tied with a strong double thread and left until it falls off on its own without harm.
Then fill the wound with an old lining, which you have already immersed in Egyptian ointment. Then take care of yourself.
If the stitch is completely cut, then it is necessary that you bring together the lips of the wound: and sew them immediately, after you see that there is no superfluous remaining.
But if you see that there remains superfluity due to the size of the stitch, then it is necessary that you go towards cutting the root of it and pulling it out: and apply the suture as we have said.
And that which contains humidities from the stitches, pierce it with a superficial perforation: so that you may see its matured place: and set the perforation at the place following below the body, as we have said.
Then apply linen with ointment and similar things after the perforation to burn off what remains from corruption, until you see that the wound is clean: then take care of yourself with a stronger flesh-generating ointment until it heals.
Chapter XLIII.
Section on epiglottis due to suffocation inside the throat.
The ancients described this section on the epiglottis, and I have not seen anyone in our land who has performed it: and this is their writing.
In those with synanchia, it is necessary to perform a section of the Epiglottis: since no benefit can be derived from it, because all veins and lungs are weak.
In those with a hot abscess in the mouth, throat or both tonsils, if there is no illness in the throat canal, it is necessary to perform a section of the Epiglottis to avoid loss from its swelling.
Therefore, when we wish to cut the Epiglottis, it is necessary to make a section of three or four circles around the Epiglottis using a small incision across its width, in that place which is between two circles, and this section should be made in sifac (a cartilage-like tissue) rather than in cartilage. This location is suitable for sectioning because it is devoid of flesh, and blood vessels are distant from it.
If the physician is timid, then it is necessary that he stretches the throat skin with a probe. Then he cuts the skin until he reaches the throat canal; he should cut the blood vessel if he sees any of it.
Then cut the sifac as we said; this is a sign of a throat canal section by phlegm that flows out from it when it bursts and the loss of voice.
And leave an open wound for some time.
When the hour comes when there is fear of swelling, gather together two lips of the wound skin and just the skin itself without the cartilage.
Then administer medicines that cause the flesh to grow until it is healed.
Says Albucasis. The summary of the discussion we have described is as follows: Exposition is not necessary except when they see that one of these abscesses has already suffocated the throat; and a weakened person who wishes to cut his breath is raised above death; they go to section the Epiglottis so that the weakened person may breathe over the wound site with some kind of breathing, and thus be saved from death; and for this reason they commanded that the wound be left open until the malicious nature of the illness has passed, which lasts about three days; then they command to close the wound and care for it until it is healed.
And that which I saw with my own eyes is, that one maidservant received a knife, and sent it into her own throat, and cut with it a part of the trachea of the lungs.
And I was summoned for her treatment, and I found her gasping, as is the gasp of the dead.
Therefore, I examined the wound, and found that blood had flowed out of it in small quantity. Therefore, I was reassured, because she had not severed the vein nor the artery; and the wind was coming out of the wound.
I approached therefore, and examined the wound, and treated it until it was well; and nothing happened to the maidservant except hoarseness of voice; and she returned on better days to a better condition.
Therefore I say that in the sectioning of the epiglottis, there is no fear.
Section on hernia of the throat.
Chapter XLIIII.
This abscess called hernia of the throat is a large abscess, according to the color of the body; and it is found much more often in women.
It is according to two modes: for it is either natural or accidental.
In the natural, certainly there is no congenital condition.
Accidental is, in two modes: one of which is similar to fatty nodes. The other mode is similar to an ulcer that comes from the swelling of an artery. And in this (there is) fear, and it should not be presumed with the iron, towards it, unless in that which is small: and you prove it, and you explore it with a probe. If you find it similar to a fatty node and it is not suspended with some veins: then cut it, as knots are cut; and extract it along with what contains it from the cavity, if it is in the cavity: and if not, then examine its entirety. Then care for the place where it should be treated, until it heals.
Chapter XLV.
[Title: On Cutting over Types of Knots.]
There are many types of knots, and I have already said all their species in division: and it is necessary that here the difference between a Knot and an Abscess be explained, when there is doubt.
I say therefore, that when an Abscess is heat and fever, and violent pains, until the boil subsides, and the overflow of pus is completed; then fever and heat subside.
But a Knot is not heat nor fever, nor pains; and it contains them in a bladder or sac that belongs to it, which is proper to the body: and it is closed like a pea or a date, and made like a walnut, and greater or smaller.
And they are, in two types: either fatty; or containing moisture. And the colors of moisture are many, as I said in division.
Therefore, when you come to the treatment of a Knot, you should test it, and investigate it first with an instrument that is called a Probe, according to its form, which will come in the chapter that follows this one.
The method of investigating boils and all nodes is to take this instrument and insert it into the moist place found in the boil: then you rotate your fingers with it gradually until you know that the instrument has penetrated the skin. Then, lay your hand according to the measure of the size of the boil.
Then extract what has been inserted, and observe what emerges in its track.
If what emerges is running moisture, whatever its color, then cut it off with a superficial incision, as I have said regarding the other boils.
And if no running moisture emerges in the track of the insertion, then you know it is greasy: cut it off above it with an incision having the form of a cross, according to this form, as I have taught you: and hang it up with hooks, and scrape the skin off from all sides with ease: and keep the container if possible over it, so that you can draw out the pus with the node.
If the container breaks apart during the operation and it is not possible to draw out the pus, then extract it fragmentarily until there remains some.
For if a little or much remains, the node returns most frequently.
If it prevails over you and a little remains: then fill the wound at its completion with some corrosive sharp powders: and suture the wound, and place warm poultice over the boil where it sits, and treat it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
If the node is large, then either two lips of its own accord will form, or you must treat it with that which makes it incarnate (i.e., grow inward).
But if it is contrary to a pulsating vein or non-pulsating one, then proceed, and fill the place with zega (a kind of powder) that has been crushed, and leave it sutured for two or three days until the wound becomes putrid and the boiling of blood subsides: then return to incise what remains from the node.
In capitulo quod sequitur dictur de figura corporis hum
External instruments for cutting and piercing.
These are the shapes of instruments and they are of three kinds.
Among them is the large one, among them is the middle-sized one, and among them is the small one.
Let them be made of iron, square at both ends properly, so that they may penetrate easily into a festered wound.
These are the shapes of perforating instruments, and there are three kinds of them. One of them is called a beryl, that is to say, a piercing instrument.
Among them is the large one, among them is the middle-sized one, and among them is the small one.
They come together to treat festered wounds, and ulcers, and abscesses, and buboes which are within bones.
And others are round, smooth, and blunt like the large needles which are used for cushions, namely of citron, or brass, or iron, or silver.
Better among them are those made of citron.
They are also made of black lead, which come together to probe abscesses whose concavity is for reflections so that they may be reflected with their bluntness along with those reflections.
There are again three kinds. Because there are long ones, medium-sized ones, and short ones, according to the size of the abscess and its constriction.
The shape of forceps, and there are many kinds.
Because there are simple ones, that is to say those with a single curve; and there are three kinds as you see, large, medium-sized, and small.
And among them are blind forceps: and there are three kinds.
And among them are forceps with two curves; and there are three kinds of these too: and among them are forceps with three curves; and there are three kinds of these too; and all of these are necessary in their place.
These are the forms of scalpels with which nodes and ulcers are cut and scraped, and they are of three types, since one is large, another is medium, and still another is small.
The extremities by which cutting is done are sharp, the other extremities are not sharp; they are not used in this way except to provide aid in scraping nodes, when fear of incising a vein or nerve arises, and so that the weak may heal and find temporary relief from the burning sensation that is found with the scraping of ulcers.
They are made of iron and are similar to a drill with which alcohol is made; and there is a hidden spatula-like point at the wide end, which runs both internally and externally as desired, just as you see.
The form of the spatula-like instruments hidden between the fingers during the perforation of ulcers; these are not grasped by the weak; and they are of three types, large, medium, and small.
The form of the ventosas (surgical instruments) with which blood flow is cut; and they are of three types, large, medium, and small.
They should be made of iron or brass, round, shorter than you see, and fine.
And it is necessary that these forms of the ventosas be large and small with you so that you can cut blood quickly when necessary, and then when medicine is not present with you.
However, you shall not use them for the cutting of blood in every part of the body, nor shall you use them except in fleshy places: such as the thighs, hips, arms, breasts, abdomen, groin, and similar parts of fleshy areas that are moist.
And sometimes they become small instruments similar to the fists' cores, according to their shape; with which the blood is cut off when it flows from the site of phlebotomy or incision of a vein or an artery; and sometimes they become round-shaped ones according to this form.
Chapter XLVII.
On the Care of Breast Lumps in Men that resemble those of Women.
Sometimes the breasts of some men swell during sleep (that is, when they begin to become dirty in sleep), until they resemble women's breasts; and remain unclean after this.
Whoever is disgusted by this, it is necessary that he cuts the breasts with a crescent-shaped incision, according to this form from line a to line b, then scrapes off all the fatty tissue. Then fill the wound with ointment of incarnateum (a type of ointment or salve). Then gather two lips of the wound with suture, and take care of it until it heals.
If the breast, however, falls to a lower position and becomes soft due to its size, as happens with women; then it is necessary that it be excavated on both sides of the upper breasts in two crescent-shaped incisions similar in form, one containing the other at their ends so that the larger line contains the smaller, according to this form from line a to line b. Then scrape off the skin that is between the two lips and remove the fatty tissue, and administer what I have said about suturing and powders, which is necessary for care until it heals.
If, however, you do not complete the incision that is necessary for you to make, due to the restlessness of the sick or due to bleeding; then fill the wound with a cottaged cloth soaked in a corrosive ointment and leave it until it corrodes what remains from the fatty tissue. Then care for yourself until you are healed.
On the Perforation of an Abscess which happens under Titillicus.
Chapter XLVIII.
These abscesses which occur under Titillicus, are of the types of hardened boils that contain cysts and those that contain moisture.
Therefore, those which contain moisture should be opened by lunar section according to this form from line b to line g. When all that is within the abscess has been evacuated with pus, then fill it up with an old cloth and leave it for another day.
Then remove the cloth, and treat it with an appropriate ointment until it is healed.
If the abscess is of the kind of hardened boils (nodules), then cut it open as we said when cutting on hardened boils equally.
If the wound extends such that it discharges pus, then administer cautery to it, according to what we said in the preceding text.
Chapter XLIX.
Chapter: On the incision of an abscess due to Artery and Vein.
When an artery is ruptured and the skin above it hardens, often an abscess occurs there; similarly, an abscess and swelling occur in veins as well.
And the signs by which it is recognized that an abscess and swelling are due to an artery or a vein are as follows: for if an abscess is due to an artery, it is long, compacted in the depth of the body; and when you press the abscess with your fingers, it feels as if there is a grating sound.
And what is due to a vein is round in the open part of the body.
And incision over this abscess is an error, and particularly when it is under the armpits, groins, neck, and in many parts of the body; and it is very dangerous. Therefore, its care should be avoided with iron, and what is even more so in the extremities or head, it should be avoided.
Therefore, over that which is due to the swelling of an artery opening, make an incision in the skin in lengthwise direction. Then open the incision with scissors, then the artery; and free it from tunics until it is exposed.
Then insert a probe under it and make it penetrate to the other side, and tie the artery with double thread at two places, as I taught you in the extraction of two arteries which are in the temples.
Then puncture the place between the two ligaments with a lancet, until all the blood that is there comes out, and the abscess is dissolved.
Then administer a treatment that generates pus, until the ligaments fall off; afterwards, care for it with appropriate ointments until it heals.
If the abscess is due to a vein incision, then you should hold with your hand as much of the abscess with skin as possible. Then insert the needle at the place you held with your hand, and make it penetrate. Let there be a double thread in it until you draw it out from the other side. Then tie the cyst with a good suture; as I told you before, in the suture of a sheep's gut, attach it to both sides with two ends of thread.
If you fear that the thread may be drawn out, then insert another needle with another thread under the cyst near the incision. Press and bind your threads in four places.
Then cut the cyst in half until it comes out what is inside; then cut off the excess skin and release what was tied from there.
Then place the potion you have immersed in wine and oil on top of it. Then apply the treatment which is made with linen cloths and ointments until it heals.
Chapter L. (Roman numeral)
[Section title] On cyst occurring due to twisting of nerves.
As a cyst occurs in arteries and veins, similarly it occurs in nerves; which happens to them due to trauma or excessive labor and similar causes; and mostly occurs at joints of hands or feet, or in any place where joints move; and the cyst is severe.
It resembles the color of the rest of the body and is found in multiple locations without pain; when it is squeezed with violence, it feels weak, like a numbness.
And the cyst is not gathered deep within the body; on the contrary it is under the skin and moves in every direction and does not reach toward the front or back.
Therefore, it should not be incised with iron where it is located at joints. Perhaps it may happen as contraction.
In what there is in the head or the forehead, find the skin with cautery. If therefore it is a small abscess, then hold it with forceps and cut it off from the root.
And if it is large, then hang it up with a hook and peel it; afterwards remove it, and dress the wound with suture; take care of it until it heals.
Chapter LXI.
Chapter on incising an abscess that occurs in the abdomen.
Accidents to some men often in their bellies, and in the remainder of their bodies, a growth called Fungalia, which is similar to mushrooms.
Its root is subtle, and its head is thick, and they are turned inside out with their lips. And there is among them something small, and there is among them what can be greatly increased.
And indeed I have already seen a man, and in his belly there were two growths that were more similar to mushrooms than other things: there was no difference between them, white, with fine roots, and they turned inside out, were closed, and moisture always flowed out from them.
I therefore cut them and found the weight of one as X VIII ounces and in the other as VI ounces. The operation on their incision is that you consider if the patient is weak, and the growth is white, moist, with subtle roots: then make the incision with a wide spatula, and have cauteries in your presence.
For often much blood is expelled upon the incision of it: therefore approach if blood conquers you, then cauterize it.
If you see a weak, fearful and timid person from the incision with iron, then take a well-made wire made of lead, and bind it to athelul: whose method is as we have said, and leave it for two days.
Then add in the binding of lead. Therefore do not cease to bind the lead, whenever it presses against the growth, until it is cut off and falls out without effort.
If however the growth of thick roots is, then there is fear and horror in its incision: especially because it is in the belly.
However, it is possible to make an incision in the middle of it. Then cauterize it, so it does not return.
Then treat it, until the wound is healed.
Be careful not to cut what is of a dark purple color, having few senses and an offensive appearance; for it is an apostematic cancer; and I will come again with the reminder of Cancer after this.
Chapter LII.
Chapter on the treatment of hernia in the navel.
A swelling of the umbilicus occurs for various reasons. It arises from hernias of the sciatic nerve, which is above the abdomen; or it comes out either bowel or intestine, according to what happens in other ruptures. It arises from blood flowing from a vein, or an artery, as was mentioned before. Or it arises from obstruction of wind in it.
If it is due to a hernia of the sciatic nerve and the passage of worms; then its color is similar to that of an abscess; it is soft, painless; and its position appears diverse. And if it is due to the passage of the intestine, then its position is much more diverse than what we have mentioned before. When you press it with your fingers, it disappears; then it returns and perhaps there is a sound; and it swells greatly at the entrance of the bath and causes severe pain.
If it is due to moisture, it is soft; then it does not disappear when pressed with your hand, nor can it be compressed, nor does it increase in size.
If it is due to blood, then with these signs appears an abscess turning black from the clavicle.
But if it is due to fleshy matter; then it is a heavy, large, hard abscess and pus collects according to its quantity.
If it is due to wind, then when touched it is soft.
And the treatment in this case is to determine whether the swelling of the umbilicus is due to blood from an artery or vein, or wind; then it is necessary to prevent its treatment. For there is fear and dread, as I taught you in the chapter where I said abscesses due to an artery or vein.
If the protrusion of the navel is due to intestine or hernia: then it is necessary that you order the patient to hold his breath and stand stretched out. Then sign with the encaustic around the entire navel. Then order him to lie down on his back upon your hands on his back. Then circle with a broad lath around the navel at the place which you marked with the encaustic. Then extend the middle part of the probe upward with a large hook. Then bind him around with a strong cord or with silk thread and the knot should be that of the alembic.
Then open the middle part of the probe which has been extended beyond the knot. If therefore you find it already caught by the knot: then extract the alembic, and insert your index finger into it, and push the intestine towards the interior of the abdomen; and if you find a hernia, then take it with the hook, and cut off its superfluous part.
If however it is an artery or vein (which is contrary to you): then circle it much. Then return to your surgery. And take two needles and insert two strong threads into them; and insert the two needles into the circle which you made around the abscess in the form of a cross, which you make penetrate.
Then stitch the abscess in four places on the needles; and if you wish, remove the needles, and leave a gap, until the rotten flesh extends: and falls off by itself; or cut it when it has become soft and rots away.
Then take care of him with whatever is required from the unguents until he is healed.
If the protrusion of the navel is from a hernia or dampness in him: then it is necessary to hollow out the abscess as we have said. And you draw out blood or moisture which you find there.
Then care for the wound along with it to make it close up.
Chapter LIII.
Chapter on Treating Cancer.
We have already discussed the types of cancer in the section on diagnosis and treatment methods for it; how to treat it with medicines and the need to avoid cutting or damaging it with iron. We also mentioned that cancer originates in the matrix (breast) and advised against using cautery in its treatment.
And the ancients said that sometimes cancer is in a location where it can be completely removed, such as cancer of the breast or hip, and similar locations, from limbs intended to be amputated; especially when it is a small, newly developing cancer.
But when it has become old and large, one should not approach it (to operate).
For I myself was unable to cure anyone from that affliction; nor have I ever seen anyone else succeed in treating it.
And the operation on it, when located as mentioned above, is to make an incision and release the patient from black bile several times (to drain it). Then perform venesection on the individual if you find a clear sign of its presence (the cancer).
Then prepare the patient by applying a preparation to the area where the operation will take place.
Then insert needles into the cancer that suit its location. Then hollow out the cancer from all sides with the skin, according to examination, until no trace of its roots remains; allow blood to flow out and do not remove it quickly or cut into it directly. Instead, press out the larger blood vessels with your hand or as possible with the instruments available there.
If the flow of large amounts of blood from an incision in an artery or vein hinders you, then cauterize the vein until the bleeding stops. Then care for yourself with the rest of the treatment until it is healed.
On the Care for Dropsy.
Chapter LIV (Roman numerals). We have already spoken about the types of Dropsy and how water accumulates; and all signs, and its treatment with medications.
And that which is treated with iron is only the type of ascites alone; and it does not approach iron when treating the type of tympanites; neither deeply for the type of hypersarcies, because it is fatal.
When you have been treated for this type of Dropsy (tympanites) with medications and the treatment does not help; then consider. For if the patient has already come to weakness, or there is another illness besides Dropsy (such as cough, looseness of bowels, and similar conditions); then beware not to treat him with iron; because it is dangerous.
But if you see a patient with an excess of strength and no other illness besides Dropsy; and he is not a child nor old; then the method of operation for him is to lift the weakened patient standing in your hands, and a servant behind him presses his abdomen by hand, forcing water down to the lower part of his chest.
Then take a sharp needle of this shape. Let it have two sharp points and long, with a sharp tip like a needle. However, there should be something short on it so that you do not go through with it during the operation to the intestines and injure it.
Then consider. For if Dropsy generation is from the intestines; then it must be extended with a cut of three fingers' width below the navel towards the lower part above the breastbone.
If however generation of Hydropsis is due to liver disease: then let your section be left from the navel by three fingers.
And if it is due to the spleen, then let your section be right-sided: and it is not necessary that the section should be on the side where the sick person wants to lie, so that excess fluids do not flow to that weak place.
Then pierce the skin entirely with an instrument. Then insert your hand into the incision, and with a spatula scrape under the skin, as if you are peeling it off: let the quantity that is scraped off be the size of a fingernail or about that much.
Then pierce the peeled skin, until the spatula reaches an empty place: and that is the watery area. Then remove it, and insert an instrument of this form into the opening. And it is similar to a cannula: it should be made of silver, copper, brass, lead, cleaned; on its lower part there is a small hole, and on the sides there are three holes, two from one side, and one from the other side: the end of it should have a cut like the opening of a reed, as you see; at the top of its upper end is a ring.
For when the instrument reaches the water, then it immediately descends upon the instrument, therefore let out as much liquid from the hour as is a half measure.
Because if you let out more than necessary from it, the sick person may perhaps die by depletion of his animal spirit; or he may suffer a syncope approaching death.

Then remove the instrument, and retain the water.
What it is, because it is immediately retained due to the skin that retains the opening which is on the sifac; about which I have told you to pierce it in this manner.
Then on the second day use the instrument again if you see that it can bear it; and also extract a small amount from water.
Do this for some days without fear, and keep yourself away from error; until there remains in the water only a little.
If you fear for the weak one, and let out a large amount from the water; then take care of him with warm sand, much sweat in the bath and sun, and wait for thirst; and take care of him with the most drying medicines until he is cured; and cauterize over the stomach, spleen, and liver, after the extraction of the water; according to what I have told you in what preceded.

De oculo exsectando.
On the extraction of a stone.
We have already discussed the appearance of a stone, its treatment with medicines, and its distinction between stones generated in kidneys, bladder, and the whole; we have also stated that operation on a stone is performed with hand and section; furthermore, the stone generated in the bladder properly is meant; and moreover, that which occurs in the spermatic cord; and finally, I am telling you this with a clear explanation and abbreviation.
The stone generated in the bladder most frequently occurs in boys.
Moreover, among its signs is that the urine exits from the bladder like water in its subtlety; it appears in it as white sand, and an afflicted man rubs his spermatic cord, labors with it, and often hangs down. Then it becomes erect and exits together with the anus in many of them.
The healing of boys is easy until they reach fourteen years of age. It is difficult in the elderly. But it is moderate in young men, because it is between that [condition] and its cure is easier for the one whose stone is larger; and if it is small, the treatment is reversed.
When we come to the treatment, it is first necessary that we cleanse the afflicted one with an enema, which draws out all the feces that are in his intestines; indeed, sometimes it prevents the discovery of the stone during examination.
Then the afflicted one should be taken with his feet, shaken and moved downwards; so that the stone descends to the depth of the bladder or leaps out from a high place several times.
Then let him sit between your hands, prepared; and his hands should be under his buttocks so that the bladder becomes totally relaxed towards the lower part.
Then ask him and touch him from outside.
If you feel a stone [calculus] in the space (bladder or urethra), then immediately approach it with incision on top of it.
If it does not fall with your touch at all, then you should wash the finger with oil of the left hand if the boy is weak; or the middle finger if he is a young man; and introduce it into his anus, and ask about the stone, until it lies under your finger; and gradually turn it towards the neck of the bladder.
Then press on it with your finger, and push it towards the outside to the place where you wish to make the incision; and command one of the assistants to press on the bladder with his hand, and command another assistant to raise the testicles with his right hand to the upper parts; and with the other hand, remove the skin that is under the testicles in the part from the place where the incision is made.
Then insert a pointed probe (speculum) of this shape: And find the place that is between the anus and the testicles, not in the middle, on the side of the left buttock; and make the incision over the stone, and your finger should be in the anus; and make a transverse incision so that the incision outside is wide and the inside is narrow, according to the quantity, so that the exit of the stone from it is not larger.
Perhaps the finger pressing on the stone in the anus during incision will compress it and come out without difficulty.
And know that from the stone are its angles and edges, for this reason its exit is difficult due to it.
And from it [stone] is smooth, like a testicle, and round; and the exit of it will be easy.
To him who has angles and edges, add a fracture (incision).
If it does not come out, then it is necessary that you apply pressure on it; or you tie over it as one ties a cord around a stone, which does not loosen from it; or you insert under it a subtle instrument with a curved tip.
If you cannot press on it, then slightly enlarge the opening (foramen). If something restrains you by blood, cut it with a knife.
If the stone is larger than one (small stone), first push on the bladder bone. Then cut it over there (the bladder). Next, push a small one after that; and do the same if there are more than two.
If it is very large, then ignorance is to cut through it with a large incision. Since it happens to the sick that one of two things occurs to him, either he dies or there is constant urine discharge; this is because the place does not heal at all.
But administer its evacuation until it comes out; or apply pressure to the fracture with forceps until you extract it gradually.
When you have completed your operation, then fill the wound with turpentine, aloe, and dragon's blood; bind it, place a cloth soaked in oil and wine (or rose oil) and cold water on top of it to settle down the abscess.
Then turn the sick man over onto his neck and do not loosen the bandage for three days. When you loosen it (the bandage), anoint the place with oil and water.
Then care for him with diaphanus ointment and basilica ointment until he is healed.
If a hot abscess or similar occurs in the wound, add catharsis and other such remedies; like if blood freezes in the bladder, and urine is prevented from passing out of it; and this is known by the passage of both blood and urine. Insert your finger into the wound, and draw out the blood. If it remains, it provokes the corruption of the wound, and its putrefaction.
Then wash the wound with vinegar, water, and salt; and apply to it everything that is appropriate for healing, until it heals.
And during the entire healing process, you must tie two thighs together and apply a poultice, because of the medicaments that are placed on the site.
If the stone is small and located in the penis, and a bladder stone presses against it, preventing urine from exiting; then treat it with what I described before you reach the incision. For many times you will be released from the incision by this treatment, for I have already proved it.
And take a "Perforator" made of iron, with this shape: triangular at one end and sharp; fixed to wood.

Then insert the "Perforator" iron into the penis easily, until the "Perforator" reaches the stone; and with your hand rotate the Perforator slowly on the stone; and you force the perforation until it makes the stone penetrate from the other side.
Urine is released immediately.
Then press your hand on what remains of the stone from the outside part of the penis. It breaks and comes out with the urine, and the sick one heals.
But if this treatment is not prepared for you for some reason that prevents it; then tie a thread below the stone, and another thread above the stone. Then cut across the stone on the penis between the two ties. Then extract him. Then loosen the ligament and clean the frozen blood that forms in the wound.
And it is not necessary to tie a thread under the stone, unless to prevent its return to the bladder: and another ligament on top, unless so that when the thread is loosened after the stone's exit, the skin returns to its place, and seals the wound: and for this reason, it is necessary for you to do so, when tying the upper thread, to lift the skin upward, so that it returns at the wound's edge, and seals the wound, as we have said.
Chapter 61.
Chapter on the Extraction of Stones in Women.
A stone is rarely generated in women.
If a stone happens to one of them, then the cure is difficult and it is forbidden due to many reasons.
One reason is that the woman may be a virgin.
And the second is, because you will not find a woman who will disclose herself to the doctor when she is chaste or married.
The third is, because you will not find a woman well-versed in this art, especially in the operation with the hand.
The fourth is, distance from the place of the stone: which requires a deep incision, and there is fear.
If necessity forces it, then one must accept a skilled woman: and such women are rarely found.
If you are unable to do it, then look for a chaste doctor, subtle and experienced in women's matters, or a woman who is familiar with this art: make her present, and especially instruct her to perform everything that you tell her about the stone.
First, check if the woman is a virgin: then one must insert a finger into her anus and search for the stone.
If therefore it is found (the stone), immobilize it with his finger, and then command the midwife to insert her finger into the weak bladder, and to investigate the stone, after she has placed her left hand on the bladder and compresses it with a good pressure.

Then cut it near the middle of the bladder at the root of the hip from whatever side it is prepared, and feel for the stone in that place; and his finger should not be removed from the stone, pressing down on it; and let the incision be small in the beginning. Then introduce a ray into that incision.
Then introduce a ray into that incision. If (he) feels the stone, then he should add to the incision according to the size proportional to which the stone is coming out from there.
And know that the shapes of stones are numerous. For this reason, it is small and large, smooth and rough, long, and round with branches.
Know its shape so that it may be signified to you about that which you wish.
If blood overwhelms (you), then add a little crushed wood ash at the place, and hold it for an hour until the blood is cut off.
Then return to your operation until the stone comes out; and make sure that you prepare yourself with the instruments which I have said for the removal of stones in men, in order to help you in your operation.

Head, LXII.
Section on watery hernia.
A moist worm (ramex aquosa) is not anything else but a gathering of moisture within the albubo (sifac), which is beneath the scrotal skin containing the egg (ovum): and it is called albubo (sifac).
And sometimes it is in its own panniculus (fatty tissue) which nature has prepared for it on the testicle's part until it is considered mature: which is another egg and lies between the albubo (sifac) white, as we said; and this does not happen often.
And the generation of this ramex (worm) is indeed due to weakness that happens to testicles: therefore, this material flows into them. And sometimes it occurs due to a blow upon the testicles.
And this moisture has many colors. For the color of this moisture can be sloping towards lemon (citrinitas), or red and blood-like (sanguineus rubeus), or feculent (foul-smelling), black, or watery white, and this is what is more common.
And the signs by which it is known where the gathering of moisture is, are these: If it is in a white boil as we said, then the hemorrhoid is round and shorter in size like the figure of an eye; and it does not appear as a testicle, since moisture keeps it contained from all sides.
And if there is moisture within the pouch itself, then the hemorrhoid is round like part of an eye, and therefore it bursts because it is another egg.
And if there is moisture between the skin of the testicles and the white boil, then it falls under the sensation (of pain or discomfort).
Therefore, when you have knowledge of the color of moisture, then test the color of moisture in the hemorrhoid with a square probe, whose shape precedes (the hemorrhoid). According to that which emerges in the footprint of the probe, judge regarding what is between it (the hemorrhoid and the probe).
When we come for treatment with iron, then it is necessary that you order the sick person to be bled if it is possible for him, and look at his body full (of fluid).
Then he lies on his back on a low bench and puts many cloths under him.
Then you sit on the left side of him, and order the servant to sit at his right, who extends his arm from one side of the skin of the testicles to the part of the rectum (anus).
Then take a broad spatula and cut the skin of the testicles from the middle along its length up to the comb (pubic bone); and make an incision according to the rectitude of the line that divides the skin of the testicles, until it reaches the white boil encompassing; and scrape and observe it, or be careful not to cut it; and let your scraping be more on the part that hangs with the testicle towards the egg (anus); and examine carefully with your scraping according to the quantity that you can handle.
Then, perforate a bladder full of water with a wide perforation and drain out all the water.
Then separate between two lips of the incision with forceps, and extend the bladder upward, and do not touch the skin surrounding the testicles holding it: and cut the bladder in any way possible for you to cut it, either entirely or piecemeal, especially the thin side. For if you do not examine and scrutinize [the area], there is no security in the incision lest water return.
If however an egg comes out externally from its own skin during your operation hour: then when you complete the incision of the bladder, bring it back. Then join two lips of the skin of the testicles with a stitch.
Then take care of it as any other wound until it heals.
If you find an egg corrupted by another blackness, then it is necessary that you tie the vessels, which are the supports, fearing bleeding.
Then cut off the testicle with its support, and extract the egg; afterwards take care of it as I said before.
If however water is accumulated in two parts, then you know that there are two branches: therefore cut the other part as equally as you did in the other.
And if it appears to you that the operation should be one, then do so; afterwards cleanse the blood. And insert into the incisions a wool soaked in oil, or pink oil; and place another wool outside which you have soaked in wine and oil, and spread it over the two testicles, and search the bowels; and put double cloths on top of it, which are small towels; and tie them above with a ligament having six knots according to this form.
Then two cloths are taken, washed, and filled with carbonic acid, according to this likeness: and the ends of it which are pressed [together] should be covered with wet wool; and they are tied together in the loins: one end is received on the anus up to the back, and the other on the part of the neck: and two ends below on the lower legs, and two other ends above on the groins; and the whole tie is tied together in the loins.
And at times, this ramel is artificially treated with a cautery in place of section, with iron: and it is to receive the cautery scalpel, subtle, and cut the skin of the testicles: and it is to be lit, as we have told: until when the sifac white containing water is exposed: then receive the cautery, according to this form.
The letter is made similar to Greek.
Then pierce it with that [tool], and it is set on fire until all the moisture exits.

Treatise on the care of fleshy roots.
Know that, when cutting upon this fleshy root [turnip], there is a danger of leading to death in many dispositions. Therefore, it seems to me that its abandonment should be saved from it.

Chapter LXIV.
Section on the treatment of branches that occur with a tree.
A tumor is enclosed by some swelling, resembling a bunch of grapes with the softening of the testicles; and it becomes difficult for weak movement and exercise, as well as walking.
And in the treatment of this illness is due to fear, because of the memory that preceded it.
However, we must say the operation according to what the first ones did.
I say that you should make the weak person sit on an elevated seat. Then push the suspender of the testicles downwards. Then hold the skin of the testicles with your fingers, with the bowls which are near the thigh; let another servant hold it and stretch it with a violent extension.
Then make a broad incision across the bowls (scrotum) with a sharp and long cut, until the testicles are exposed.
Then scrape off all the fat from every part, as we told you in the extraction of arteries in the temples.
Then insert a needle with a double thread into them (the vessels), and tie it at the places where they meet veins; and tie it again at the end of them. Then cut it (the vessel) in a straight middle section along the body's length and extract what collects from the foul and corrupted humors.
Then care for the wound with wound treatment, in which pus is generated to drain the testicles that nourish one of them. It is not harmful through it.
If the vein happens to encompass all the vessels, then they must be drained because of this for the testicles with the vessels: so as not to be deprived of its nutriment due to incision and decay or burn, and not be beneficial with them.
Chapter 65.
Chapter on the care of intestinal roots.
The passage of this root (intestine) is from the incision that happens on the stretched sifach over the abdomen in the groin part of the liver.
Why do the intestines come out through this rupture to one testicle. And this rupture is either from the sifach or its extension.
These two kinds of rupture occur from various causes: either by impact, jump, shout, lifting of a heavy object or similar things.
And the mark when it is from extension of a vein. It happens gradually over a long time and not suddenly; it is an abscess equal in depth to the surface; because sifach compresses the intestine.
And the mark of it when it is from a cut sifach, because it causes a strong pain suddenly at first; and it is an abscess different, appearing under the skin nearby; and this is due to the outlet of the intestine, and the course of it towards the exterior sifach.
And sometimes it comes out with the intestine: and this is called an Intestinal branch, and zirbia; and sometimes it happens with diarrhea.
And sometimes it runs into the intestine with feces, and is retained there; and this is a danger to the sick, because it causes severe pain, especially when pressed.
And in treating the disease with iron there is fear; therefore, one should be careful about accidents in this.
And the method of operation is to order the sick person to reduce the intestine with his own hand towards the concave parts within if he obeys the return. Then it lies on its back on its neck between your hands and raises its legs.
Then stretch the skin that follows the skin towards the upper parts, and cut the entire skin of the testicles in length. Then tie the incisions with hooks on both sides of the cut according to what you need to open the cut with them; and the cut should be according to the quantity that is possible so that the egg can come out from it.
Then scrape the sifak and what is under the skin of the testicles until the white sifak appears hard from all parts; then insert your index finger into the area following the testicle, into the area between the white sifak, which is under the skin of the egg, and between sifach according to it, and without the adhesion that is in the posterior part of the egg.
Then move with the right hand to the inner skin of the testicles; and as this is done, extend the albumen upward with the left hand; and lift the egg (ovum) with the albumen towards the part of the section; and command the servant to extend the egg upward; and you dissolve the adherence that is behind by a complete dissection.
And ask your fingers if there is anything there from the intestine rolled up in the hard albumen. If, however, you find something from it (the testicle): then push it down towards the lower belly.
Then take the awl, in which there is a thick thread, made of ten threads like linen: and insert it into the last albumen, that is, the membrane, which follows the section, that is under the skin of the testicles; then cut the ends that project from the thread until there are four threads. Then arrange some of them on top of others in the shape of a cross; and bind with it the thread which I mentioned, that is, the strong ligament of the testicle membrane, until no fluid from the sacs that nourish them can pass to them: so that a warm abscess does not occur there. And place the second ligature beyond the first ligature, distant from it by more than two fingers. And after these two ligatures, release from the albumen under the skin of the testicles an amount equal to a finger's breadth; and cut the rest all around in the shape of a ball, and remove the egg.
Then cut in the lower part of the skin of the testicles along a line where blood and pus flow, as we said in that which was mentioned before.
Then apply wool soaked in oil to the wound; and apply the ligament that we mentioned. And sometimes a white sifach is cauterized as we said, after its incision to fear blood flow. This translates to: It often happens that (something) is (happening). The original sentence does not provide specific details And release the ligament until it falls by itself.
If the case should delay, then fumigate it with hot water; and place over it what I said until it falls.
Then care for the wound with the rest of the treatment of wounds, until it is healed.
Chapter LXVI (Roman numerals).
Chapter on Pneumonia.
In this pneumonia, I have not seen anyone who dared to treat it with iron.
And at first they said that it happens as we narrated in pneumonia that is with wheat. It is to tie vessels after cutting on them easily below; then cut in the middle, and care for it afterwards with what opens it up until the vessels fall out; and care for the wound according to what I said until it heals.
Chapter LXVII (Roman numerals).
Chapter on Disruptions that occur in groins.
When rupture occurs in groins as we said and the place emits and something from the intestines does not descend towards the testicles; and if it descends, it is insufficient, and it returns every hour; but if this continues for a time, a tear is added to the sifach until the intestines descend into the sifach.
It happens with the extension of sifach that is in groins as we said. It is because the sifach is extended; then it is softened, the place is scraped and it emits.
Care for it with cautery as its preceding narrative said.
And sometimes it is cured with iron, in this manner: and it is, that the sick one lies upon his back on your hands. Then cut the place of rupture and protrusion, by incision in width, according to the quantity of three fingers.
Then tie the ligature and those under the skin until the white sifach is exposed, which is below the skin that follows it.
Then take a radium (small rod), and place it upon the protrusion from the sifach, and press it to the depth of the abdomen.
Then make two incisions upon the protrusions at the end of the radius from the sifach, and connect them with a suture; then remove the end of the radius.
And do not cut the sifach at all, nor stretch the egg, nor anything else, as I have told you in the treatment of intestinal branches (intestines).
Then treat that with the dressing for wounds. When you make a suture, clean it, and restore the wound, until it heals.
For the sifach contracts, and no protrusion is added to the rupture.
And cautery is better in this place, because it is closer to healing.
Chapter LXXVIII (78).
Chapter on the softening of scrotum skin.
The skin of the scrotum is often softened in some men because the flesh that is between them becomes soft and the appearance is corrupted.
Therefore, it is necessary for the one who is asked to treat this, that he makes the sick man lie on his back, and cuts all the softened skin that is over the natural skin.
Then gather the two folds of skin together with a suture; and if you wish, remove the surplus of the softened skin by three or four stitches, or a strong one.
Then make a cut between the sutures.
Then, take care of the treatment of the remaining wounds until they heal and the threads fall off.
Chapter LXIX.
Section on Castration.
Know that Castration in our law is excommunicated: and therefore it is permitted to me, not to remember it in my book; and its remembrance is not necessary, unless for two reasons.
One of these reasons is that it should be in the knowledge of a physician when asked about it: and so that he may know its treatment if it happens to someone.
And the other reason is that we often need castration of certain animals for our benefit through it, such as sheep, goats, and cats, and similar ones among animals.
I say therefore, that Castration is done according to two ways. Or by attrition. Through a cut and a split.
In what is performed through rubbing, the method of operation is this: we make the animal sit in warm water until its testicles soften and become loose and hang down; then rub them with your hand until they resolve and are not perceptible to touch.
In castration through a cut and a split, it is necessary that you hold the animal, and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand.
Then tie the sack, and cut above all the egg with one section until two eggs appear; then cut what remains after you have peeled both of them, and do not leave anything on it except a little sifaket (subtle matter), which is over the vessels.
And this method of castration is better than the one performed through rubbing; because rubbing perhaps leaves something of the testicles, wherefore the animal desires copulation.
Then take care of the wound until it heals.
Chapter 70.
§ On the care of a Hermaphrodite in two ways.
Hermaphrodite is from men according to two modes. One of them is because it appears in him what follows space, or in the skin of the testicles, in that which is between two testicles, with a figure like a female wolf, in which there are hairs: and sometimes urine flows out from that which is in the skin of the testicles.
In women there is one species, and it is like a female wolf over the comb like small testicles of a man, projecting to the outside; of which one is like Priapus of a man, and two like two testicles.
And the cure of the three species, two from men, and the species of one from women, is: because it is necessary that you cut the flesh added to them until the impression of them flees away. Then heal them with healing of other wounds.
As for the second species of men from which urine flows out, which is in the skin of the testicles, there is no operation, nor is there any healing at all.
Chapter LXXI.
§ On the cutting of Tentigins, and the projecting flesh in wolf-women.
A tentigo (suture) may be added over a natural part until it becomes unsightly and repulsive in appearance; and sometimes it is extended so much in some women that it reaches to copulation.
Therefore, it is necessary to hold excess suture with hand or hook and cut; and not to cut too deep during incision, especially at the root; so that there is no bleeding.
Then care for it in wound healing until it heals.
Meat (flesh) arising is the flesh that is born in the opening of the matrix, until it fills the same; and perhaps it comes out to the outside like a tail; and for this reason some call the condition 'cauda'. Therefore, it is necessary to cut it as we cut a suture and care for it until it heals.
Chapter on the treatment of a woman's wound that has not been pierced.
Chapter LXXII.
A woman's wound that has not been pierced, or the opening is small. It may be either natural (spontaneous) or accidental (traumatic).
Accidental is due to an illness that precedes; and it may be from flesh arising, or spisso (adhesion), or sifach (fibrous tissue); and it may occur in the deep part of the matrix, in the sides of it, in the upper or lower part of it; and it prohibits coitus and impregnation, and possibly delivery, and perhaps menstruation.
Its identification is made by the appearance of an obstetrician if the protrusion is nearby.
If it is not apparent, then search for it with your fingers or with a probe.
If the protrusion is from fibrous tissue (sifach) and is near two lips; then push it out and tear it apart.
And it is to place two small plugs on top of the lips.
Then put your index fingers together and the woman shall be lying on her back with her legs spread apart. Then extend the two lips forcefully until the sifach is torn subtly and the opening is created.
Then take thread, dip it in oil and place it on the site; let the woman rub it every day to prevent hardening of the area.
If the sifach is thick and swollen, then it is necessary to cut it with a large, sharp scalpel-like leaf of myrtle.
If the opening is due to flesh growth, then hang it with hooks and cut it; use medicines that stop blood flow without causing pain such as acacia, dragon's blood, and resin mixed with egg white.
Then administer a wide cannula of lead to prevent quick healing of the wound and keep it for several days; apply linen cloth, then treat the rest with usual care until it heals.
And sometimes there may be birth of other flesh-growths in the womb; therefore they should be cut according to this method: before it becomes a cancerous ulcer (for cancerous growth that is in the womb should not come into direct contact with iron at all).
Chapter 73.
Chapter on Hemorrhoids, by Athaeliel and Botor of Red Wine for women.
Hemorrhoids are indeed an opening of the vein's outlets, until blood flows frequently and abundantly from them.
When hemorrhoids become chronic, they become piles; and I have already said about their species and signs in the division of them; here I will tell which ones receive treatment and which do not.
I say that hemorrhoids which are within the opening of the womb and do not appear to the senses: then there is no treatment with iron for him.
But those which are above the opening of the womb, where sensation falls upon them, are those that can be treated.
Therefore it is necessary to introduce a woman into a cold house. Then extend the anus with forceps or with rough cloth, and cut them from their roots.
Then sprinkle powder upon them at the flow of blood from one of the incision wounds without biting: such as asphalt, dragon's blood, pitch, and similar things.
Then push his feet against the wall at the hour of six (midnight). Then place her in cold water.
If the flow of blood persists: then make her sit in a decoction of sumac, and pomegranate bark, and of green walnuts, and similar things.
Then take barley flour, and make it into a poultice with honey and vinegar, and apply the plaster on his back.
If blood is separated with it, that is good; and if not, let adhesive winds (blisters) form on the back, and on the breasts, without cutting or scratching.
Then take wool and dip it in the juice of tarathith, or the juice of arnoglossum, or the juice of the leaves of alaulla (wild bryony), Pontic wine, and make it sticky with it on a leaf.
When the abscess has ceased, then treat the place with ointments until it heals.
Albarth however is red like a boar's head and has a rough appearance.
Therefore it is necessary to cut what appears from it, as I said about hellebore equally: and treat it until it heals.
Quomodo operari debet Mulier in partu, et quibus cas
On the perforation of a Caesarean section that occurs in the womb.
When to operate on a woman in labor and what types of lesions may occur in the womb: cancer, stone abscess, ulcers, adubelati (herpes), fistulae, hemorrhoids, ragadiae, thilil, warm abscess.
And indeed, I have already said that all these diseases and their types, the symptoms of each one, and their treatments should be addressed in another discussion: it is necessary to discuss here the hot abscess that occurs in the womb, which is among those abscesses that collect pus. It is important to know how its opening with iron should be performed.
Therefore, consider this. If the pain of the abscess is acute at its onset with striking and burning sensation, and fever: if you feel it swelling, then do not perforate it. Treat it in a manner that helps maturation until the acuteness of the symptoms subsides.
Then the woman should be made to sit on a couch with two chairs on either side, and recline or lean on her back, and place her feet at the lower part of the abdomen: her hips should be spread out, and she should put her arms under her knees and tie them together with a bandage at that point.
Then the midwife should sit on the right side, and administer the instrument used to open the womb.
And when you are to administer this instrument, it should be shaped like a rod that penetrates the woman's womb without exceeding its depth and causing harm to the weak.
If the instrument is too deep, then one should place powder on the cover of the deep matrix to prevent the entire instrument from entering deeply into the matrix. One should also place a stirrup, which runs through the instrument, on the upper side. This should hold the instrument and turn the stirrup until the deep matrix opens.
When it appears to be an ulcer and is touched with the hand, and it is soft and tender: then one should cut it off at its head with a broad-blade.
When pus is discharged, then one should put linen saturated with rose oil into the wound: or green oil, in which there is some styptic, and place a lint and make an incision in the deep matrix.
And place outside on the matrix, and over the comb, clean wool saturated with water in which boiled mallow has been.
Then it should be treated for two days with an ointment that suits it until it heals.
And sometimes the matrix and wound are washed so that they are cleansed with water and honey: then with water in which the root of the lily or long aristolochia has been boiled, and then return to the ointment.
If the wound is hidden within the matrix, then one should refrain from treating it with iron, rather cure it with what has been said in the division.
Chapter LXXXVI.
Chapter on Obstetrics: How to treat living embryos that have come out abnormally.
It is necessary for an obstetrician to first know the shape of a normal delivery.
Therefore the signs of this are that when you see a woman being pressed towards her lower parts, and she wants to smell air and urinate on herself from what is above her in childbirth, and she hastens the exit of the embryo: then know that this delivery is according to a natural shape, and the exit is above its head, and the afterbirth with it: or suspended, or hanging from the navel.
When therefore you see these signs, then it is necessary that his belly be compressed, so that the embryo descends quickly.
When it descends upon his head, the second one also descends with it, and it is cleaned from these superfluities with good purification.
But he who is beyond this birth is unnatural, inadmissible.
Because sometimes the fetus comes out beyond his feet, and his body comes out before his head itself, and his feet themselves, and one hand or one foot: or the head and one hand come out: or the belly comes out: and perhaps it turns over on its neck, and similar unadmissible figures.
