Therefore it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and skillful in all these matters and to avoid error and deception: and I am showing every figure of them, and how there is intelligence in it, and it is indicated by that, and it will remain on top of him.
When the fetus comes out beyond his head in a natural delivery, and it becomes violent over the woman, and the labor is difficult for her, and you see his strength already weakened: then make her sit on a chair or women hold her: and warm up her womb with fenugreek cooked and with moist oils.
Then the midwife introduces a small spatula between her fingers and separates the second one, and cuts it with her nail until it runs out of wetness: and compresses the woman's belly until the fetus descends.
But if it does not descend, then it is necessary to cleanse the woman with fenugreek mucilage and sesame oil.
Then order her after the cleansing to be compressed: and make her sneeze with a snuff mixture, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour. The fetus will immediately come out.
If two hands of the fetus emerge first, it is necessary that you gradually pull them back with ease. If it does not comply during delivery, then place the woman on a seat and elevate her feet upwards; then strike the seat on the ground; and hold the woman so that she does not fall due to the shock.
If the hands do not come out and the fetus dies, then cut them and extract the remaining part of the fetus; and tie his hand with a cloth, and pull him out equally; for he will also come out.
§ The exit of the embryo is above its feet. When the fetus comes out above its feet, then it should be pushed upwards; then it should be slowly turned over; and finally it should be pulled out equally.
Then grasp one of his feet and gradually stretch it.
When they emerge up to the hips, then command him to hold back and make her sneeze with a pinch; for he will come out if God so wills.
And if it does not emerge as we have said, then gradually pull the fetus back until you place him in his natural position. For he will then come out easily through the exit.
If it is not permitted as we have said, then take some mallow, aleppo pine oil, and softened gum; grind the whole in a mortar with good pounding; afterwards spread the paste of it on the woman's vulva and inside her womb. Then make her sit in warm water until she feels comfortable.
When you see that the lower parts of her are now warmed up, then apply to him a warm piece from myrrh and place it on top of him. When therefore the hour [of the operation] holds [comes], then make her sit on a chair. Then make her sneeze, and pinch her own nose and snout; and press the lower part of the abdomen gently with pressure. For feces will come out immediately.
The exit of the fetus over the knees and hands. When it comes out in this manner, then insert your hands slowly. Then the woman lies on her back, and let her feet hang downward; and she lies reclining on a bed, and embraces her hands. Then press slowly above her abdomen. Then extract what is beneath her feet from the anus, until it is prepared below [ready for birth]. If the fetus does not come out, then take her feet and shake them violently. Then press what is above the pubic bone slowly, until the fetus rises to the higher parts. Then insert your hands and press the fetus gently; and command the woman to be pressed, until the fetus comes out.
The exit of the fetus hangs laterally from the hands. Insert your hands for reducing [the fetus]. If it cannot be reduced [positioned], then lift the woman and make her walk.
If she cannot walk, then make her lie on a bed; and strike her legs violently with a strong blow.
Then apply the ointment you have prepared from gums [resins].
If she receives delivery, then make her sit on a chair. Then study the reduction of the hands and press the fetus according to its natural shape; and make her sneeze, and command her to press herself until it comes out.
The outcome of the fetus is above its neck, with hands spread open, and its face is towards the back of its mother. The midwife should hold the fetus' hand and then gradually turn it, equalizing its position with ease.
When it is evened out, then place oil and gum over the place I mentioned.
Then command him to move gradually. When you have done that, then make her sit on a seat and command her to lean towards the right side. Then command her to press down, and make her sneeze with pepper or another similar substance.
The outcome of the prepared fetus is on the side. When it descends to the mother's opening in this manner with the afterbirth, then cut the afterbirth with your nail until it is expelled due to moistness.
If the fetus hangs over its face and neck, then cut it from the navel so that it is not retained and dies.
Then push the fetus inside until you place it as needed; and command the woman to press herself several times, for it will come out easily by itself.
The outcome of twins or multiple fetuses. Know that twins often give birth: and sometimes three or four are born. However, this is unusual and rarely happens.
Five are indeed outside nature and do not live completely; and the afterbirth contains them, although they multiply, yet only one afterbirth; and they are separated by a string, distinguishing between them tied at the navel of each one of them.
And sometimes they come out like a single fetus in a natural easy delivery, and they come out in an unnatural way as I have mentioned.
If some of them are difficult at childbirth and reach what we said in unnatural figures, then care for them as we have described: let it be subtle and act with ease and slowness, and invent according to every figure with that which is prepared for him leading to health by his intellect.
Remembrance of the one formed in the womb from embryos, and they are aborted.
Sometimes one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and more than ten are formed in the womb: and it has been verified by me, that a woman, while giving birth, expelled seven, and another fifteen, all formed ones.
What was done by the measurement of the glorious sage.
Therefore, this whole thing should be in the knowledge of Obstetrics. Perhaps it will come to a similar one: therefore, oppose it with what is necessary.
Chapter LXXVI.
Chapter on the extraction of the dead fetus.
When you take care of a dead fetus with what I have said in division and it does not come out, and you must use manual operation, then you should consider the following.
If the woman is of healthy virtue and there is no danger to her from any accidents that might cause harm to her: then she should lie down on a bed on her back, with her head lower and her legs raised, and a servant should hold her from both sides or tie her to the bed so that her body is not pulled out during the extraction of the fetus.
Then wet the cervix with olive oil and mucilage of althea, fenugreek, and flaxseed.
Then the obstetrician wets his hand with these oils and mucilages, then he introduces it into the womb with ease. Then he shall seek a place with it where he will fix the hooks on the fetus, and places suitable for that.
Then consider if the fetus is prepared to come down upon its head: then fix hooks in its eyes, or in its neck, or in its mouth, or in its palate, or under its beard, or in its armpits, or in places near the ribs, and below the hypocondria.
If, however, the descent is upon its feet, then in the breastbone, and in its middle ribs.
And it is necessary that he holds the hook with his right hand: and places its sharp edge on that which is between the fingers of his left hand: and introduces it with ease, and fixes the hook in one of those places which we mentioned, until it reaches an empty place.
Then fix another hook, or a third one, if needed: so that the constriction is equal, and it does not deviate to one side.
Then it should be extended with an equal length, and not only in a straight line, but rather moved to all parts, so that its passage is relieved: as is done when a tooth is extracted.
And it is necessary that in what is between [the hooks], the extension should be softened. If a part remains in it, then it is necessary that the midwife binds certain fingers with oil, and introduces them from the side, to turn what remains with them.
If a part of the fetus comes out, then the hooks should be moved to another higher place: do this until the whole fetus comes out.
If a hand or another part comes out first and cannot be returned because of its constriction, then it should be wrapped with a cloth over it. Then extract it entirely until it comes out completely, cut it either at the joint of the foot, or at the elbow: and thus you should do this with one hand and in both feet.
If the head of the fetus is large, or if it encounters a dislocation during delivery, or water has collected around its head: then it is necessary to insert Spatumile (a pointed stick) between the fingers and break the head with it and remove the water; or tear it apart with the instrument called Almisdac, whose shape comes in the same chapter as those of the other instruments.
Similarly, do so if the fetus has a large head by nature, then it is necessary to cut off the amnion (algengematu); or extract it with misdach, as we said. Then draw out the bones with forceps.
If the head emerges and becomes dislocated at the neck: then break it, until all the moisture that is in the chest is released.
If it does not twist, nor submits to delivery: then cut the head piecemeal, as far as possible for you.
If there is an abscess or hydatids (hydropic cysts) below the womb, then you should pierce it until the moisture runs out of it.
If however the fetus is above its feet, then its extraction is easy and its direction to the cervix (matrix) is light.
If it becomes dislocated in the abdomen or chest: then you should extract it with a cloth that you have wrapped around your hand and break open the abdomen or chest until all that is within them runs out.
If the remaining limbs are removed and the head returns: then let the midwife insert her left hand. If the cervix (matrix) is open, then insert your hand deep into the womb and search for the head with it and draw it out with your fingers up to the cervix; then insert a hook or hooks and draw it out with them.
If the bone of the matrix (uterus) is dislocated due to a hot abscess that has occurred to it: then it is not appropriate for it to be laboring on it, instead it is then necessary to administer an infusion of moist substances, oily; and apply poultices; and sit in waters that soften and moisten.
If the fetus is on its side, then it can be turned: then what I said for a living fetus should be administered.
If that cannot be done, it should be cut fragmentarily, and extracted.
And it is necessary that nothing at all from the second layer (membranes) inside should be left behind.
When you have completed your operation, then what I said for hot abscesses that occur in the matrices should be administered.
If bleeding occurs, it should descend into waters of styptic (a substance to stop bleeding), and the remaining cure should be administered.
And indeed I myself have seen a woman, in whose womb a dead fetus was; then she became pregnant again on top of it, afterward another fetus also died. Therefore, after a long time, an abscess occurred in her navel, and it became swollen until it was opened; and it began to discharge pus.
I was therefore called for her treatment, and she was treated for a long time; but the wound did not heal.
Therefore, on it I placed some strong adhesive plasters; and the bone came out from the place. Then several days passed, and another bone came out. I was therefore amazed when there was no bone in the womb.
I therefore thought that since the fetuses were dead bones.
I therefore asked for the wound and extracted many bones while she was in good condition; and she lived thus for a long time, but discharged little pus from the place.
And I did not bind here this foreign matter, except because there is knowledge and help for that which the healing craftsman administers with his hand in cure.
Chapter LXXVII.
On the shapes of necessary instruments for the extraction of a fetus.
The form of the Spindle for opening the Matrix.
Here is the form of a Structure (Clamp), to which books are adjusted, having equally two spindles at the ends of the two pieces of wood. Nevertheless, this Spindle should be more subtle than the Clamp; and to make it so, either it can be made of Ebony, or from Birchwood.
And the thickness of all the wood should be as two fingers: and the edge of each of both is like one finger, and the length of each of them is palm and a half, or less: and in the middle of the two pieces of wood there are two reinforcements made of the same kind of wood, which are now firmly fixed on either side, whose length is half palm or less: and the width of each is as two fingers, or less.
And these two reinforcements are inserted into the bone of the Matrix, so that it opens when you turn the two Spindles.
Another form similar to that one, but more subtle and lighter.
Make it of Ebony wood or Birchwood, in the likeness of forceps (tweezers). Nevertheless, at the end of it there should be two reinforcements, as you can see here above: and the length of each reinforcement is a palm: and the width of each is two fingers.
When you wish to open the Matrix with it, then do this: make the woman sit on the bed, with her legs apart, opening what is between her thighs. Then insert these two reinforcements together into the Matrix: and you hold the end of the instrument below her hips. Then open your hand with the instrument, as you do with tweezers, equally according to the amount you wish for the opening of the Matrix, until the Midwife does what she wants.
Form of Dizziness other than what the ancients called Form of Pushing, by which the fetus is pushed.
The form for breaking a large head (skull): it resembles a pair of forceps with teeth at the end, as you can see.
And sometimes it becomes like a pair of forceps in this form (the one mentioned earlier), as you can see, with teeth similar to those of a saw, on which the skull is cut and crushed.
The form of a scissor with one spike.
The form of a scissor with two spikes.
The form of a spatula with two ends for cutting off the head (skull).
The form of two broad spatulas.
These instruments are used in greater numbers according to their variety, and the more prepared they are by the craftsman, the faster they are for the operation, and higher among men due to their quantity.
Therefore, do not overlook that an instrument is not prepared with you. It is inexcusable to be without them (the instruments).
Chapter LXXVIII.
Chapter on the second extraction (cesarean section).
When the Afterbirth is retained during childbirth, then it is necessary to instruct the woman, to retain her breath. Then make her sneeze and pinch her nose and your hand over her mouth. If she does this, it is good.
If not: then take a pot, and make a hole in the cover of it; and put in them herbs opening the womb, such as balm, rue, anise, camomile, sage, cassia wood, centaury: take all these herbs or some of them, and submerge them with water, and place them over fire.
Then place the plug of reed on the hole of the pot cover, and another end into the womb; and hold it until the vapour reaches the cavity of the womb.
Then make her sneeze as we said before. The afterbirth will come out easily.
If it remains after this treatment and does not come out: then instruct the midwife to dip her hand in sesame oil or althea mucilage. Then insert your hand into the womb and search for the afterbirth with it. When you find it, then take it out slowly.
If it is attached deep within the womb, then insert your hand as described before until you find the afterbirth and draw it out slowly so that it does not fall down the womb due to violent attraction; rather it should be moved with ease from side to side; then more should be added to counterbalance the attraction. It will obey then, and be saved, and come out from the attachment.
If the womb is contracted, as we have already said: treat it with sneezing, and with the potion from the pot with herbs.
If it does not come out as we have described, beware not to tire yourself in the repetition of the extraction.
It is necessary that what comes out to the bone matrix from it (the wound), you tie it to the woman's hip. Then, fumigate her with a four-ingredient ointment. Indeed, it will rot her after days, and it will melt and come out.
However, when it rots, lift it from her abdomen and head, and harm the weak part of that. Therefore, suitable fumigations should be administered for that.
Some of the ancients have already found suitable fumigations from nasturtium and dried figs.
The shape of the instrument with which a woman is fumigated during the retention of Secondina (afterbirth) and menstruation.
Make it similar to an alcohol flask or a jar, and its wide end should be placed over the fire; the fumigation should be placed on prunes; hold her until that fumigation is consumed; then repeat another one.
Chapter LXXIX.
Chapter on the treatment of an unperforated anus.
Many boys are born and their anuses are not perforated, which have already been circumcised by a sharp scythe. The obstetrician must therefore perforate that with her finger; and if not, she should perforate it with a sharp Spatula; and let her avoid touching the muscle.
Then place upon him a cloth soaked in wine and oil. Then take care of him with salve until he is healed.
If she fears that it (the placenta) may stick, then place a lead pipe in the opening, and let it remain there for many days, and remove it when the child wants to come out.
And now occurs obstruction of the anus, also from the hardening of wounds or abscesses. Therefore it must be cut (the obstruction), then treated as we said with the treatment and lead.
Chapter 80.
Chapter on the treatment of fistulas that occur in the lower part.
Fistulas that occur in the lower part are nodes and swellings that occur near the outside of the anus; or in a space of one member; and there is one fistula or several.
When the node is cut open, watery liquid, white or pusulous, flows out from it.
And at times they (the fistulas) penetrate through these. Therefore they are recognized by what comes out when there is diarrhea or bloating in a sick person; and perhaps worms come out from them.
There are fistulas among these when they penetrate through the space, reaching to the bladder or the root of the penis. There are fistulas that penetrate as far as the joining of the hips and as far as the coccygeal node.
From that which is recognized as a fistula penetrating to the anus, even if it does not penetrate, it is to insert your index finger into the anus; and to insert a probe made of metal or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
If there is a twist (tortuosity) in it, then introduce into it a thin probe made of lead, or a hair from horse's mane, until you feel the probe, or a hair on your finger.
If you do not feel it all the way through, nor does anything come out from the opening, nor any wind or worms as I said: then you will know that it is not penetrating; therefore proceed to treatment.
And when the fistula is penetrating into the bladder or into the urinary passage: then its sign is the outflow of urine from it, and its prohibition is this, that the place should be made firm with medicines.
But if it is penetrating to the junction of the hip or to the hip bone: then its sign is that the probe reaches up to there, if it is not twisted up to the bone; and the finding of pain in the surrounding area, and that pus comes out from it always; and that medicine does not help in it, nor does it become firm with an ointment.
And in all such penetrating fistulas there is no cure at all; and the treatment of them is labor and vanity for him upon whom they are formed.
In that which is not penetrating and not ancient, healing is hoped for with a scalpel; according to what I tell you, and I have already proved; and it is, that it lies weak between your hands on its backside; and you loosen the legs of it up to above its hips; and its hips should be inclined towards its belly. Then introduce a probe made of lead or copper if there is a twist in the fistula, until you know where it has reached.
But if the patient feels pain near the anus, then you must insert your little finger into the anus.
If therefore you feel that it has already pierced your finger by itself, detected, except that you feel between your finger and the bone or flesh: then you will know certainly that it is penetrating; do not labor on it, because there is no healing in it, as we have said.
They say that flesh heals in some men, and that the remedy for it which is hoped for is, to heat a cauterium (small rod) with subtle fire according to the width of the fistula (abscess or channel), as was mentioned before, and to insert the heated cauterium into the fistula until it reaches around the anus. Then do this twice or thrice, until you know that all the flesh added to the filter, which is similar to a chicken feather pen, has been burnt off.
Then take care of it with linen wrapped in butter until the burnt flesh comes out; then take care of it with unguents that cause and consolidate the skin.
If it heals, it is good.
And if not, then it will never heal with any other treatment.
If it comes out (the foreign body) and does not reach your finger which is in the anus, and there is a thick covering of skin or flesh between it and the foreign body: and you see that the fistula follows the surface of the skin, then cut the skin from the beginning of the fistula, and you go on cutting with the foreign body as it is in the fistula until the incision reaches the end of the foreign body, and the foreign body is released and falls out.
Then clean the filtering flesh that resembles a chicken feather pen, to ensure there is nothing left of it.
If blood defeats you and causes the flesh to separate between you and your operation, then it is better that you cauterize it with fire or with a sharp medicine.
Because cautery with fire brings good dispositions, burning of those added tissues, and the excision of blood and moisture.
Then treat it with linen wrapped in butter or boiled cabbages until the place emits pus, and the burnt flesh comes out into the pus.
Then treat the wound with consolidating ointments, which make the flesh hard; and there are ointments containing styptic and drying properties.
For when it is restored, then it heals; do not fear repetition.
If the fistula has already reached the depth of the anus and is prolonged beyond the body's superfluity: then insert your finger into the anus, and investigate it.
If you therefore feel a membrane between you and her that is made of sifak or flesh, and it is near to penetration: then there is no operation in this case, except according to the way of trust and hope.
This is because there are three methods for administering it in him: either to cauterize the same, as we said; or to excise it until you reach the concavity of it, so that it is possible for you to insert linen and cure from nearby. And do not proceed too much with the excision, so as not to cut the muscle containing the anus, and there be an unfortunate result of evacuation without will. Then treat it with what I said.
Perhaps it will heal; or else you remove the membrane itself and cleanse it after you cut it near to the anus, as we said, either with the probe, or with another sharp instrument. Then cleanse those tissues filtered which are in the excision, as far as you can with examination.
Then strive for the restoration of the entire wound with a section, and at the superior part where it consolidates; and the fistula remains open on the internal part of the anus, and it will be easier on the sick one.
Sometimes the fistula is drained in this way; it is when you insert a probe into the fistula, which is on the side of the anus near the body surface with skin and margin of the anus; then take a probe pierced at its end, which is like a needle aleskef, that is to say prepared from calfskin, in this shape. Insert into it (the fistula) a thread rolled up from five threads, about the same size. Then insert a probe with a thread into the fistula until it follows its hollow.
If it penetrates the internal margin of the anus nearby, then pull out the thread from that opening; so that you insert your finger into the anus and pull out the end of the thread, and gather both ends together; and tighten each one, and let go after one or two days; and the more the thread cuts into the flesh, tighten it well until the flesh between the two ends of the thread falls off; then care for the wound until it consolidates and heals.
If the opening of the fistula is not penetrating; then make it penetrable in whatever way you can prepare yourself, unless it is too deep. For you do not have the skill to do that without damaging it (the fistula).
Then treat it as I said until it heals.
The shape of the spatulum with a sharp point used for draining a fistula, whose sharpness is very acute, and one part is not acute so as not to damage what is not necessary, as you can see.
Chapter LXXXI.
On the suturing of hemorrhoids, from which blood flows upon their incision; and treatment for fissures.
Hemorrhoids are of two kinds. Or they are within the anus, like bladder stones or cherries; or they resemble the seeds of grapes. And there are small ones and large ones; and blood always flows from them, and it is single, and they are numerous. They are also outside the anus and at its extremities.
However, those that are outside the anus are for the most part few in moistness, from which runs yellow water or a small amount of blood with persistent flow; and they are according to the color of the body.
And its treatment that is within the anus is as follows: you should instruct the patient to purge; and it shall be expressed until it appears in your sight. Therefore, also, grasp them with scissors or hold them with your nail. Then cut them at their roots.
If they cannot be held with scissors due to their moistness and softening, then grasp them with a rough cloth or thick cotton pad, and pull them out with your fingers. Then cut them again, and dust some warm powders over the place of the incision to make it cauterize. Or cauterize them according to what was described in the chapter on cauterizing. Then treat them with the rest of the treatment until they are healed.
If the anus does not obey the expulsion, then administer a suppository to the patient containing a small purgative, so that he may be cleansed with it from the bowels, and quickly obey the expulsion when the patient purges himself.
If the atheres are external from the anus, then their nature is light and easy; it is as if you grasp them with your nail, or grasp them with a pair of forceps, and cut them. Then care for them with what has been said until they heal.
And if one recoils from the incision with iron, then it is necessary to administer a suture for them according to this manner. Take a thread rolled up and insert it into the point (of the wound). Then draw out the atheres towards the top, and make it penetrate with the point into the root on the other side; and roll up the ends of the thread, in the lower part of the point, and let them be wide; and tie the atheres tightly with a strong suture. Then knot the thread, and draw out the point.
Do this with all the atheres, and leave one of them; do not bind (them) to each other so that excess blood flows from it.
Then place a cloth soaked in rose oil or caustic over the anus and put it on the anus; and command the sick person to rest. Then let him go until he falls (to sleep).
When the atheres have fallen, care for them with ointments, and with the rest of the treatment, until they heal.
Chapter on the Care of Fissures. For often they occur due to drying of feces and constriction of nature.
When they become old and medicine does not work on them; then it is necessary to shave with the pointed spatula or with your nail until they become wet, and remove the superior layer of skin which prevents their consolidation. Then care for them until they consolidate as needed.
If they do not consolidate; then shave them more forcefully than before until they bleed a lot, and then care for them until they heal.
On the treatment of the hernia of Almirmar, and not of those not hernias; and on the treatment of Athelil's sores, and of ants.
Chapter LXXXII.
You should know that Almirmar is not anything other than a round knot similar in color to the body; it resembles a nail head, and it can occur throughout the body, especially in the lower parts of the feet or fingers, and this pain occurs during walking.
It is necessary therefore to cut what is around the nail, and hold it with forceps or a curette, and pull it out from its root.
Then care for that: and if you wish to cauterize it according to what was mentioned in its chapter.
Furthermore, there is a small prominence of one kind that is dry and rough, filtered, round on the surface of the body. And it often happens in the hands of children.
And its treatment is to stretch the prominence, and cut it; or sew it with silk thread; or with hair until it falls off. And if you wish, cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine; and now the prominences that grow backwards and not backwards are pulled out with the tool I will mention.
Moreover, a small prominence that is dry and rough, large on the surface of the body, penetrates deeply; and when cold is found, it feels like an ant bite throughout the body; and it mostly occurs in the hands.
And its treatment is to take a needle from the goose feather or strong vulture feather; and place the needle on the ant prominence until it encircles the prominence with the circumference of the needle. Then turn your hand with the needle until it cuts what is around the ant prominence; and place it deeply into the flesh, and pull out the ant prominence from its root.
And if you wish, do that with a brass or iron needle in this shape.
Above the needle there should be a loop of thread extending to its end, so that it is pulled tight on the finger and its rotation.
And if you wish, cauterize the ant prominence according to what was mentioned in the chapter on cauterization of the prominences.
Chapter LXXXIII.
On the shapes of instruments used for enema treatment in illnesses of the anus, and solutions for the abdomen, and for colic.
When an enema is made of silver, or gold, or brass, or iron beaten.
And sometimes it is made with these small and large instruments, according to those for whom it is administered.
Therefore, what is given for the treatment of small children should be small; and those with weak or painful anuses, so also their enemas.
Large enema.
The cannula of this (enema tube), that is the upper part where it is tied, should be wide according to this method; and there should be a distinction so that it can be tied as you see, and the lower end which is inserted into the anus, should be closed, that is not open, soft, very, pulling towards fineness; and on one side of it there should be two holes, and on the other side one hole.
And the size of the hole should be according to the thickness of straws, and somewhat larger but not much, and there should be a bladder in which the medicines are placed, either from an animal's bladder, or from sheepskin, which should be small in shape like that of a syringe: whose root should be one palm.
And it should be perforated with many holes as is customary, and the space between each hole should be the thickness of a finger. Then insert into the holes a thread, perhaps from raw silk, which should be about ten threads or around that, and bind it with it like a syringe. When it is placed in this bladder, the upper part of the enema should be tied at two distinct points with a strong binding. Then administer the enema with it.
And this is the form of a circle as shown here, and of holes.
The quality of making a clyster is as follows: to fill the bladder or the bowel with medicine that has been heated according to the tolerance of the patient; and be careful that it is not excessively hot or excessively cold.
Then the patient lies down on his back and raises his legs towards above; and place underneath him a bedding or linen cloth.
Then anoint the end of the clyster with oil, or with white egg yolk, or with slippery elm gum, or similar substances. Then insert it into the anus gently. Then receive the one who is to administer the clyster with both his hands and squeeze it out forcefully until all that is in the clyster is evacuated into the intestines.
Then remove the clyster and let the patient raise his legs towards the wall.
If the medicine compels him to evacuate, then hold him as much as possible. And if he sleeps all night with it, it is more beneficial for the healing.
If you use the clyster on him with bowel diseases that cause rapid evacuation, then administer several more until he is cured.
If there are hemorrhoids or ulcers in the anus, then make the clyster very subtle and soft, like those used for children's clysters.
And this is the shape of a subtle clyster on which the skin should be tightened.
Chapter 84.
I have already said in the division of wound treatment that it is appropriate for a book, and here I shall say their treatment with hand, and with medicines according to completion.
Therefore, wounds are distinguished according to their nature and the place on which the wound falls.
Thus, the types of wounds are often like a stone's throw: either a cut by a sword or knife; or a strike with a spear, wooden staff, or arrow; and similar to these things made from various objects.
Wounds that occur according to the parts of the body are such as a wound on the head, neck, chest, abdomen, or back; and similar to these from other members.
And I am telling the treatments of certain wounds, so that I may put forth reasoning and rule for the remaining wounds.
And I shall begin with simple head wounds, since the memory of compound wounds will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
Therefore, (I say). If a simple head wound occurs and there is no bone fracture, consider then if it was caused by the throw of a stone or similar objects and only broke the skin; and if the wound is large and you fear the possibility of an abscess of hot matter, then hurry and perform cephalic phlebotomy immediately; do not delay this; and remove it from the blood according to its potency quantity, unless there is something prohibiting phlebotomy, especially if the blood flowing out of the wound is scant. And let the phlebotomy be on the opposite side of the wounded part.
And let the phlebotomy be on the opposite side of the wounded part. Let the weak person take care to avoid being filled, and wine, and heavy foods.
If something prohibits reduction (phlebotomy), then reduce from food, and do not approach meat or wine.
Place warm poultice on ulna if it gets a hot abscess; apply cooked wheat in rose oil alone, or with wine containing styptic agent.
If the ulna has a hot abscess, put warm poultice on it; if it is recent and still has its own blood, and air hasn't changed it yet, then apply the powder I will mention shortly; but if the air has already changed it, then put some unguent on it until it heals.
If the ulna is large or from a sword cut and similar ones, do not join its edges with small stitches; then join it with suture, as I will explain about abdominal wounds in relation to their suturing.
If the ulna has already been exposed by bone and hangs without retention, except for a small suspension; then cut it. Then take care of the ulna with medicines and restore the hard flesh in its place where skin is, and instruct the weak one to eat foods that are thick, such as heads (of animals) and cooked wheat, until it becomes soft; and similar ones.
If you find decay on the skin that does not adhere to the bone; then cut away the decayed part and throw it out; then take care of the remaining part.
If there is an artery or vein from which blood flows in these wounds that cannot be cut by medicine; then look for the artery. If you find it uncut, then cut or tie it with Spatulilus (suture material). If necessity forces and it does not allow what we have said, then cauterize it to stop the blood flow.
If these wounds are small and simple, the matter is easy and light; so apply this powder to them as it consolidates them before air changes them.
Method for treating a ulcerated wound. Recipe one part of olibanum, two parts of dragon's blood, and three parts of unslaked lime: grind all well and sieve it. Fill the wound with this and apply good pressure until it adheres well to it and coagulates with blood.
Then press it with small stones on top and let it be until it does not come off, so that it does not discharge. For the medicine will not be removed from it until it is healed.
And sometimes lime alone does it when there is no olibanum or dragon's blood present for you at the moment; and the same operation is performed with it in many large wounds, when it is necessary to apply it on top of them and press them, and the wounds are recent and have not been altered by air.
If air has already altered the wound in some way, particularly when it is in the summertime, then there is no purpose for this powder: treat the wound with what I have said before, namely apply some digestive unguents on top of it; or apply on top of it poultices made from wheat flour, made with water and honey, until pus is emitted. Then treat the remaining part of the wound with the rest of the cure until they are healed.
If however it happens that the wound is a bone fracture and it is small, then extract it with trephine; and I will now say the treatment for skull fractures in what follows.
On wounds of the neck.
If a wound occurs in the neck, then there is no difference in treatment between it and a simple head wound.
If the nerve or artery of the neck is cut, if it is a nerve: then there is no remedy in it, except to avoid treatment of it, as with ziniar and zegi and similar things which cause violent constriction. Because nerves harm, and they contract them.
And do not place anything cold at all on the wound: because the substance of nerves is cold, and their continuity is with the brain, which is above the organs; and let it be that which is cured from soft medicines, such as lime plaster with sweet water several times infused with oil, or rose oil, and tuthia, when it is also washed even with sweet water: and the remaining mineral stones, according to this method, and moist unguents.
If the wound is large, then administer a stitch: or the rolled lips of it with pulverized chalk. Then heal it, until it heals.
If the wound has depth or occurs in it a cavity in the lower part of it, where already pus collects, then perforate it at a more depressed place within it.
If the artery is already cut in the wound and blood flow follows: then separate it or sever it and tie it; or cauterize it, if necessity demands that.
If the spondyles of the throat are already fractured, or all of them, and the cartilages have been saved: then attach the lips of skin with stitches above the neck of the throat, and do not touch the throat, on the contrary support it, and reduce it to its natural shape. Then tie it up with a suitable suture and let it be for some days. Then treat it with ointments that contain astringents and drying agents until it heals.
If the wound has already made an impression on the bone, then examine it. If there are fragments of bone within it, extract all of them as much as possible: and what cannot be prepared, leave it until the wound rots, separates and is relieved.
If the wound is recent, then sprinkle powder over it as I have told you. If it seems that a bone is visible in the wound and a fistula forms: then treat it with what is mentioned in its chapter.
Chapter on wounds treated with spatulas.
If it is a wound made by a lance or knife and you can see its depth, then examine it. If pus comes out of the wound when the sick person is breathing heavily, then know that the wound is fatal.
If its depth is not severe and it is recent with blood, do not apply powder to it from the beginning, nor tie it up so that blood does not remain in its depth and return to the heart and kill the sick person: instead, put on attracting ointment on it and dissolve it twice a day.
If you do not have the attracting ointment, then place old clay on the wound opening to dry what comes out from it due to moisture: and make the sick person sleep on the wound so that it runs together what collects in it.
If three or more days have passed since the wound occurred and there is no spasm for the sick person, nor a bad heart tremor, nor shortness of breath due to constriction, and you see that its remaining conditions are good: then know that the wound is healthy. Care for yourself and with bandages, and in all other treatment, until you are healed.
If the healing is excised and it opens again, then you will know that it has become a Fistula. Care for it from its own chapter.
And if the wound is from sword or knife cut, and it is simple on the surface of chest or back, then care for it with what was mentioned before in suturing, if it is large; or with powder, if it is small.
But if it has already made an impression on the bone and cut off splinters from it: then examine the wound, and rush to extract those splinters, if they are separated. But if they are not separated, then leave them until the wound rots, because extraction of them makes it stink.
As for other wounds occurring in the remaining limbs, the judgment in treatment is that which we said.
Chapter on wounds of abdomen, and outlet of intestines, and their emergence.
Disruption that occurs in the abdomen is great, middle and small.
From a great disruption, at times the intestine or number of intestines comes out.
Therefore their insertion is done and its suturing is more violent and difficult.
And a small disruption also occurs in another way. Therefore it is more difficult to reduce them if you do not rush to its insertion to its place immediately; because it swells, opens and becomes larger; therefore the entry is difficult.
Therefore a medium-sized disruption is better; because with it the reduction of the intestine is not difficult, as it is with these two types.
Know that stitching of veins is according to four modes.
Two common stitches are used for stitching the abdomen, and for other wounds of the body; and two other stitches belong particularly to other wounds. However, those are more proper for the stitching of the abdomen; and I shall tell you one by one with explanation and clarification.
Therefore, when the wound is small and something comes out from the intestine, and it becomes difficult to reduce it; then that is due to one of the two modes. Or because of the smallness of the rupture, as we said; or because there is distension in the intestine due to cold air.
When that is the case, then one should heat it (the wound), so as to immerse a sponge or wet cloth in warm water alone. Or boil in water cumin, caraway, and spike, and wormwood along with it, until the distension is resolved.
At times it (the solution) makes wine in which there is stipitate; and that is better than water alone in resolving the distension.
When you see the distension already resolved, then moisten the intestine with water in which wormwood or mallow has been boiled. For that opens up the entrance of it (the wound) when the injury is small.
If, however, the return of it (the intestine) is extruded again after this treatment; then stitch up the rupture with a tool used to cut piles (hemorrhoids).
And the first treatment is better when it is prepared, than cutting; and it is not forced to cut after necessity and lack of instruments.
Let one part of it (the stitch) be twisted, sharp, and the other part not sharp; and the end should not be too subtle like a needle, but rather bluntish; and that is similar to a thorn, as you can see.
When the wound is enlarged and enters the intestine, then it is necessary to reduce its shape back to its natural form in its own place, if possible on top of it; because it is better.
When the wound is wide at the lower part of the belly: then it is necessary to make the weak person lie on his back, and place his legs higher than his head. And if it is in the upper part of the belly, then raise his head and chest higher than his lower parts.
Similarly, if the wound is in one of two parts of the belly, then place your intention and attention always in this, that the part where the wound is should be higher than the other part.
Thus, it is necessary to introduce it into large wounds and medium-sized wounds.
In small wounds, place it as you prepare yourself.
Then make sure there is a devout servant present among your hands who holds the wound entirely with his hand; and join the lips. Then cut something from it for the one who follows to sew on something; and this is the common method of sewing one [layer].
And it is that you receive a needle or a number of needles according to the size of the wound. Then cut off from the edge of the wound the amount of a ring finger, that is, of a doctor; and sew one needle through the skin in two places, with the two places of the sifac which are under the skin from the inside, until you make it penetrate from another side, and you have already joined the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the sifac; and they become four layers.
Then sew with double thread around the needle several times from both sides simultaneously, until the two lips of the wound are joined by a good joining.
Then release the thickness of the digit and also fix another point on them; afterwards straighten it with thread, as you did with the first point. Do not cease to do that with the required needle until you complete the constriction of the entire wound.
And let the needle be of medium size between thickness and fineness; since fine needles deeply penetrate the flesh quickly, and coarse ones have difficulty entering the skin; therefore it is necessary that they should be medium in their sharpness and bluntness.
And it is not proper that the needle should be shaped at both ends of the skin close by; so as not to penetrate the flesh quickly and open the wound before its consolidation, and also so that they may not extend when sewed, so as not to prevent the wound from consolidating.
Then cut the point of the needle, so as not to hurt the sick man in his sleep; and place cotton balls on both sides of the needle to hold its ends; and release them until you know that the wound has already consolidated.
And this kind of sewing with needles in such a manner is more suitable for small wounds. Since it suffices to sew them with one needle or two, or about as many.
The second sewing is common, so as to gather together with the sewing the ends of four; that is, the ends of two skins and the two ends of sifac (or one end) in its place, when there is thread on the needle equal in sharpness and bluntness.
Then when you penetrate with the needle these four ends, draw back the needle from the side where you began so that the thread falls out from the upper part of the wound; so that the sewing is like the sewing of cloth where they bind together cloths, and place between every stitch an amount of thickness equal to the smallness of a finger.
Humans know this suture.
With this suture I stitched up the wound that happened to a man in his belly, who had been wounded with a knife, and the wound was larger than one palm: and from the intestines about two palms came out from the middle intestine, and the disruption was in the middle of the stomach.
I returned it (the intestine) after it had remained outside the wound for 24 hours.
The wound was consolidated in a space that was about 15 days: and I cured it, and it healed; and he lived after that for many years, converted to his own habits.
And the physicians judged that it would not heal.
And it was a miracle that I did not cure it with ointment. Because I was in a place where no ointment was found nor anything from the medicines. I therefore put old dough on the wound twice a day, and I attended to its cleansing with water of honey until it healed.
I will speak about two kinds of sutures according to the narrative of the language.
And it begins with sharp suture: and you insert the needle from the outside to the inside part.
When the needle enters the skin and moves along the length and width of the entire body: release the end of the sinew in the side where you inserted the needle, and let it penetrate to the other end from the inside part to the outside at the opposite end.
When you have made it penetrate, then make it penetrate in this way at the same end: and release the end of the sinew that is on this side, and let the needle penetrate to the other end from the inside part to the outside; and make it penetrate with your penetration which you make it penetrate into the tendon end that is in that part until it penetrates through all of it.
Then also begin from the same side, and extract it as well with its extremity, which is from sifac on the other side, and draw out the point that has penetrated through the skin.
Then return it into the same skin, and its extremity, sifac on the other side, with this extremity of mirach: extract it from the skin that is on its part, and do this once and then the other, and do this again after, until you have extracted all of it according to the example.
The conclusion of this stitch is that the stitches of skins should be made so that one end of the sifac is on one side of the skin and the other end released on the other side, until it is completed.
The second type of stitch, which Galen mentioned.
This conversation is about how to do it as some physicians do, gathering all parts that join by nature and applying the end of the sifac to its other end, and the end of mirach to another. And this is done as I have told you.
It is necessary that you push the point into the end of mirach close to you from the outside and let it penetrate to the inside only, and release both ends of sifac. Then turn the point and let it penetrate from the outside to the inside towards both ends of sifac.
Then turn both and let both penetrate from the inside to the outside towards two ends of mirach on the opposite side.
And this method of stitching is better than a common and easy stitch, and it is the stitch whose preceeding has been mentioned before.
Therefore, this is also the speech of Galen.
And they said certain ones. The hernia stitch is to be rectified with two needles. That is, introduce one thread into each of them: and begin with the needle-point from the one which is near to you, and make it pass through to the other side, according to the stitching of those who sew leather equally.
And know that, when a rupture is in the middle of the belly: then the stitching of it is more difficult than of the other parts of the belly.
But the judgment on the dressing of a wound is the judgment on all wounds.
That is, when you seize a fresh wound with its blood, before it changes from the air: and you reduce the bowel and bind it up, and tie it up: then place it on powder of the earth.
If the air has already changed the wound: then place some unguents upon it, which are present with you, until they cause pus: and let the threads fall, and bind them up with sifac, and cover with miret. Then care for it thus as is the care of all wounds, until it heals.
If there are not present with you any medicines, then place immediately upon it as soon as it begins to emit pus, old cloth: and change it twice a day, as I taught you, until it heals.
For you do not need another medicine in many dispositions, when the wounds are simple.
But if you fear that the wound may communicate to the principal members in injury, then it is necessary that you immerse wool softened in oil tempered with warm temperature or in rose oil: and place it on the circumference of the places which are between the groins and under the armpits.
If it feels pain or punctures or rotting in the bowels (for this often happens): then clisterize it with wine of soap, black, warm: especially if putrefaction has already reached the intestine and become a perforating exitus penetrating to the concavity of it.
And know that which is from the large intestine is easier to heal; and that which is from the finer ones, is harder to heal.
The intestine called Jejunum does not accept healing from a wound that happens to it in any way; and this is due to the multitude of its veins, and the size of them, and due to the subtlety of its body, and the proximity of its nature to nerves.
If however that which proceeds from the wound is serous and you are able to seize it fresh: lead it back according to your reduction method, by which you reduce intestines equally.
But if space has passed by it and it is already turned green or black: then it is necessary that you tie it with thread above the place which has become dark from it, to prevent blood flow. For in serous there are veins and arteries.
Then cut what is beyond that ligament, and place two ends of thread hanging from the bottom part of the wound outside it: to relieve your pressure on it, and removal of serous at the site of the wound, and discharge of pus from the wound.
Memory of the wound that occurs in the Intestine.
When there is a rupture in the Intestine and it is small: then it can be restored in certain people; because I have seen one who was wounded in his belly with a thrust of the lance, and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it was an old wound; and it became a Fistula, and it discharged feces, and it became windy.
So I placed the treatment until I was not confident in its healing; nor did I cease to refine it until it healed and the location became solid.
After I saw the place already consolidated, I feared some accident happening to the weak man, that an accident evil would occur in his belly; and it did not happen to him from that accident evil. And he remained in better dispositions of himself, eating and drinking, and copulating, and entered the bath, and was trained in his own regimen.
And some of the experienced ones said that when a wound occurs in the Intestine and it is small, then it should be tied in this manner. It is, to take ants with large heads. Then gather two lips of the wound, and place one ant with an open mouth on the two lips of the wound. When therefore the head is upon it, and closes its mouth, cut off its head, for it will stick to it, and will not be released.
Then place another ant near the first one, and do not stop doing that with the ants according to the size of the wound in its entirety.
Then reduce it (the patient), and suture the wound. For these heads remain attached to the Intestine until it is fed, and it heals, and no harm occurs to the weak man completely.
And now it is possible that the Intestine can be tied even with a fine thread; which was removed from the animal's intestine, attached to it after it is inserted into the point.
It is, to take the end of this thread from the intestine, and scrape off much of it. Then tie a fine linen thread at the end of it (the intestine). Then insert that thread into the point, and suture with it the intestine. Then reduce him to a rupture.
This method of suturing with ants and the intestine, is not except by the way of confidence and hope.
Know that a large, broad ulna (forearm bone) is especially troublesome if it is in one of the slender intestines; then there is no skill except subtlety, and there is no healing of it at all.
On the care of scrotal hernia and fistulae.
You should know that every wound or boil that becomes old and grows, turns into an ulcer and does not consolidate, and always emits pus without being cut off; then it is universally called a fistula in whatever member it may be, and we call it scrotal hernia.
And indeed a fistula is, according to the truth, a filtered knot, hard, white; with which there is no pain, but it has a depression like the feather of a bird; and for this reason some call it "Risat", that is, the feather.
And it is moist in some hours, which emits pus. And perhaps its moistness is cut off in some hours. And sometimes this moistness is much and it is little; and it is thick, and it is fine.
And I have already mentioned in division when I spoke of wounds, that every ulcer which does not heal and flesh is not born in it, is not this but because of one of the nine causes.
One of these is because the blood is scarce in the body; or because it is malicious; or because there is hard flesh between it and its edges preventing the growth of flesh; or because there are many dirt and corruption; or because the ulcer itself is putrid, and the matter that is sent to it is of bad quality; or because the medicine is inappropriate for its healing; or because the falling decay in the region is a kind of pestilence, or by the property of the region, as happens in Caesaraugusta: where the digestion of diseases is difficult, and the healing of boils is delayed by nature; or because there is one bone in it, or the number of bones.
And I have already shown you all those causes and their signs, as well as the treatments of them along with medicines in division: it is necessary here that I make you know the treatment for Fistula and Ulcer, which is made through the way of surgery with the hand.
You know therefore, that a Fistula occurs in all members of the body. For among them are Fistulas that reach the great veins and arteries, or nerves, or organs; or the intestine, or the bladder, or any of the ribs: or the vertebrae of the back, or any of the joints composed together: such as the hand, and the foot: and there are those that approach the proximity of the main member, and similar ones.
Which of these Fistulas is in this manner, is difficult to heal from illnesses and does not receive treatment, and the care with it is labor and ignorance.
If there is any of the Fistulas whose depth does not reach those places that I mentioned and you hope for its treatment, and you wish to come to know it, then take a probe made from brass or iron if the Fistula runs in a straight line, and search it with the same.
If there is a winding in the Fistula, then explore it with a fine lead probe. Because lead with its own body is softened and molded around the winding.
If the Fistula has multiple openings, it will not be possible for you to sign on it with a probe. Cleanse therefore one of its openings from among its openings.
For the moisture with which you cleanse it runs towards other openings and flows out from them.
Then examine and search according to the method that is possible for you, so that you know whether there is a bone or nerve there, and if the Fistula has a long hollow or is near: or it is one Fistula with many openings that covers the whole thing, with all your strength: with your questioning, as you question the sick person, and by feeling pain under pressure with your hand on the spot, and similar signs from its occurrences.
When you have therefore stood over all things in a correct position, then go for treatment according to confidence: and it is that you should consider at that time, whether it is a Fistula nearby appearing, or in a safe place distant from the juncture, or from a nerve, or artery, or vein, or one of the places which I told you: then cut the Fistula according to what has been mentioned in my narrative, and remove what is in it by filtration, and corruptions of flesh, which is born in its opening from flesh, or membrane, and similar things: and take care of it until it heals.
If a Fistula is in deep recesses and is correctly placed: then it is necessary that you cut it as deeply as possible for you. Then cleanse it from all corrupted flesh of its own.
Then administer a linen swab dipped in sharp medications and introduce it as far as the concavity of the Fistula which you have seized with an iron: do this several times, until the sharp medicine corrodes all that remains in the concavity of the Fistula from corruption.
Then restore it with ointments which produce healthy flesh, until it heals.
If it does not heal by this method, then cauterize it according to what we have said.
If the cause of the Fistula is bone, and it has been confirmed to you in this way: then investigate it and cut it according to what I have told you: if it does not forbid you anything from vein, nerve, or main member, as we said.
If a bone is exposed to you and there is something corrupted and blackened in it: then grind it down until the entire corruption is removed. Then take care of the bone with that which causes it to heal until it heals.
If it does not heal and discharges pus as it did: then you know that you have not reached the complete eradication of corruption.
Excise therefore over it again, and search for the reason of its recurrence, and thoroughly cleanse the wound with all your strength.
Then restore it. If it heals, that is good: and if not, then you know that the corruption is in the depth of a distant part of the body, which you did not reach. It is not in that case your ability, but to let it go according to nature.
If the rotten bone is small and accessible to you, pull it out with fine forceps that are suitable for the purpose.
If there are many bones, then you should carefully pull out all of them, without leaving anything behind with your strength.
If however the water prevents you from anything in making an incision, and there is no fear or error, then cut those waters and fleshes, if they are there, and free the bones.
If you are not prepared to remove the bones at your hour, then place something on the wound that will rot it; and let it go until it rots what is around the bones from fleshes and waters.
And keep the wound from healing. And tie the section which you made during your operation. Or place on top of it, if you are afraid, warm pitch softened with oil; or warm pitch immersed in Egyptian ointment, or any green ointments.
For when those waters rot and separate from the bones, their removal is facilitated, and their pulling out.
If there is one large bone, such as the bone of the leg or hip, or similar, and what has rotten from it is a large part, then shave it with the final rasp, until the blackness and corruption are removed. Then restore the wound.
If what is in it [the wound] has become rotten and it is a large part and the rot has already reached the marrow of the bone, then it is necessary to sew it up and cut it completely to the place where the rot has reached: then take care of it until it hardens.
And I tell you about the case that happened to a man in his leg: put it as an example and aid for your operation.
There was a young man of about thirty years old, who had pain in his leg, caused by something moved upon him within the body, that is, from the inside, until it reached the material at the leg, and an abscess formed a large one: and there was no external cause for him.
Therefore, at that time with the mistake of physicians, until the abscess was opened, many substances gathered with it. And the care was put off for him until his leg became fistulous and many openings were made in it: which all discharged pus and body fluids.
Therefore a multitude of physicians cared for him for about two years, and he was not wise in the art of handwork, until I was called, and saw his leg and the materials that were flowing from those openings with a great flow: even the whole body of the man was already stiff, and his color was citrine.
I inserted a probe into one of the openings, and the probe reached the bone.
Then I examined all the openings: and found that they were reaching each other from all parts of the leg.
Therefore I approached, and cut above one of the openings until I exposed a part of the bone: and found it rotten: which was already rotten, decayed, rotten, pierced through, until it had reached the marrow.
Prepare therefore what I have found and prepare it from corrupted bone.
And I have appointed that there should not be in the bone except that corruption which was to be cut off and sawed. And now I will uproot it (the corruption).
Then I placed the wound repair with strengthening medicines at a distance (long space). And it is not solidified.
Then I tried again and found continuity of corruption with the bone: and I sawed what appeared to me also from that corruption.
Then I attempted its repair. And it is not repaired.
I therefore tried again and did not cease cutting the bone into pieces and attempting its repair: and it is not repaired, until I cut about one palm's breadth from the bone and extracted that along with its marrow.
Then I repaired it with medicines and it was quickly solidified and healed: and this iteration was not necessary in its operation or cutting, except for the disposition of debility of the patient, his small tolerance and my fear of him concerning death: because it happened to him at all hours from excessive evacuation of syncopal attacks.
He was therefore healed completely and there grew hard flesh at the place of the bone, and good arrangements were made for his body, and its strength returned: and it turned back to its own dispositions: and no harm came to him from walking at all.
If however the protruding bone at the body's place is already broken, then it should be sawed in this way: and that is: that you take a tendon, tighten it at the end of the protruding bone: and command someone to extend it upwards: and put another thicker ligament from wool first. Then tie [it] over the bone that is skin: and extend its extremity, so that you may draw the flesh towards the lower parts: and you shall expose the flesh on the place which you wish to cut, so that the saw does not cut the flesh.
Place a stick or a board beneath the bone at the bottom properly: because when you do this, it is not forbidden to cut corrupt flesh.
It is necessary that the saw be above the place of corruption a little, so that there is not corruption in the depression of the bone: and it should not appear to the senses in its appearance, and compel another [to be] its substitute for the saw.
If the bone is corrupt and not prominent but continuous with another part, and corruption is in its middle or a part of it, then expose the flesh from all parts entirely. Then place a stick beneath [it].
Afterwards saw it from the first part, where there is corruption, until the saw is continuous with the other part: and let the saw be according to length a little away from the corruption, as we said.
If the corruption is at the junction, cut the corrupted joint and saw the bone where it is continuous with another part.
But if corruption is at the continuation of two joints, then there is no remedy except abrasion.
If corruption is in the beak of the hand or the foot, then the matter is very difficult in that [case]. But it is necessary for you to examine how the corruption appears to you. And abrade it and clean it according to whatever disposition is possible for you, and with whatever remedy it can be corrected for you: when it does not make opposition to the Vein or Nerve [for you].
And know that the saws and knives for cutting these bones are many according to the position of the bones, and their preparation, and their size, and their subtlety, and their magnitude, and their smallness, and their hardness, and their rarity. Therefore, it is necessary to prepare an instrument suitable for every kind of operation.
And know that these operations indicate to you the type of instrument you need, when your study is prolonged. And the knowledge of the methods of this art is a testimony to the methods of diseases: then indeed you will find that which is suitable for each disease among the instruments.
I confirm to you the number of instruments at the end of this chapter, which you place as examples upon which you cut, and the proof by which you test others.
Form of another Saw.
Form of a Scraper for joints. Let the head of this Scraper be in the shape of the head of a star-shaped nail and its points be shaped like the points of an elongated fork.
And it is not suitable unless it is used to scrape the joints when they are broken or a large and thick bone.
Form of a larger Scraper.
Form of a wide Scraper.
Form of a Scraper with a concavity.
Form of another thin Scraper.
Form of another Scraper with a curved end.
Form of a small, fine Scraper.
This resembles a saw and its end is like a saw: it is used in many places for the scraping of bones.
Form of the Razor that suits its purpose, which has been made from bones.
The end of it is triangular and sharp-edged.
Made from India. And similarly, it is necessary that all the things I have said be made of razors, scalpels, and saws.
On the incision of limbs, and the sawing of bones.
Limbs become putrid either from an external cause, or from an internal one.
If you have treated the corruption with medicinal treatment and it does not improve: and if you see that the corruption is advancing into the limb which has not been affected by anything: then it is necessary to make an incision in that limb until the point where corruption reaches, so that the sickness can be expelled through it either from death or from a greater evil caused by the loss of the limb.
And the sign of this is that the limb turns black until it is thought to have been consumed by fire or has become rotten after turning black: until the rot spreads until the point which follows the limb and creeps throughout the entire body.
Therefore, when an incision is made and similarly if the cause of corruption is from the sting of some poisonous creatures such as sea scorpions, weasels, hedgehogs or similar ones.
If corruption or a sting is in the limb of a finger, then incise the finger and do not leave any space for the corruption to advance until it reaches the rest of the hand.
And similarly if this occurs in the hand, then incise it from the root of the palm and do not leave any space for the corruption to advance until it reaches the arm.
And if it penetrates into the arm, then incise the arm at the elbow joint.
If however corruption passes through and you see him about an elbow: then in that case is the death of the weak. And to administer beyond that in treatment, is quantity virtue.
And similarly do with the foot, when corruption invades a toe; then cut it off at one node: and if it enters into the heel of the foot, then cut off the entire foot. If however it rises to the knee, then cut off the leg at the juncture of the knee.
If however corruption has already reached above the knee, then there is no remedy in it except for abandonment and leaving the weak to die.
And the manner of cutting a limb or sewing it is that you tighten the ligament below where you wish to cut, and then tighten another ligament above the place. And stretch one minister ligament downwards; and stretch another minister ligament upwards towards the top. And you separate the flesh that is between two ligaments, with a broad spatula, until the flesh is entirely exposed. Then it is cut or sewn.
And it is necessary that you lay linen cloth over all the parts, so that the knife does not touch a healthy place; and an additional injury is added to the weak, and a warm abscess.
If however there is a flow of blood internally while you work, then burn the place quickly; or lay on it some powders that absorb blood. Then return to your treatment until it is completed.
Then bind the wounded limb with a suitable ligament and care for it until it heals.
And I tell you what happens to a man in his foot; the same thing happens that I am telling you.
That is, because blackening happens in the foot as a result of burning that resembles fire burning; and corruption first occurs in his toe, until it began to involve the entire foot.
The man cured himself, after he saw corruption occur in a limb with great severity, which he discovered from pain and burning: and he cut it off at the joint, and he healed.
And when a long time had passed for him, that same corruption happened to him in the index finger of his hand.
Therefore he came to me, and I attempted to regain that loss with him by placing medicine over his hand after cleansing his body: but the loss was not gained back, and it started to spread to another finger: until corruption began in his hand.
So he called me to cut off his hand: and I did not want that, hoping for recovery of the loss from me: and I also feared death itself for him at the cutting of his hand. Since the man was above his loss.
Therefore when he gave up hope in me, he returned to his own land: and it came to me about him, because he acted quickly, that he cut off his entire hand: and he healed.
And I did not bring this narrative, except to be of help for that which falls under the nature of this illness: and to be a signification, and according to which it should be done.
Chapter on the treatment of sinuses, and the quality of cleansing with medicines.
When a boil occurs in some fleshy parts and the space of the boil extends until it collects pus: then it breaks or perforates, and what is inside the pus exits, and there remains an empty place as if it were a vessel: and the skin that is over it like a cloth that has been softened: and it does not reach its ultimate corruption, nor presses on the bone, nor on the nerve, nor on the ligament: it deserves to be called a sinus: and it is not called a fistula: but if the space of it extends until the corruption presses into one of these parts, then it is called a fistula or a zuken.
The care of it is that you cut the entire skin as it rolls out; and especially when it has been refined and made like cloth; and trust that it will not adhere to the place due to its corruption.
If you expect the skin to adhere, and that is not due to the ultimate corruption; and if there is a thickening of flesh in the skin, then treat it with Clisterium; and it is necessary to consider towards the Anus.
If it is large and there is pus that smells foul from it; then clisterize it with the Egyptian medicine which is vinegar, oil, and zinnia, taking equal parts, mixed together in a vessel; and boil it over fire until the medicine turns red; and let it come to the consistency of honey.
Then take from it what is necessary for you; and dissolve it with water and honey, and clisterize the Anus with it; and tie up its opening, and let the medicine remain there for a quantity of two hours.
Then remove it by pressing; make that day as many times as necessary until the Anus is cleansed, and the foul smell removed.
And sometimes clisterize with water and ash, when this medicine is not present for you; and it is necessary to take ashes from vine wood or ashes from holly trees; and pour water over it. Then boil it, and clisterize with it until you trust that the Anus has been cleansed.
If the sick person cannot tolerate the Egyptian medicine or water and ash, then clisterize it with water and honey to which something of crushed zinnia has already been added. Or clisterize it with honey and wine mixed together, since the property of honey is to cleanse and wash; and wine makes the Anus adhere, especially when there is an excess of stiffness and dryness in the wine.
When you do that several times and trust that the sinus corruption is already removed: then cleanse it with it, along with what causes flesh to grow within it.
And you should take from the plaster dyafinicon: and you will dissolve it with rose oil and stiptic wine; or cleanse it with certain medicines, and other ointments, whose properties I have written about in the treatise on unguents.
If the opening of the sinus is narrow and a cannula cannot enter it to cleanse it: then widen it slightly with iron; or place linen wrapped in Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment within it until it becomes wider.
And similarly, if the opening is also wide, then bring together its lips with stitching; and allow the amount that the cleansing agent can enter without addition.
And similarly, if the opening from which pus flows is raised to a higher place: then cut it in a lower area that is within it, so that the pus may flow out towards the lower part; since pus when constricted at depth prevents flesh from growing within it.
If it is not possible for you to cut the sinus at a place below as desired: then try to prepare a body part so that the pus may flow out from there easily, according to your preparation. Try not to retain anything at all from the pus within it; and take consolidating medicines that are placed on the wound, appropriate for what you desire. Spread them out on a linen cloth. Let the linen cloth be of such size that it will provide communication for the entire sinus. Then cut with scissors directly through the opening of the sinus a hole larger than the sinus opening itself. Then spread a soft ointment over another cloth, according to the size of the opening; and place it on top of it, positioning it far from the orifice of the Sinus, so that the exit of pus from it is relieved; and do not remove the large cloth unless after several days, instead.
The one who is over the orifice of Sinus, that is the one you remove at all times, so that what accumulates in it may come out; and that you know if what runs out from it is much or little; or digested, or undigested.
And when this is done again, consider the place of the Sinus itself, whether its master feels pain in it, or not; and if there is pain in it, whether it is an abscess, or not an abscess.
When therefore your medicine is thus applied and you see the matter that comes out from the orifice of Sinus, then you know if the Sinus already adheres or approaches adhesion; then solve it in the morning or on the third day; and when you dissolve the wound, then change the cloth, and renew the ointment.
If, however, a subtle venom comes out from the Sinus after a long time, then do not despair of its adhesion, for healing of it is approaching; since there are people who have a slow generation of flesh in their wounds, and there are those who act against this.
If, however, undigested pus comes out from the Sinus after several days, then you know that the Sinus does not adhere.
If, therefore, the adhesion of Sinus is delayed and prolonged; then add in the drying treatment of medicaments; but let the physicians do this so that the medicaments are wet in substance, and dry in effect; such as unguentum dyafinicon, when the excess is added to it from zeug.
And from the last one to be treated is this: to receive the ointment of dyafinicon, and it shall be dissolved with rose oil, and it shall be grinded upon it an equal quantity of ancient wine in substance.
Then mix it up together, and use it.
And now makes a similar action when you do not have the ointment of dyafinicon at hand, honey, when you cook it until it thickens, and use it instead. Or receive myrrh, and aloe, and frankincense: grind all of it, and powder it over honey while it is on fire. Then apply linen cloth over it, and bind it with a bladder: and line it with the honey you cooked, until it thickens; and powder the substance over it, and place it again on the linen cloth, and bind it.
