And at the end of it (the lathe) is a hole where the piece of wood is fixed, whose length is a palm with what revolves; and there are similar holes on the two other pieces of wood as well.
Then tie the ligaments which you have tied in the chest of the sick one at the bandage that is at his head; and tie the ligaments which you have tied in his legs at the bandage that is at his feet.
Then let the attendant be at every bandage, who twists his hand with the linen, by which the bandage is twisted; and the physician presses on the spondyle, as we have said.
This is the form of the bandage that follows.
Then after the spondyle returns and the place is pressed, then it is necessary that you put an ointment of dry plaster with egg white. Then apply a poultice (stuppa). Then put above the ointment a star-shaped patch from wood, whose width is three fingers, or about that. And its length should be such as to contain the hollow of the back, and on the healthy part of the spondyle.
Then it is tied with the ligament that I have mentioned. And the sick one shall eat delicate food until he gets better.
If anything remains elevated in the place at the end of healing: then it is necessary that medicines which soften and soothe be administered, with the administration of the tablet that I have mentioned for a long time. And now the lead sheet (lamina plumbi) is administered to him.
And sometimes there remains an elevation at the last spondyle of the back; and it is thought to be a dislocation, and that bone which has now protruded. Therefore, it is not necessary for this medicine to be assumed without caution; for perhaps it will cause death.
Chapter on the cure of a dislocated ankle.
You know that the joints of the ankle and shoulder do not occur except in dislocation; nor does it occur to them what occurs to the other joints due to slight displacement and hollowing.
And indeed, the joint of the Ancle is dislocated in four parts. It is because it is dislocated to the anterior and to the posterior.
Furthermore, it is mostly dislocated internally: it is less dislocated to the anterior and to the posterior.
And the treatment for the internal dislocation is: because when you join the weak leg with a healthy one, it is longer: and its knee is more protruding than that of a healthy person, and the weak cannot double his foot near the groin: and there is a place following the groin which is pressed with a hot poultice, for this reason, because the head of the hip has already reached there.
And the sign of an external dislocation is that its symptoms are opposite to these symptoms (internal dislocation).
And the sign of an anterior dislocation is that it stretches out the healthy leg to a certain extent: but it does not double without pain in the knee: and if he tries to walk, he cannot move forward over it: and his urine is retained, and his groin is pressed, and while walking, his foot is stepped on at the calcaneum.
And the sign of a posterior dislocation is that it does not stretch out the knee nor can it double before doubling the groin: and its leg is even shorter than the other: and his groin is softened, and the head of the hip is at the place (of the wound).
However, the reduction of this dislocation is to consider at that time if the dislocation is old, which has already become chronic with the one who has it. Then, if you administer the reduction and it remains according to its own position: then there is no cure at all (in that case). Therefore, do not presume too deeply upon him (the patient).
In that case where dislocation is recent, and it belongs to one of the four types of dislocations: then hasten to do this, that you press the joint, and extend it towards inside and outside, and move it right and left: perhaps it returns, and does not need other care.
If it does not return by this means, then it is necessary that you prepare a strong helper and he extends the leg from its lower part: either with his hands, or with a rope which is tied above the knee: and another helper extends the hand thus that he introduces his hands under the fingers. Then bind it gently with a rope around the root of the hip and hold the other end of the rope.
And let the extension be either from the front of the groin to the breastbone, or from the back to the spine.
And let the extension of all (the limbs) be one, until the weak one with his body is lifted off the ground and remains hanging.
And this kind of extension is a common type among the four types.
If therefore the dislocation returns as we said, it is good: and if not, then it is necessary in every case to do what I will say about its treatment.
In the reduction of its own kind (of dislocation), when it is towards the inside, it is necessary that the weak one lies on his healthy side. Then put the rope around the root of the hip where it is between the head of the hip and the place that is under the groin. Then extend the rope from the lower part of the groin to the upper part of the body, to the breastbone.
Then let another strong helper take his arms and make a narrow place in the large part of the weak hip and extend it with a strong extension towards the outside. Now, indeed, it returns to its place.
And this is one of the simpler species of cure, by which this member is reduced.
If, however, it is excised above you and does not obey you to enter with this species of cure entirely: then it is necessary that two weak feet be tied together with a strong ligament, soft, on both heels and on both knees: and let the length of each one be four fingers' width apart from its origin: and let the leg be weakly extended by more than twice the length of two fingers.
Then, the weak one is suspended above the head of a post, which is in the house: and let its length from the ground be two forearms.
Then command a strong youth to guard the head of the hip: and suspend another with the weak one: and push another youth, guarding the hip with strength, for it returns to its place quickly with union.
In its reduction, however, when there is a dislocation to the outside, it is necessary that the weak one lie on a platform, as we said in the one with humpback. And bind a ligament over its leg, the weak one's own, and over its chest.
Then, two posts are placed, one at his feet, and another at his head. Then a post is placed in the middle of the platform, fixed well: over which are wrapped wet cloths, so as not to harm the weak one: and let the post be between his hips, so that it is not drawn downwards during extension.
Then, let every servant go to his place, and the doctor equalizes the reduction with his hand.
If it, therefore, obeys for reversal, it will be good.
And if not, place it on the table and press it equally, as we said in humpback. The sick one should lie on his healthy side.
If the dislocation is towards the front, then it is necessary to extend the sick person's leg quickly; and according to this same account on a stool; and let the doctor place the palm of his right hand on the sick person's hip. Then bend him with one hand, and while bending place him extended to below towards the knee part.
If the dislocation is towards the back: then it is not necessary to extend the sick one below; and he should be raised on the ground: instead he should be placed on a hard surface, as it is also necessary if his shoulder is dislocated towards the outside, according to what we said about his lying on two sides: and it is on his face, and the ligaments are extended; according to what we said recently.
It is necessary to administer compression with a board also on the place from which it goes out joining, when reduction is completed according to what is necessary.
And the sign of its reduction is not hidden from you; and it is that you extend two legs of the sick one; and when you see them equal, and the sick one tightens his leg, and opens himself without hesitation; then you know that the limb has returned, according to what is necessary: then join the hips, and place an ointment, and tie with a bandage, that is, a roller; so that the shoulder does not move to any part; and let the sick one remain quiet for three days or four.
Then loosen the ligament, the ointment, and compare the leg with the other; then if you see them equal in position, then you know that the dislocation is already fixed; therefore release the sick one for walking.
If you see something softening: then return, and apply the ointment, and bind it according to your first tightening; and leave it also for three days.
Then dissolve it and make him slow in walking on both sides for a few days until he recovers well.
On Dislocations of the Knee.
The leg gets dislocated in three ways. It gets dislocated to the outside, to the inside, and to below (or behind), namely, to the back.
And it is not dislocated to the front.
And a sign of this dislocation is that you command the patient to apply his leg to his hip. But if it does not adhere to the hip: then you know that the leg is dislocated.
And the restoration of all the modes of this dislocation is that you make the patient sit upright, so that he can now extend his leg if he can over it, and let his back touch his face; and place his foot between your feet.
Then let the patient's leg adhere to your palms, and straighten them out over the leg. Then apply with your palm both sides of the leg forcefully. And another servant extends his foot, until the leg returns to its place.
And a sign of restoration is that the leg adheres with the hip gently, not forcefully.
Then apply plasters to it and let the patient's leg adhere to the hip. Then bind them together with a bandage for three or four days. Then unbind them.
And the patient should not walk for some days until he is healed.
But if the reduction is refused by him, then administer a strong extension with bindings, whose method of application has been previously mentioned in the treatment of the ankle, until it returns.
Section on the treatment of calcaneal dislocation.
The calcaneus is sometimes removed by a small removal, and sometimes dislocated according to its completeness. And the dislocation of it [the calcaneus] occurs either towards the internal parts or towards the external parts.
And the sign of its [calcaneus's] dislocation is that you see the calcaneus swollen, proceeding towards the part to which it is dislocated.
The cure of its [calcaneus's] removal is easy return: and it is to stretch it with ease by hands, and equalize it until it returns.
In the treatment of it [calcaneus] when dislocated according to its completeness, it is necessary that you make the sick man sit upright: and the strong servant should hold him tightly from behind the middle part of his back.
Then hold it [the foot] with your right hand from the upper part of it, and with your left hand from the lower part of its foot, in the place of the ankle.
Then pull the foot towards you with your right hand. Then with your left hand take hold of it from both sides.
Then extend [the foot] with the left, and push the heel of the foot with the right turned towards the calf without effort.
Do this twice, as we have said.
Then push the heel of the foot towards the calf with your third effort, and you pull on the ankle.
If it returns in one or two efforts according to this method, and you see the foot equalized, it is good: and if not, then repeat the operation on him, because it will return by itself.
If the return of it [calcaneus] is prevented by him [the patient], when we have said this, then make the sick man lie on his back on the ground, and fix a peg in the ground firmly, so that he falls between his thighs: and you should already have wrapped him in cloth, so as not to harm the sick man.
Then let the servant take his hip: afterwards let another servant extend the foot, either with his hands, or with a strap that binds over the neck of the foot. Let every servant extend himself against the stretching device set up for him: let a peg be standing between the hips of the sick man to keep him from being drawn downwards towards the stretching device.
Then the physician sets the dislocation with his hands, and another servant holds the sound leg downwards. For a dislocation returns quickly.
When the dislocation has returned and is declared to you as healed, then place ointment and wool, and bind it tightly with bands, and bind the foot with a strap to the sound leg.
And you must be careful or fear the nerves that are above the heel bone at the back, so that the strap is not too tight and injures them.
Then dismiss him for two or three days. If the strap becomes soft, bind it; then loosen it on the third or fourth day; and prevent the sick man from walking for forty days. But if he attempts to walk before that period, there is no security except that the dislocation may burst open again and be spoiled, and not receive treatment afterwards.
If he has a hot abscess, then it is necessary that you administer to him the sedative mentioned earlier in another part of our treatment, and embrocation until it is removed.
Chapter on Dislocations of the Fingers of the Foot, and Treatment.
It is necessary that it be adjusted which has been dislocated with slight extension without difficulty; this indeed is easy rather than difficult.
But if the dislocation is in certain knuckles of the foot, then it is necessary that the sick man sit with his foot on a level place or table; and he stands as if walking.
Then you stand, and place your foot upon that which projects from those joints. Then you press it with your foot with force until it returns and you see that it is now even, and no projection appears at the place.
Then put under the sole of his foot a flat board which can hold the whole foot, having two feet. Then bind it with a bandage fitting well for three days. Then unbind it and let it rest from walking for many days, until bound and secured from any recurrence of the reduction.
[Paragraph] On types of dislocations with wound or fracture.
When something happens to it (i.e., the fracture or dislocation), and you attempt its treatment and restoration, death often occurs repeatedly; therefore, one should not presume to undertake such a cure unless he is wise in long practice, merciful, pious, slow, not bold, nor presumptuous. Moreover, he should use only medicines that calm the pain with warm applications, and he should leave the weak one to divine judgment. Unless you see or hope for healing from destruction with mildness of disease, and where there is something that suggests hope. Therefore, attempt the reduction of it immediately at the beginning, before a hot abscess occurs.
If the limb therefore returns as we wish, then administer a regime that calms the abscess; and care for the wound with whatever is suitable to it from dry ointments.
If the dislocation is accompanied by a fracture and separate sequestra occur in the bone, then attempt to remove them; and do in this what was said for simple diseases at the places where they were found.
And be careful according to your strength and guard yourself from entering into the path of fear; according to what my previous teaching has taught you.
That is better for you with your Creator, and more lasting for your glory, and more healthy for your body among them in your time.
